# 高上玉皇本行经集注皇经集注

**Highest Celestial Emperor’s *Běnxíng Jīng* with Annotated Commentaries**
*Title:* **Highest Celestial Emperor’s *Běnxíng Jīng* with Annotated Commentaries**
*Short Title:* **The *Huáng Jīng* Annotated Commentaries**
*Author:* **Zhōu Xuánzhēn (Chou Hsuan-cheng)**, a Quanzhen Daoist master of the Ming Dynasty.
*Content:* A compilation of commentaries on the *Yùhuáng Jīng* (玉皇經) by scholars from the Song, Jin, Yuan, and Ming dynasties, along with annotations on the *Yùhuáng Xīnyìn Jīng* (玉皇心印經). Ten volumes.
*Source Edition:* **The *Wànlì Continuation of the Daoist Canon*** (萬曆續道藏).

---

**Volume 1: Annotated Commentaries on the *Huáng Jīng***
**Preface to the *Huáng Jīng* Annotated Commentaries**

The Dao is beyond words—all scriptures are the traces of the True Saints’ breath.
Yet since words reveal the Dao, even the sages and worthies do not discard them.
Since the Three Realms were divided, the teachings of names were established,
and though their essence is fundamentally unified, those who err may distort them.
Distortion is not the truth.

Before the myriad kalpas, the Original Beginning sat in radiant illumination.
At that time, the supreme cosmic order gathered,
and the myriad True Ones questioned the Jade Emperor about the causes of his deeds,
whereupon he expounded this scripture.
Thus, it is the most honored of all doctrinal texts,
the first of all sacred writings—no other scripture surpasses it.

Its profound words are hidden and subtle,
not indulging in extravagant ornamentation.
Though paired with the *Dàfàn* (大梵), its meaning is boundless,
and even the saints cannot fully articulate it,
nor can speculation reach its depths.
This scripture encompasses all mysteries as if they were held in the palm.

I, **Zhang Zhòng** (張仲), was devoted to ancient texts during my lifetime,
serving in the Zhou Dynasty.
My lineage revered the Celestial Emperor,
and upon hearing this scripture,
I vowed to preserve it as a lifelong treasure.

The Emperor, comparing my merits and demerits in the mortal world,
recorded me as one who walked the path of loyalty and filial piety,
and thus entrusted me to oversee the transformation of the Nine Heavens,
commanding me to compile this scripture.
Within its depths, I tasted its ineffable mysteries.

Alas, those in the world who study this scripture
fail to grasp the saints’ intent or harmonize with its Daoist essence,
erroneously publishing and transmitting it—sometimes misquoting its words and rhythms—
leading to its division into two titles: *Dòngxuán* (洞玄) and *Gāoshàng* (高上),
each clinging to private interpretations in their transmission.
This greatly contradicts the original intent of the scripture,
even to the point of rigidly adhering to falsehoods.

The reckless and deluded may either disbelieve this scripture,
or claim it borrows from other canonical works,
or ignorantly force interpretations upon it.
All such errors fail to recognize its supreme authority,
yet the consequences of karma—blessing, guilt, and retribution—
cannot be evaded.

I, Zhang Zhòng, could not bear to see this sacred text lost,
nor the vulgar ignorance of the age misapplying its teachings.
Thus, I petitioned the Emperor
to have the Daoist immortals elucidate its meaning and spread it among mortals,
making it the key to exhausting the scriptures’ depths,
and the ladder to humanity’s path.

May those who follow its sacred laws
cross the endless sea of delusion;
may its Daoist elixirs
ease the deepest of afflictions.
Hearing this scripture and awakening to the Dao,
one shall forever abandon false speculation;
encountering its teachings and recognizing the True,
one shall finally escape the cycle of rebirth.

From the Three Thousand Great Thousands,
every realm is the domain of the Great Unity;
from kalpa to kalpa,
every generation becomes a field of joy and benefit.

Seeking the Dao, one must attain it;
no wish shall remain unfulfilled.
The virtues of this scripture
are thus without reproach.

Respectfully composed.
With utmost reverence, **Zhang Zhòng**, the Imperial臣 of the **Nine-Heaven Transformative Texts** (九天開化文昌梓橦帝君), prostrates himself a hundred times.

---
**On the Dao**
Composed by **Lǎorén Yānxiān** (老人臞仙), the aged sage of the Southern Pole.

**On the Dao**
Composed by **Lǎorén Yānxiān** (老人臞仙), the aged sage of the Southern Pole.

---

Yānxiān says: When examining the origins of the Daoist teaching, in the primal chaos when distinctions first emerged, human affairs were yet incomplete. The Celestial Mandate (天命) bestowed upon our Daoist Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor (轩辕黄帝), to inherit the **Nine Sovereigns’** (九皇) dispensation, wield the **Six Dragons** (六龙) to govern Heaven, and establish the Celestial Pole (极) in place of Heaven, thus ordering the **Three Talents** (三才). At that time, the heavens and earth were still indistinct, lacking script, so he used knotted cords (结绳) to administer affairs; lacking dwellings, he lived in nests and caves (巢居以穴处); lacking garments, he bound grass to cover his body (结草以蔽体); lacking vessels, he drank from his cupped hands (汗尊而杯饮). Our Daoist Ancestor, the Yellow Emperor, first devised script, garments, palaces, and vessels, thereby completing human affairs. Today, among the **Nine Schools** (九流) and within the **Three Teachings** (三教), the script used, the garments worn, the dwellings inhabited, and the vessels employed are all originally instituted by the Yellow Emperor. Thus, these all stem from the Daoist teaching of the Yellow Emperor.

Moreover, the **Laozi** (老子) proclaimed: *"To give birth to Heaven, Earth, humans, and all things, there must be that which gives birth. I do not know its name; I forcefully name it the Dao, and forcefully call it Great, hence the Great Dao, and its teaching is Daoism."* Only then did the term *Dao* (道) appear in the world. Therefore, those who speak of *practicing the Dao* or *studying the Dao* are all appropriating the words of the **Laozi**, using *Dao* as their name. Are they not the disciples of the **Laozi**?

Again, when the **Laozi** spoke of *"the Mysterious beyond the Mysterious, the Gate of All Marvels"* (玄之又玄，为众妙门), the two characters *Mysterious* (玄) were also taken as names and applied to scriptures. Thus, these are all uses of the **Laozi’s** words.

Further, the *Zhuangzi* (《庄子》) text states: *"There is the Great Awakening (大觉), and only then does one know the Sage."* The term *Great Awakening* (大觉) was a name established by **Zhuangzi**; the **Emperor Huizong** (徽宗) adopted it and conferred the title *Golden Sage* (金仙) upon it. The scriptures all employ this term—these are all derived from the Daoist texts and the teachings of the Yellow Emperor, **Laozi**, and **Zhuangzi**.

---

**Preface to the Imperial Scripture’s Continuation and Annotation**
The character *Dao* (道) is revered equally by the **Three Teachings** (三教). Yet, reckless and deluded sects falsely label the Dao as the **Two Vehicles** (二乘), which is a profound misunderstanding. The **Jade Emperor** (玉帝) is likewise venerated by the **Three Teachings** (三教). Blind followers sometimes call him the *Lord of Heaven* (天主), claiming he is not sufficiently honored—this fails to grasp the **Jade Emperor’s** true essence and origins.

The Emperor’s virtue is boundless; his merit, unspoiled. His station is most exalted, his name most triumphant, governing all ten thousand worlds, encompassing the **Three Teachings**. He rules over the **Three Thousand Great Thousands** (三千大千), transcending kalpas with ease. The Confucianists call him the *Supreme Lord* (上帝), the Buddhists name him *Flame-Light* (燃灯), and the Daoists honor him as the *Mysterious Master* (玄主). His grandeur surpasses all others.

Beholding this scripture, one recognizes the Emperor’s wondrous deeds, dispelling doubts and perplexities of ages past and present. Alas, those who fail to understand it, who have not yet grasped its meaning, still indulge in false speculation, unable to awaken, and their sins deepen evermore. Do they not realize that human life originates from the Dao, is governed by the Emperor, and finds clarity in the Sage’s instructions?

If one scorns the Emperor, belittles Heaven, defames the scriptures, or fails to comprehend the Great Dao, it is as though one turns away from one’s roots and forgets one’s kin—unaware of the fundamental source of life and creation. Your servant, **Lǚ Wēi** (吕嵓), has long lamented this, and thus composes this preface at the head of the scripture’s annotations as a warning.

---

**Second Preface to the Imperial Scripture’s Continuation and Annotation**
The existence of Daoist scriptures is like the presence of the sun and moon in Heaven, or the statutes of a state. To behold the sun and moon yet turn one’s face to the wall is to avoid folly; to follow the laws of the ancient kings is to commit no errors. Then, to revere the true scriptures is surely the standard for entering the Dao.

Moreover, this scripture was transmitted by **Yuánshǐ** (元始), and the **Jade Emperor** and all the gods proclaimed it. It is the highest grade among the **Three Teachings**, the secret speech of the **Great Sage** (大圣), worthy of reverence in every place and kalpa.

Yet, the Dao that transcends speech is already embodied in this scripture—why need further annotations? Still, the scriptures are written in words, and only those who have already attained the Dao can truly perceive them. For those who have not yet entered the gate, these annotations are indeed a profound aid. Without a raft, how does one cross the river? Alas, to seek the Dao apart from the scriptures is wrong; to cling to the scriptures as the Dao itself is also wrong.

With the heart observing the scripture, and the scripture illuminating the heart,
when heart and spirit merge in harmony—
this celestial treasure of sacred verses
is inherently within my very nature.

**True enlightenment** thus transcends mere textual fixation—
how could there be any duality of affliction?

With reverence, **Chángchūn Fǔhuà Míngyīng Zhēn Jūn** and his disciple **Qióu Chǔjī** prostrate and pay homage.

**Preface to the *Royal Scripture*’s Collected Commentaries (First Four Sequences)**

The Dao is vast, the Jade Emperor’s majesty supreme—
the *Royal Scripture*’s sacred profundity
has long been known to me with awe.

Yet the world is often blind, giving rise to false speculation,
claiming the Dao can be abandoned,
the Celestial can be profaned,
the sacred scriptures can be slighted?
How could this be?

For the Dao exists in the scripture,
and the scripture is the very nature of this body;
the Celestial Emperor exists in Heaven,
and the Heavenly Sovereign resides within this form.

Without this embodied form, nature has no foundation,
and its marvels remain obscured;
without the Heavenly Sovereign, the body lacks a master,
and the form becomes mere emptiness.

Since body and heart cannot be abandoned,
how could the Emperor’s grace go unrepaid,
the scripture’s merit go unacknowledged?

Yet faith in the scripture is not mere textual adherence—
it is the divine realization of the heart.
If truly attained and never forgotten,
then the wondrous fruit will surely manifest.

With reverence, **Léitíng Dàyuán Shuài** and his disciple **Dèng Tiān Jūn** prostrate and pay homage in solemn devotion.

**Three Praises**
**Dèng Tiān Jūn** kneels and declares:

**Praise**
Great is the Supreme Dao, without sectarian bounds—
the True One above all.
The Dao
Soars beyond the Three Teachings,
and this alone is most honored.

**Praise**
Majestic is the Jade Emperor,
unmatched among the Three Teachings.
The Emperor
Over vast sands and calamitous ages,
eternally returns to the Supreme Sovereign.

**Praise**
The Imperial Scripture, a grand canon,
subtle and profound.
The Scripture
Embraces all Three Teachings,
its dharma-rules most exalted.

**Preface to the *Royal Scripture with Annotations: Initial Compilation***

The Sage-King did not speak of gods,
yet revered the Supreme Sovereign;
The Confucian scholar avoided esoteric talk,
yet upheld the study of the heart.

The Supreme Sovereign was indeed what the Confucian
dared not slight—
yet none observed the Dao-scriptures,
grasped the profound intent,
or fused the Three into One.

Was it because they established separate schools?
Or because they lacked time to practice the Way?
Alas, how narrow-minded!

The matter lies not in conforming to names,
but in the true benefit of the Dao.
If the Mystic Scripture is wrong,
how can it speak of the Way?
If it is correct,
why then does it differ from Confucianism,
and why cling so rigidly?

Your servant, Hong Xian, in youth studied Confucian texts,
and once encountered the Mystic Canon—
as if gaining some insight, yet dared not claim it.
Later, ascending to the Dragon’s Peak,
dwelling on the Golden Phoenix Slope,
I had the chance to peruse the Three Teachings’ writings,
and came to know that none surpasses the Dao,
none is deeper than the Mystic.

Among the Three Teachings, none surpasses the *Royal Scripture*,
like beans, grains, cloth, and silk—indispensable.
Its profound meanings are hard to fathom;
the annotations of the immortals must be transmitted.
Thus, I withdrew to the secular world,
devoutly compiling this volume.
Alas, my frail body weakens daily,
and I have not yet seen it published.

Later, I met a recluse from Shandong’s Jinan,
Master Zhou Yunqing,
who lectured on the Mystic Scripture
and compiled the *Dao Canon*,
so I entrusted my words to my friend Tian Zhuozi
to record and pass them on.

Winter of the Ming Dynasty’s Wanli thirteenth year,
former Chief Examiner Fang Yiji of Jiangxi
knocked at my door to request this preface.

**Preface to the *Royal Scripture with Annotations***

The difficulty of speaking of the Dao has long endured.

---

I, **Xuan Zheng**, am but a coarse and lowly scholar of the secular world—how dare I speak of the Dao, or compile the *Mystic Canon* and annotate the *Royal Scripture*?

To carry a mountain on a mosquito’s back is folly; it only reveals my inadequacy.

Yet the Great Dao does not abandon the humble and unrefined, and even the lowly can grasp its teachings.

Though the *Jewel Scripture* is profound, the annotations of the immortals are clear and evident.
When **Master Luo Taishi** entrusted me with this work, not including it in the *Dao Canon* would be to conceal Heaven’s treasure;
including it without proper understanding would be equally perilous.

I fear that my limited insights may misrepresent the Dao’s essence,
fail to harmonize the immortal’s intent with my own,
and force-feed interpretations that leave readers unsettled—
spoiling the Dao’s pure flavor, and thus my own guilt would be all the greater.

Alas, those who expound the Dao are few in this age,
and I, a humble and unlearned man, presume to record my thoughts.
It is fitting that I incur blame without merit.

But my resolve is to uphold the Dao,
and if the esteemed **Dao-adept** **Yingliu** examines my words with compassion,
then continues to elucidate their meaning to propagate this Scripture’s truth,
my labor will not be in vain.

Respectfully written,
**Ming Wanli fifteenth year (1587),** the Dao-adept **Zhou Xuan Zheng of Shandong** pays homage in a hundred bows.

---

**Preface to the *Royal Scripture with Annotations*—Copy for Circulation**

To uphold the Dao and illuminate one’s name,
thus honoring one’s ancestors—
this is the age-old principle of **loyalty as the fulfillment of filial piety**.

I, **Wang Jingcu**, was raised in Confucian scholarship,
though I knew of Heavenly Emperor’s grandeur,
I truly understood that the Dao’s practice lies beyond worldly gain.

After studying the *Dao Canon* under **Master Zhou Yunqing**,
and diligently transcribing texts,
I observed the *Royal Scripture’s Annotations* and realized:
the Three Teachings share a single principle,
and **Nature** and **Dao** are inseparable.

This Scripture points directly to the Mystic Essence—
understanding it reveals the Dao in its entirety.

Thus, I presumptuously wrote this preface to inspire myself,
**Ming Wanli sixteenth year (1588), summer, in the capital**,
the Dao-adept **Wang Jingcu** pays homage.

---
**Examination of the Dao’s Origins**

**Examination of the Dao’s Origins**

The Dao is originally formless and nameless—who could probe its source, whence could it be examined? From the Primordial Beginning, the Great Void bore the Mystic Existence, and the Dao’s hidden splendor emerged, its name thereby established. The One True Principle encompasses the Three, and the Three Teachings stand forth. Being and non-being, beginning and end, are not beyond the Five Phases. Eon follows eon in generation, sage follows sage in transmission—all are the Dao. Even if one transcends the Three Realms and lies beyond the Five Phases, one cannot escape being a practitioner of the Dao. Thus, the Dao’s manifestation and the name of the Daoist school originate here. Therefore, we first trace the source of the Scripture.

**Source of the Scripture**
Scriptures bear the Dao, guiding the world with compassionate passage. All scriptures are the sacred utterances of enlightened sages, containing nothing but supreme truth. Yet this Scripture originates from the Primordial Beginning, its transformation rooted in the Jade Emperor. The Primordial Beginning is the first of the Three Teachings, the Jade Emperor the sovereign of all laws. This Scripture reaches the utmost profundity and subtlety, surpassing the Three Teachings; it is also the king of all scriptures, enduring through endless calamities. Its transmission begins from the beginningless, concealed in the Mystic Heaven, hidden within the Jade Peak. Its characters are not of ordinary kind—each spans a yard in breadth, their light piercing infinitely. The Celestial True Person, in response to the times, inscribed and passed it down to the world. Thus, the Scripture’s proclamation was made.

Therefore, we continue tracing the Dao’s source.

**The Jade Emperor: Supreme Sage, Original Master, and Lineage**
The Master, to guide the world, dispels delusion and extracts beings from suffering, transmitting the Dao and bestowing scriptures, opening the path for future generations. The Great Dao Master unifies the Three Teachings, encompasses all laws, dwelling in the Heaven of Heavens, as the Sage among sages—beginningless and endless, its origin unfathomable, prior to all phenomena. Yet the Dao’s subtlety divides into the True: it manifests in the radiant, pure, and blissful realm of the past eon.

Mortals observe the Yang Dao of Heaven’s brilliance—Yang governs bestowal, its mechanism ever active. The Emperor is thus revered as the **Zhang Emperor**. Misguided followers fail to grasp this truth, falsely claiming that the present **Zhang clan of Xingtai, Hebei (formerly True Definition Prefecture, Row Tang County)**, descends from the Jade Emperor. How could they confuse the **Zhang clan of Row Tang**, descendants of **Zhang Guo** and heirs of the **Zhang Immortal**, with such a claim?

This is merely an examination of lineage and clan.

If one speaks of lineage, the Jade Emperor is the primordial emanation of the Great Dao, the ancient ancestor of the cosmic cataclysm—how could he be bound by birth, death, or name? The Emperor’s sacred consort, sacred children, and attendants are all manifestations of the Light-Strong Prince’s celestial retinue in past eons. When the Emperor ascends, his retinue attains the Way entirely. In truth, the Emperor and his retinue are not of mortal female form—they are the purest essence of Heaven. To guide all beings, they manifest in female form, as the scriptures have already stated. Even the Buddha attained enlightenment with his wife and children achieving sainthood.

To call the Jade Emperor the **Dao Ancestor**, across countless eons, all beings and classes are the generative intent of Heaven and Earth, branches of the Dao’s vital pulse. Who among them is not part of the Jade Emperor’s retinue and lineage? When the retinue of the Great Luo Palace attains the Way, they become celestial and saintly bodies. As with Manjusri presiding over the Immaculate World, or the Dragon Princess attaining the Way and transforming into male form—this is the same principle.

Yet today’s monks, Daoists, and common folk fail to grasp this truth, falsely believing the Jade Emperor has a retinue, undergoes rebirth, and is bound to the Two Vehicle fruits. How could they know that the celestial realms are countless, while the Three Pure Ones’ realm and the Great Luo Heaven are boundless? The celestial emperors undergo rebirth, but the Jade Emperor does not. For the Jade Emperor is the Dao Body—Dao is endless, how could the Jade Emperor be finite?

Truly, the Jade Emperor is the supreme teacher of all Buddhas of the One Vehicle, the sovereign of all heavens, and his retinue is the marvel of Dao transformation. Such is the essence of the mystical lineage.

Scholars must not speak recklessly—examine this carefully.

**On the Merit of Engraving Scriptures:**
In ancient times, there were no paper or brushes; records were inscribed on bamboo and wood. When **Mong Tian** and **Cai Lun** invented paper and ink, the merit of preserving scriptures doubled. Later, high sages carved wooden blocks for printing, multiplying the merit yet again.

Yet ignorant followers of false sects do not know that Mong Tian and Cai Lun received blessings from the **Tusita Heaven**, and that these two were later punished in the underworld for their sins. Their journey through the netherworld was guided by the **Great Sage of the Great Elixir Heaven** and **Kshitigarbha Bodhisattva**, who entered the underworld with scriptures to transform and liberate those guilty of heresy. How could these two suffer in hell? Their merit was vast—they were of the highest rank in engraving and propagating the teachings.

**On the Merit of Reciting, Chanting, and Teaching Scriptures:**
Recitation and exposition must be done with utmost sincerity, free from attachment, greed, or delusion. The merit will then match the scriptures’ words. Printing and distributing scriptures bring even greater merit, as they spread the Dharma widely. To treat scriptures lightly, defame them, or damage them is a grave offense. Be warned—do not betray the teachings of the sages.

**On the Similarities and Differences of the Jade Emperor’s Sacred Titles:**
The Jade Emperor’s sacred titles date from before the cosmic cataclysm, were further honored in the Middle Ages, and are now praised anew. Rulers who cherish the Dao, moved by the **Mysterious Grace**, honor them according to their own revelations and devotions. As circumstances align and deeds are accomplished, their fame spreads, and all revere the divine titles, establishing their names.

The Jade Emperor has four forms:
1. The **Taiwei Jade Emperor**, named after the star **Taiwei** in the **Taiwei Enclosure** during the Han dynasty under Emperor Wu;
2. The **Brahman Heaven Jade Emperor**, named after the **Celestial Market Enclosure** during Emperor Xuan’s reign;
3. The **Flame Flower Shao Wei Jade Emperor**, named after the **Primordial Fixed Position** during Emperor Ai’s reign;
4. The **Zixu Jade Emperor**, named after the **Post-Heaven Stem** during Emperor Guangwu’s reign.

None of these are the true Jade Emperor. The true Jade Emperor bears the title:
**Emperor of the Golden Gate of the Highest Sovereign of the Natural and Mysterious Perfection, the Primal and Perfect, the Jade Sovereign Emperor, also called the Highest Supreme Jade Emperor of the Mysterious Vault.**

This Emperor governs all heavens, never decaying or perishing. The world does not fully understand, mistakenly equating him with **Shakra (Indra)**. Yet the Jade Emperor’s titles are distinct. The four Jade Emperors all fall under the governance of the **Highest Supreme Jade Emperor**. Those who speak of the Four Emperors and the Heavenly Sovereign as equals are also mistaken. Those who understand the heavens will clarify this.

**On the Jade Emperor’s Sovereignty Over the Extremes:**
**Ge Xianhui** said: The heavens of the world, as perceived, are the same. Confucianism speaks of **One Heaven and Earth, One Emperor**. Daoism speaks of **thirty billion worlds**, each with thirty-six heavens, each heaven ruled by an emperor, all under the governance of the **Highest Supreme Jade Emperor**. Buddhism speaks of **three thousand great thousand-world systems**, each with thirty-two heavens, each ruled by a Jade Emperor.

Though the three teachings seem divergent, those who speak of **One Heaven** refer to the **Great Void** beyond, calling it unfathomable, and speak of **thirty billion worlds**—beyond which lies the **Inconceivable**. Those who speak of **three thousand great thousand-world systems** say that beyond them lies the **Limitless**. Thus, Confucianism follows the **Imperial Norm**, saying, *"The sage approximates Heaven."* Heaven’s body is boundless, and this principle holds true at the **Great Convergence of the Cosmic Cycle**.

Daoism speaks of the **Highest Supreme Void**, the True Emperor who never decays; Buddhism speaks of **Suchness**, self-liberated and never regressing. Both affirm that the Jade Emperor never perishes. Thus, speaking of **One Heaven** is not an omission—it is a general name encompassing all, harmonizing with Dao and Buddhism. Speaking of **thirty billion worlds** or **three thousand great thousand-world systems** is not false—it is a division by number, aligning with Confucianism.

As for Buddhism’s claim that each world has its own Jade Emperor, each realm has its own **Ultimate**, Daoism asserts that all worlds share **this Jade Emperor**, all realms share **the One Beyond Extremes**. The **Great Void**, the **Inconceivable**, the **Limitless**—all speak of the unchanging Dao, the Jade Emperor ever-present. If one divides worlds and claims the Jade Emperor differs, how could the **Beyond Extremes** have duality? If one says the Emperor changes with cosmic cycles, how could the **Beyond Extremes** decay?

Since the Dao does not decay, the Jade Emperor is eternal. Truly, do not cling to demonic doctrines to defame the sages.

**On the Jade Emperor’s Realm of Qingwei Heaven:**
**Wang Chongyang** said: **Qingwei** is the highest and most mysterious realm of Heaven, the Daoist **Seed-Citizen Heaven**, the Confucian **Boundless Beyond**, the **Enduring Azure**—and in Buddhism, the **Non-Regressing Realm**.

「Now within the chaotic scriptures of Chan Buddhism, there is a mistaken claim that the Jade Emperor resides atop **Mount Sumeru (Must Prāṇidhāna)**, which is actually the realm of the **Four Heavenly Kings of the Day and Moon (Sūryaprabhāraja, Candraprabhāraja, and the four Dikpāla)**—a place where destruction may occur, save for the **Inner Court of Maitreya (Maitreya’s Inner Sanctuary)** as the **Non-Regressing Realm**.

They also speak of **Mileo Enclosure (Mīlùo Yuán)**, **Mileo Garden (Mīlùo Yuán)**, or **Mileo’s Pure True Realm (Mīlùo Xuánzhēn Jìng)**—these three names refer to the **Supreme Primordial Lord (Wúshàng Yuánjūn)** of Daoist scriptures, who manifests as the Jade Emperor in the **Non-Regressing Realm of Mileo’s Pure True Realm (Mīlùo Xuánzhēn Jìng)**. The **Four Heavenly Kings of the Day and Moon**, however, are the abode of the **Lesser Heavenly Emperor (Tàiwēi Yùdì)**, not the **Great Heavenly Emperor (Dàtiānzūn)**, the exalted Jade Emperor. Hence, Daoist scriptures say:

*"At the peak of **Mount Xuangu (Xuángǔ Shān)**, there is an **Imperial Sovereign (Dìjūn)**. One must pay homage to the **Jade Sovereign, Great Heavenly Emperor (Yùhuáng Dàtiānzūn)**."*

**Mount Xuangu (Xuángǔ Shān)** is the Chan Buddhist **Mount Sumeru (Must Prāṇidhāna)**, the master of the **Day and Moon Heavenly Realm (Rìyuè Tiān)**, and the deity governing this realm—akin to the **Prefect of the Imperial Capital (Jīngzào Yìn)** of ancient times. Thus, when the **Buddha (Rúshì)** preaches the **Dharma (Fǎ)**, and the Emperor of the **Heavenly Realm (Tiānshì)** spreads his canopy—this is the **state examination (Zhuàngyuán Jìdì)** where a scholar attains highest honors. The **Golden Hall (Jīndiàn)** transmits the successful candidates, the **Ministry of Rites (Lǐbù)** raises the cups, and the **Prefect of the Imperial Capital (Jīngzào Yìn)** spreads the canopy to honor the **court’s recognition of virtue (cháotiān zhēngxián zhī yì)**. The heretical sects thus falsely equate the **canopy-spreading Emperor of the Heavenly Realm (Zhānggài Jīngzào Yìn)** with the **Great Heavenly Emperor (Dàtiānzūn)**, declaring the **Prefect of the Imperial Capital (Zhānggài Jīngzào Yìn)** as the **Emperor (Huángdì)**. How erroneous this is! Such falsehoods are most perverse.

As for the claim that **Mount Kunlun (Kūnlún Shān)** has eight abodes: the **Eight Directions** may indeed encompass eight extremes, but all eight extremes converge in the **western-northern direction (xīběi)**, where **Mount Kunlun (Kūnlún Shān)** stands as the **Pillar of Heaven and Cornerstone of Earth (Tiānzhù Dìwéi)**—the Daoist **Mount Xuangu (Xuángǔ Shān)** and the Buddhist **Mount Sumeru (Must Prāṇidhāna)**. How could there be eight of them? The common folk have long been misled by such falsehoods, so now, in examining the **Non-Regressing Realm of Qingwei Heaven (Qīngwēi Tiān)**, I clarify and warn against mistaken theories.

**On the Jade Emperor’s Rank and Status (Yùdì Zūncì Kǎo):**
**Liu Haichan (Liú Hǎichán)** said: The Jade Emperor, in Daoism, is the **manifestation of the Three Pure Ones (Sānqīng)**. Daoists first speak of the **Three Pure Ones (Sānqīng)**, then the **Void (Xūwú)** and the **Mysterious Existence (Miàohǔ)**, which are the **Non-Extreme (Wújí)** and **Great Ultimate (Tàijí)**—not implying any hierarchy of superiority or inferiority. In Buddhism, he is the **Ancient Lamp Buddha (Rán Dēng Gǔfó)**, who reveals himself in the **body of Śākyamuni Buddha (Shìjiā Fóshēn)**. Chan Buddhists, however, place the Jade Emperor before the Buddha, following the foreign custom of honoring their **ruler (Zhǔ)** before the **Chinese Emperor (Huángdì)**.

If we examine the Daoist reverence, the *Golden Wheel Sutra (Jīn Lún Jīng)* states:
*"The Jade Emperor mounts the **Mysterious Command Chariot (Yùdòu Xuánmìng Jià)**, his spirit traverses the **Supreme Extremity (Shàngjí)**, with the **Five Stars (Wǔxīng)** as his messengers before him, and the **Buddhas and Devas (Shìfàn)** as his **威仪 (auspicious retinue)** behind him."*

The **Buddhas and Devas (Shìfàn)** are **immortals, Buddhas, and Bodhisattvas (Xiānfó Púsà)**. The Jade Emperor’s trust in the **Three Pure Ones (Sānqīng)** and the **Buddhas (Fó)** demonstrates his **body (shēn)** and **degree (dù)** to guide all sentient beings, leading them to **return to the Dao (guīdào)**. The common folk, however, arbitrarily divide the **ranks of the divine (shèngwèi)**, failing to investigate the **source and flow (yuánliú)**, and consider the Jade Emperor as a **secondary deity (cìzūn)**—thus implying there are beings greater than the Emperor. Even more absurd, they compare the **Three Pure Ones (Sānqīng)** and the **Buddhas (Fó)** to the **Supreme Emperor (Tàishàng Huáng)**, contradicting the **progressive manifestation (xiān-hòu xiǎnhuà)** of the Jade Emperor. Further, they falsely equate the **divine with different surnames and titles (yìxìng yìhào)** to father and son, their offense being even more grave.

Alas! The world cannot do without the Jade Emperor, just as a life must have its **ancestral lineage (zōngzǔ)** and **parents (fùmǔ)**. To defame the Emperor and establish separate sects is to **abandon one’s ancestral lineage and parents while elevating oneself (shě zōngzǔ fùmǔ ér zì zūn)**. How can this be justified?

**On the Jade Emperor’s Auspicious Title (Yùdì Hào Chēng Lìyì Kǎo):**
**Lan Caihe (Lán Cǎihé)** said: People know to honor the **Emperor of Heaven (Tiānshì)**, yet they do not recognize the **Jade Emperor’s sacred title (Yùdì Bǎohào)**. Confucians may say reciting it is improper, but do they not know that **great filial piety is to revere one’s parents throughout life (Mò fùmǔ ér xīnchéng)**—is this not the teaching of **Mencius (Mèngzǐ)**?

To **revere one’s parents with sincerity (mò fùmǔ ér xīnchéng)** makes one a **filial son (xiào zǐ)**. To **invoke the Jade Emperor’s title with sincerity (chēng Dìhào ér xīnchéng)** ensures one will never commit transgressions, making them a **true child of Heaven and Earth (Qiánkūn xiāozǐ)**. To **embody the form and emulate the Dao (jiànxíng wéi xiāo)** is to **submit to Heaven and Earth (tiān dì jiēguī)**, and what greater benefit could there be?

**On the Auspicious Benefits of the *Imperial Scripture (Huáng Jīng)* (Huáng Jīng Lìyì Kǎo):**
**Zhang Ziyang (Zhāng Zǐyáng)** said: With the rise of **imperial rulers (Dìwáng)**, there must be **imperial institutions (Dìwáng zhì)**. Those who transgress these institutions are rare indeed. Yet, the **Heart Seal of the *Imperial Scripture (Huáng Jīng Xīnyìn)**** is the **essence of Daoist practice (Dàodào Zhīyào)**, embodying it makes one the **Supreme Sage (Zhìshèng)**, far beyond merely avoiding transgressions. If people today do not believe in its benefits, it is because they have not **sincerely practiced its recitation and essence (tǐhuì shìchí wèichéng)**. The wise should ponder this.

**On the *Imperial Scripture’s* Record of Merit and Demerit (Dì Jīng Jiàolù Gōngguò Kǎo):**
**Zhong Lizi (Zhōng Lìzǐ)** said: The **birth of all beings (Rénwù zhī shēng)** originates from the Dao, all receiving **true essence (Zhēn)** from the **Heavenly Emperor (Tiāndì)**. Thus, if one is **virtuous (shàn)**, their **virtue moves Heaven (Dé dòng Tiān)**, and blessings naturally arrive, even if they are poor and lowly, their **tranquility and joy surpass others (ānlè shèng yú tārén)**, making them the **True Hall of Blessings (Zhēn Fú Táng)**. If one is **wicked (è)**, they **create their own calamity (zì zuò niè)**, and Heaven sends **disasters (Tiān xiàng yāng)**—even if they are rich and noble, their **misfortune and retribution (xiōng jiù)** make them an **active hell (Huódì Yù)**.

**Destiny of blessings and calamities (Huòfú)** is fixed, following the **virtue or wickedness of mortals (rén shàn è)**; the **interaction between humans and Heaven (Tiān rén jiāoyìng)** is swift as **echoes and responses (yǐngxiǎng)**. The deluded do not believe this, so they speak of **merit (Gōnggé)** as follows: **"Sincerely reciting the *Imperial Scripture (Huáng Jīng)*** in its entirety earns **a thousand kinds of merit (qiān zhǒng gōngdé)**, leading one to ascend to **Heaven’s Hall (Shèng Tiān Táng)**."**

**"Sincerely reciting (Zhēn shìchí)"** means **unifying inner and outer (nèiwài zǒngyī)**, **words and deeds aligning with the Dao (yánxíng hé dào)**, not merely **uttering scriptures with one’s mouth (wéi kǒu shàng niàn jīng)** but **practicing true goodness in one’s heart (wéi xīnxīn shíshàn)**. Truly well said!

**Wang Lingguan (Wáng Língguān)** said: *"Why should the skilled hand draw my likeness? Only wish your heart align with mine."* If one’s heart can **align with the Heavenly Emperor’s (Xīnxīn hé Tiāndì)**, then **virtue and blessings flourish together (Dé fú bìng miào)**, achieving **true recitation and meritorious deeds (Zhēn shìchí shàn gōng)**. As for the rest who merely **recite scriptures and restrain their mouths while disciplining their hearts (Jǐ kǒu zhì xīn)**, though they may have **faith and merit (fúdé)**, their blessings depend on the **size of their virtue (shàn zhī dàxiǎo)**—this is yet another inferior level.

**On the Demerits (Guògé):**
They say: *"If one does not believe in this scripture, they fall into **heterodox paths (xiédào)***, for their **heart does not align with the Dao (xīn bù hé dào)**, thus becoming a **wicked person (yé rén)**."* They also say: *"To **defame true scriptures (huǐ chán zhēn wén)** is to **fall into hell (shēn duò Dìyù)**."* Those who do not believe merely **hear of the scripture’s merits (jīngzhōng gōngdé)**, yet fail to **truly embrace them (xīn shì bù jí)**, are guilty of lesser transgressions. But to **defame the scriptures is to erase Heaven’s decrees (fèi Tiān zhāng)***—their **heart commits great evil (xīn zuò dàxiè)**, their **misfortune and retribution (xiōng jiù)** are boundless, sinking them into **dark and malevolent realms (yīn è zhī dì)**, their crimes unforgivable, thus they fall into **the path of hell (Duò Dìyù Lù)**.*

They further say: *"To **slander the Emperor and defame the Sages (Dìshì huǐshèng)**, **abolish the divine abode (fèi shén zhù)**, **tear apart true scriptures (liè zhēn jīng)**, and **persist in wickedness without remorse (wán è wú quān)**, will forever suffer **karmic restraints (yè jìn)**, and their **calamity extends to seven generations (huò jí qī zǔ)**."* To **defame and tear apart scriptures (huǐliè jīngwén)** is to **blaspheme the sacred texts (kǒu shàn língzhāng)**, their **words dare Heaven’s authority (yán mà Tiān wēi)**, so their **crime rests upon themselves (zuì zài zìjǐ)**. To **slander the Emperor and tear apart scriptures (Dìshì liè jīng)**, to **indulge in evil without repentance (zòng è bù quān)**, makes one’s **body unvirtuous (shēn wéi bùshàn)**, leaving **endless infamy (yí chǒu wúqióng)**, harming one’s **substance (tǐ)** and **dishonoring one’s kin (rú jīn)**. Even if one were a **filial son or a kind grandson (xiào zǐ cí sūn)**, they could not **redeem this across a hundred generations (bǎi shì bù néng gǎi)**."*

「The **karmic faults (guì yè)** of one’s own person—when will they ever cease? The **calamity upon one’s ancestors (zǔ qīn zhī jiù)**—how could they ever be pardoned? If not, then the state establishes laws, and punishing criminals is acceptable. Yet why are there those who **exterminate the three lineages (yí sān zú)** or **destroy the nine lineages (miè jiǔ zú)**? It is because the **crime exceeds the measure (zuì fàn guò zhòng)**, thus extending to one’s relatives. But if this is so, then though the **legal net (fǎ wǎng)** may stretch far, others may still **hold erroneous views of scriptures (yǐ chǒu jīngdiǎn)**, or **recite them without reverence (sòng zhì bù qián)**, or **misinterpret and belittle them (chí niàn éu màn)**, or **arbitrarily alter their teachings (màng yì cái dù)**, or **condemn one while praising another (shì cǐ fěi bǐ)**, or **prefer the latter while disparaging the former (yōu bǐ liè cǐ)**. According to their **transgressions’ severity (guò zhī dà xiǎo)**, there is a **fixed retribution (yīdìng zhī bào)** awaiting them.

*Alas!* The **Imperial Sutra (Dìshì jīng)** is the **law of the present age (jīn fǎ)**. To **disbelieve the sovereign’s law (bù xìn Wáng fǎ)**, the **statutes have clear decrees (lǜ yǒu míng zhāng)**; to **not follow the sacred precedents (bù zūn shèngdiǎn)**, how could **Heaven’s ordinances (Tiān tiáo)** not exist? Lamenting that **the human body is hard to obtain (rén shēn nán dé)**, and the **supreme Dao is difficult to hear (shàng dào nán wén)**, parents labor to give birth to us—**their toil and suffering are the same (láo kǔ tóng)**. Those with **virtue (dé)** bring **blessings to their ancestors (fú zǔ qīn)**, ascending in this very life to the **highest ranks (dēng jiǎ kē)**, and receiving **honors that exalt their kin (fēng zèng xiǎn qīn)**. Those with **faults (guò)** bring **calamity to their ancestors (huò zǔ qīn)**, just as today’s **offspring and descendants (zǐ dì fàn shì)** may be punished for crimes, **and the penalty falls upon the family elders (zuì zuò jiā zhǎng)**. Though **human bodies are equal (rén shēn tóng)**, **good and evil differ (shàn è yì)**; though **parental kindness is the same (qīn ēn tóng)**, **blessings and karmic consequences vary (fú yè shū)**. Why then does a person **not choose goodness but delight in evil (wú shàn zuò è)**, **merely burdening their ancestral lineage (tú yí lèi zǔ zōng)**?

The **Imperial Sutra’s (Huáng jīng)** teachings on **merit and demerit (gōng guò gé yán)** demonstrate its **truth within the human heart (zhēn jīng zài rén xīn shàng)**. **Pure goodness (chún shàn)** naturally fulfills the **sutra’s merit (jīng gōng)**. The **highest sages (shàng zhì)** act in **harmony with the sutra’s essence (zì hé jīng)**, not relying on mere **verbal recitation (kǒu sòng)**. The **middle sages (zhōng zhì)** **discern the Dao through the sutra (yīn jīng jiàn dào)**, while the **lowly and ignorant (xià yú)** **do not believe even when told (yǔ yán wú xìn)**. Since **highest sages are rare (shàng zhì bù cháng yǒu)**, and **lowly and ignorant few (xià yú yì bù duō)**, the **common folk (zhōng rén)** are vast—**thus the efficacy of teaching and cultivation (jiào huà zhī gōng)** cannot be neglected.

Those who **contemplate this sutra (guān zhì jīng)**—how could they **fail to embody the Jade Emperor’s (Yù Dìshì)** **compassionate guidance of the world (cí bēi dù shì zhī yì)**, and instead **regard it as ordinary (shì wéi fàn cháng)**?

Regarding the **annotations and interpretations of the Imperial Sutra (Huáng jīng jí zhù yì lüè kǎo)**:
Zhōu Xiànlín states:
*The **Imperial Sutra (Huáng jīng)** speaks of the **true nature of the Dao (dào zhī zhēn)**—what is inherently **divided by one’s innate nature (wú xìng fēn gù yǒu)**. It should **not require elucidation (yí bù xū jiě)**. Most people are **overly concerned (duō lǜ)**, with **varying capacities (zī yǒu gāo xià)**. Those with **partial insights (piān jiàn zhě)** are many, and the **immortals (zhū xiān)** interpret it thus—**not all can fully expound the profound meaning (fēi néng jìn shuō xuán zhǐ)**. This is merely **prepared for later generations’ reconciliation (gū bèi hòu rén zhī zhé zhōng ěr)**.*

Regarding the **differences in the Imperial Sutra (Huáng jīng tóng yì kǎo)**:
Zhāng Zǐfáng states:
*This sutra originally had **no dual names (bēn wú èr míng)** or **distinction between Highest Sage and Supreme Spirit Jewel (gāo shàng líng bǎo zhī fēn)**. Later scholars **erroneously annotated (cūn rén chuān jiàn)**, **arbitrarily adding or subtracting words (suí yì zēng jiǎn zì jù)**, **forcibly linking texts (qiān hé wén)**, and **utterly lost the original intent (shū shī běn zhǐ)**. Now, upon **examining the Highest Sage and Supreme Spirit Jewel (gāo shàng líng bǎo)****,** they stem from **various immortals’ praise (gè xiān zhēn chēng yáng yǔ)**. Later generations mistakenly **took them as two separate texts (wù zhí wéi èr)**. Here, we **adhere to the Mystic Capital’s (Xuándū)** **definitive analysis (dìng lùn)** and **record the transmitted versions (lù chuán shì jiān)**. Later students **should examine this carefully (jiàn zhì mò tǐ)** and, upon encountering **errors in transcription, transmission, or exposition (yù yú kān xiě chuán jiǎo chā chù)**, **cross-reference with authoritative editions (cóng gōng kǎo jiào)**. Any **external additions of words, phrases, or illustrations (wài tiān wén jù zì huà)** are all **erroneous (é wù)**. **Enlightened ones should not rigidly cling to these (dá zhě wù ní zhí yán)**.*

Regarding the **annotations, interpretations, and transmitted commentaries of the Imperial Sutra (Huáng jīng jí zhù kān chuán shū wén)**:
**Your humble servant, Zhōu Xuándéng**, a **successor of the Complete Perfection (quán zhēn)** **disciple of the Small Dao Master (xiǎo zhào shēn)**, **sincerely fearful and reverent (chéng huáng chéng huáng)**, **prostrates himself with head bowed (qǐ shǒu dùn shǒu)**, **fasting and purifying himself with a hundred bows (zhāi mù bǎi bái)**, **petitions:**

*Truly, the Dao’s **mystery and effortless nature (miào wú wéi)** **manifests itself through time and circumstances (měi yīn shí ér zhuó jiàn)**; **human hearts have awareness (rén xīn yǒu jué)****,** and thus **should accumulate merit according to the place (yí suí dì yǐ jī gōng)**. Your humble servant, **Xuándéng**, though **of lowly disposition (wéi zhì)** and **the least of the Three Talents (sān cái mò pǐn)**, **aspires to the wondrous law and returns to the Mystic (mù miào fǎ yǐ guī xuán)**. Originally **a Confucian scholar (běn rú háng)**, he **later encountered the Dao (huì dào)**. Upon **first glimpsing the Imperial Sutra (yī dǔ Dì jīng)**, he **received its rare and precious truths (shèng huò zhēn yì)**. He **then meticulously studied each character (jí zhú zì yǐ jīng yán)**, hoping to **grasp enlightenment through its words (jì yīn wén ér liǎo wù)**. But since **the sacred texts lack annotations (shèng diǎn wú zhù)**, **true comprehension is difficult (tǐ rèn wéi nán)**.

Your humble servant **devotedly seeks sincere understanding (shēn zhì fā chóng qián)**, **exploring its multifaceted meanings (bó fāng jiě yì)**. He **compiled the Immortals’ and Saints’ sayings (xù zhuàn xiān shèng gé yán)**, **incorporating them into the Daoist Canon (huì rù Dào zàng hán bù)**. For the **three volumes of the true text (yīn sān juàn zhī zhēn wén)**, he **collected and arranged their sequence (yòng jí xù cì)**; for the **five grades of secret teachings (wù pǐn zhī mì lùn)**, he **listed them under chapter titles (yǐ liè piān míng)**. The **ten volumes (juàn biān wéi shí)** total **six hundred sheets (fú jì liù bǎi)**, **encompassing one hundred and eighteen chapters (zǒng liè yībǎi shíbā zhāng)**, with **over tenfold myriad words (dà luè shí yuè wàn yán)**.

The **heart-laws of a thousand sages (qiān shèng xīn fǎ)** **shine forth in these volumes (shǔ cè zhāo rán)**; the **vast sufferings and profound principles (hào jié xuán zōng)** **are visible at a glance (jǔ mù rú zài)**. Though your humble servant **cannot yet fathom the secrets of the Highest Sage (wèi néng dú kuī shàng shèng zhī yùn ào)**, he **hopes to at least enable others to witness the most exalted true texts (shì zhòng shí wén)**. **Even a small effort has its effect (cùn láo jì xiào)**; **a good connection may yet endure (liáng yuán ruò cún)**.

**With humble devotion (qiān jí)** to the **auspicious morning (cháo)** and **reverent diligence (qián kè)**, he **provides benefit to those of good faith (zī shàn xìn yǐ xié chéng)**. **The preface of this petition (yù zòu shū cí)**, **presented to the Mystic Judgment (shàng gān xuán jiàn)**, **augments the Emperor and people’s purity (zēng jūn mín qīng jìng zhī fú)** and **pardon the Small Dao Master’s presumption (shè xiǎo zhào jiàn wàng zhī zuì)**. May it **illuminate all realms and directions (shǐ zhū jiè duō fāng)** with the **seventeenfold radiance (shí qī guāng míng zhī zhào chè)**; may it **span past and future (jué jīn qīng gǔ)** and **immerse all in the thirtyfold great vows (shí sān shí dà yuàn zhī táo róng)**. May all **ascend to the Heavy Mystic (zhòng xuán)** and **eternally benefit from the law’s blessings (míng yáng yǒng zhān fǎ lì)**. Though your humble servant’s **sincerity is but a fraction (shǒu shēn xuán zhēng zhī chéng)****,** it **slightly fulfills its purpose (shǎo shēn wàn yī yǐ)**.

**Respectfully submitted (jǐn zòu)**.

Regarding the **meaning, annotations, and chapter arrangement of the sutra (jīng zhù míng yì xù cì kǎo)**:
*The original text sometimes appears as **one volume (zuò yī juàn zhě)****,** following the **model of the Supreme Ultimate (xiàng Tài jí)**. Others divide it into **three volumes (fēn sān juàn zhě)****,** symbolizing the **Three Talents (sān cái)**. Now, this annotation **comprises ten volumes (jīn zhù zuò shí juàn)****,** representing the **tenfold Supreme Ultimate (shí jí zhī yì)**—for the **Dao’s numbers are complete in ten (dào shù chéng yú shí)**. The **five grades (wù pǐn)** symbolize the **Five Phases (wǔ xíng)**. When the **Five Phases, Four Symbols (sì xiàng), and Eight Trigrams (bā guà)** are combined, they yield **seventeen (dé shí qī)**—all **divisions of the Supreme Ultimate (jiē Tài jí zhī fēn)**. Thus, the **Emperor attains the seventeenfold radiance (Dì yú shí qī guāng míng)**; **Heaven is born (Tiān yǐ shēng)** and **Earth is perfected (dì yǐ chéng)**.

The **Jade Emperor’s (Yù Dìshì)** **sutra is the **Earth’s (dì)** **curved completion of all things (qū chéng wàn wù)**. Earth’s **numbers are thirty (dì shù sān shí)****,** so the Emperor **manifests thirty kinds of virtue (shì sān shí zhǒng gōng dé)**. The **Emperor’s virtue surpasses the tenfold Supreme Ultimate (Dì dé chāo chū shí jí)****,** hence the **ten titles (jù shí hào)**. After **cultivating for countless kalpas (xiū yì wàn jié)****,** he **embodies the ten thousand virtues (zhōu wàn dé)**. Now, this **six-hundred-sheet annotation (liù bǎi fú zhù)** **mirrors the Fire Scripture’s six hundred chapters (xiàng huǒ jì liù bǎi piān)**; the **one hundred and eighteen chapters (yībǎi shíbā zhāng)** **follow the Emperor’s eighteen hundred precepts (cóng Dì qiān bā bǎi jiè)**. The **tenfold myriad words (shí wàn yú yán)** **reflect the Emperor’s ten thousand wondrous and mystic deeds (xiàng Dì shí wàn miào xíng xuán guāng)**.

As for the so-called *Imperial Sutra Annotation (Huáng jīng zhuàn)*, your humble servant fears that **the lowly and ignorant (xià yú)** **cannot fully align with the sacred text (bù néng quán qì shèng wén)**. He **summarizes the essentials (jǔ dà yào)** to **instruct others (yǐ zhào rù)**. Knowing this **intent (yì)****,** how could there be **divergent interpretations (bù tóng zhī zhǐ)**?

Regarding **contemplation, recitation, and exposition of the sutra’s precepts and teachings (guān sòng jiǎng shòu jīngdiǎn jiè yì)**:
**When observing or reciting any sutra (fán guān sòng zhū jīng)**, or **lecturing and transmitting its teachings (huò jiǎng míng shòu jiè)**, one must first **fast and purify oneself (zhāi míng zhěng yī)**, **adorn oneself in proper attire (yī zhuóng)****,** and **reverently place the sutra on a clean table (sù róng qǐng jīng zhì jìng qǐ shàng)**. **Sitting upright and steadying one’s mind (duān zuò dìng zhì)****,** one should **forget both good and evil (shàn è liǎng wàng)****,** **abandon all vehicles (yī chéng bù lì)****,** and **att

**Copying Sutra Precepts**
For all who copy the sutras, the ritual observances are the same as for recitation. With a rectified mind and a true pen, it is not for the sake of fine calligraphy—this very act is the Dao itself.

**Distinguishing Similar and Divergent Names of the Sutra**
Carefully examining *Baopuzi* states: *"The Highest Above"* refers to the sovereign of all sentient beings, reaching the utmost limits of Heaven—its height is unmatched, corresponding to the Buddhist term *non-retrogression* (不退转之地).

The *Jade Emperor* is the most revered among the Saints and the most noble among the Gods. All Buddhas and Holy Teachers, all Celestial Emperors, thus earn the title *Jade Emperor*.

*Lü Dongbin* says: *"Dao supreme and peerless is called Emperor."*

The *Most High Emperor* is boundless in benevolence and trust, surpassing all previous sages in perfect virtue and beauty—praise for Him is endless.

His station is in *Yuqing* (玉清), proclaiming the transformations of *Yuan Shi* (元始), hence the title *Jade Emperor*.

*Han Xiang* says: *"The Original Conduct"* recounts the Jade Emperor’s sacred roots and the cultivation of wondrous practices.

*The Collected Sutra* gathers the five wondrous utterances of *Yuan Shi* into one text, showing posterity the true path of practice.

*Guanshan* says: *"Only Heaven is supreme,"* for the Jade Emperor’s abode is the highest Heaven, surpassing all others, hence *"Highest Above."*

Men see the Jade Emperor’s grandeur and assume His virtue is absolute, beyond mortal reach. Yet the Holy Dao knows no division—I stand equal to the Most Holy.

The Emperor’s majesty, His marvels—these are achieved through conduct.

Thus, *Tian Shū* Zhang Shangling transmitted this text, urging men to emulate the Sage and attain True Reality.

The clear decree states: *"The Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct and Collected Sutra"* is meant for men to observe, attain enlightenment, trace the roots of merit, follow the Most Holy, and thus become *Shang Zhen* (上真).

Later, it was also called *"The Taishang Dongxuan Lingbao Scripture"*—speaking of the Great Beyond measure, the Highest Beyond reach, hence *Taishang*. It expounds the primordial *De* and *Dao*, serving as the eternal foundation of all scripture. It penetrates the Three *Jing* (景), revealing profound mysteries, hence *Dongxuan*. The essence of *Xuanling* is the eternal treasure of Heaven and man, hence *Lingbao*.

In essence, the scripture clarifies the Dao, and the Dao belongs to my very self. If man fulfills his nature and attains his destiny, comprehending this Dao, tracing its roots, and embodying it in conduct—then he may enter Sainthood.

**Belief in Scripture and the Discrimination of Ascension and Depravity**
From *Taiji*, man is born and transformed. Heavenly paradises and hellish realms are detailed in the scriptures—yet the world does not believe. Is this mere fabrication?

Though death returns to emptiness, what does not perish is the *hun* (魂) bound by deeds. *Bo You* became a ghostly calamity; *Zi Chan* believed him, and the Master did not deem it false. Are there no hells?

Purified rebirth returns to the cycle of creation; heavenly paradises exist as well. Yet blessings cannot be begged for, and karmic retribution cannot be evaded. Heavenly paradises and hells are shaped by human intent.

If one believes in these doctrines by name but does not cultivate virtue, he invites disaster himself. Even if he speaks daily of retribution, what good will it do?

For those who recite the scriptures, there are pure-hearted incantations—these are omitted here. Since earlier teachings aligned the heart with the Dao, this very recitation is the true incantation, so their texts are not recorded.

The original *Huangjing* (皇经) first listed thirty-six sacred titles, following the meaning of *"thirty-six from Heaven."* Now the scripture retains only ten precepts—why? The ten titles represent the ten extremes, used as the Emperor’s designation. It is not a matter of omitting due to brevity or inclusion. The observer should ponder this carefully.

**Commentary on the *Highest Above Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct and Collected Sutra***
This meaning is the *Dongxuan Lingbao*’s paired exposition—later generations should not doubt it.

**Long Kneeling and Reverent Adoration**
This scripture expounds the Jade Emperor’s wondrous conduct as revealed by *Yuan Shi*, so those who recite it must kneel in long reverence, offering sincere devotion.

**Supplication to the Three Pure Ones**
I humbly address the Three Pure Realms—the supreme, unmatched Three Pure Ones. Knowing the Dao’s height and the Three Pure’s grandeur, I sincerely aspire, surrendering body, spirit, and destiny, ascending to the True Heart.

**Gazing Up in Reverence**
I supplicate the *Yuqing* (玉清), the *Shangqing* (上清), and the *Taiqing* (太清).

The Three Pure Realms are the most exalted:
- *Yuqing* is the sacred realm of *Yuan Shi*,
- *Shangqing* is the true realm of *Lingbao*,
- *Taiqing* is the immortal realm of *De* and *Dao*—
the Three Pure Ancestors, the Great Celestial Worthy.

**Supplication to the Great Luo Heaven**
The boundless celestial expanse where life originates.

*Lü Dongbin* says: *"The Jade Emperor’s abode is the sovereign of the three thousand great thousand worlds, never retrogressing. Supreme beyond compare, hence *Great Luo* (大罗)."*

The *Xuan Qióng* (玄穹) Master—vast and solemn—is the sovereign of all celestial assemblies.

**Supplication to the Three Pure Realms and the Attendant Divine Multitude**
*Zhang Ziyang* says: *"Attendant"* means standing beside. *"Divine"* refers to the lofty, ineffable realm beyond sight or hearing. *"Multitude"* means all—
the *Nine Divine Ones of Primordial Heaven*, the *Heavenly Saints of Later Heaven*, all gods, Buddhas, bodhisattvas, *Arhats*, and *Vajrasattvas*—all are present here.

**The Marvelous Dao Beyond Conception**
The most marvelous, supreme Dao—
the highest vehicle—
cannot be grasped by thought,
cannot be spoken of,
is beyond conception.

**Entering the Mysterious Gate**
*Zhang Zifang* says: *"Entering"* means attaining through true knowledge and practice. *"Mysterious Gate"* is the gate of Daoic principle.

The myriad marvels of profound mystery are difficult to enter, yet through gradual enlightenment, one enters the Mysterious Gate.

This is what *Mencius* called *"dwelling in it securely, then drawing from it deeply,"* and the scriptures say: *"Hearing and thinking alone, without practice, leads to emptiness."*

**The Sutra’s Marvelous Sound and Profound Essence**
*"Loft"* (抉) means to decide, to extract. *"Profound Essence"* is the unfathomable mystery.

This marvelous scripture extracts divine inspiration from the true realm—this is the extraction of profound essence.

**Guiding the Dust-Ensnared to the Path**
*Yuan Shi* expounds the marvelous scripture, extracts the profound essence, and guides the dust-bound, lost souls out of the sea of suffering, freeing them from their karmic bonds.

**I Now Purify the Three Karmas**
*"I"* refers to those who read or recite the scripture. *"Three Karmas"* are bodily, verbal, and mental deeds. *"Purify"* means sincere devotion, permanently abandoning these deeds.

*(The recitation continues with) mouth and heart in unison.*

The devotee who recites this scripture speaks with true sincerity.
With mouth chanting and true heart receiving,
I humbly pray for boundless compassion—
May the Great Compassion open to accept my plea.
*"Compassion"*—one variant reads *"Reverence"*—but *"Compassion"* is correct.
In reciting this scripture, I humbly pray that Yuan Shi, the Jade Emperor, and all the Celestial Worthies extend their boundless compassion, reveal their merciful countenance, and accept my supplication.
If *"Reverence"* were used, it could not carry the meaning of the preceding three petitions.

May the radiant compassion illuminate my humble unworthiness,
May the Divine Hearing listen to my devotional chant.
May the sacred light of all Saints shine upon my sincere, lowly heart,
And may the Divine Hearing attend to the sounds of my offerings and recitation.
May my recitation resound through the Ten Directions—
When I recite the scripture, may the Dharma-sound echo through the Ten Directions, so that all beings in the Ten Directions may hear and believe in the Great Law.

May all my wishes be fulfilled,
As the scripture describes.
May I attain enlightenment through this scripture and cultivate the Dao,
Fulfilling all virtuous aspirations,
Just as the scripture recounts the Jade Emperor’s wondrous deeds across kalpas.

From this point onward, may I gradually progress in cultivation,
Achieving the Great Dao and serving the Celestial Saints.
From this moment, may I steadily advance in my practice,
Realizing the Great Way and paying homage to the Immortals and Saints.

With utmost sincerity, I bow and entrust myself—
Though my devotion may not yet be perfect,
If my heart is not fully devoted, even a slight regret would not be true surrender.
In reciting this scripture, I vow eternal sincerity without wavering in my practice, hence the phrase *"With utmost sincerity, I bow and entrust myself."*

To the Pure and Refined Celestial Realm—
Yuan Shi, the Most Exalted and Unparalleled,
The Sovereign of the Central Heaven,
Supreme over Immortals and Buddhas,
Whose abode is eternal and unspoiled—this is the Pure and Refined Celestial Realm.
The Celestial Palace of *Qingwei*. *(To be clarified in subsequent revelation.)*

Within the **Yùluó Xiāotái** (Jade Emperor’s Lofty Hall),
At the **Jǐngshàng** (Supreme Pinnacle) of the utmost heights,
A heaven within the heavens, radiant and fragrant with divine light,
Serene and truly pure—
Thus it is spoken of as **Yùluó Xiāotái**’s realm.

Above the **Sēnluó Jìnghóng** (Forest of Ten Thousand Things, Pure and Boundless),
Where resounds the vast and profound **Dharma** (Teachings),
So deep that it cannot be fully exhausted—
The heavens encompass myriad phenomena, profound and unfathomable,
Yet **Yùqīng** (Jade Purity) stands above all heavens.
Thus it is spoken of as above the **Sēnluó Jìnghóng**.

The **Míngxiǎn** (Manifested Form) is its **Fànxiàng** (Dharma Manifestation),
**Yuánshǐ Tiānzūn** (The Most Exalted Sovereign of Primordial Beginning),
As the **Zōng** (Founder) of the **Sānjiào** (Three Teachings),
Illuminating and transforming all beings,
Whose wonders are inexhaustible—
This is the **Míngxiǎn** (Manifested Form) of the **Yìfàn Miàoxiàng** (Ten Billions of Buddhas, Marvelous Manifestation).
Possessing the **Shéntōng** (Divine Penetration) of **Wújí** (Boundlessness).
Possessing the **Shéntōng** (Divine Penetration) of boundless magnitude.

It is said: *Yuánshǐ* (Primordial Beginning) is the **Wújí Dàdào** (Boundless Great Dao/Way),
Thus it is spoken of as such.
Expounding the **Zhēn Xuán** (True Mysterious),
Breaking the hindrances of **Wúyǒu sèkōng** (Non-existence, Form, and Emptiness);
Expounding and propagating widely,
Illuminating and elucidating the **Zhìzhēn Xuánzōng** (Ultimate True Mysterious Principle).
Breaking the worldly hindrances of **wúyǒu sèkōng** (non-existence, existence, form, and emptiness).
The **wú** (non-existence) is the principle of non-duality;
The **yǒu** (existence) is the indulgence in life;
The **sè** (form) is the attachment to existence;
The **kōng** (emptiness) is the failure to transcend **wúyǒu** (non-existence and existence).

*Yuánshǐ* (Primordial Beginning) in this **Sūtra** (Scripture),
Illuminates the **Zhēn Xuán** (True Mysterious),
Not confined to the **Sān guān** (Three Observations),
Nor trapped in the **Liǎng jì** (Two Realms).
Directly pointing to the **Rúrú Jiànchéng** (Thusness, Realization).
Thus breaking the hindrances of **wúyǒu sèkōng** (non-existence, existence, form, and emptiness),
And leading to the **Mìao** (Marvelous Dao/Way).
Rescuing and elevating all **Qùlèi** (Emotional Karmic Types),
Severing the divisions of **Zhìyú gāoxià** (Wisdom and Folly, High and Low).
Rescuing and elevating all beings of emotional karmic types, freeing them from dust,
Not discriminating between ancient and modern, saints and fools—
All can practice the **Dàodào** (Dao/Way).
This is the **Mìao fǎ** (Marvelous Law) of **Zhēnyī Wú'èr** (True Oneness, Non-duality),
Severing all distinctions of wisdom and folly, high and low.
Marvelous applications beyond measure,
Mysterious **Língjī** (Spiritual Mechanisms) beyond reckoning.
The **Zhìshèng Miàoyòng** (Supreme Saint’s Marvelous Applications) have no bounds,
Difficult to perceive, and the **Xuánlíng Dàojī** (Mysterious Spirit’s Dao Mechanisms) are beyond calculation.

With **Dàbēi Dàyuàn** (Great Compassion, Great Aspiration),
**Dàshèng Dàcí** (Great Saintliness, Great Benevolence),
**Wúliàng dùrén** (Boundless Salvation),
*Yuánshǐ Tiānzūn* (The Most Exalted Sovereign of Primordial Beginning).
Great Compassion—deep pity for the world;
Great Aspiration—endless transformation;
Great Saintliness—the most exalted among saints;
Great Benevolence—salvation without end.
Boundless Salvation—without limit.

The phrase of *Yuánshǐ*—to be clarified in subsequent revelation.

**Zhìxīn Guìmìng Lǐ** (With Utmost Sincerity, I Bow and Entrust Myself—Homage)
This is the declaration for those who **recite and contemplate** the **Sūtra** (Scripture),
With true heart paying homage to the Most Exalted.
Those who merely **mouth this phrase** today are not the same.

**Shàngqīng Zhēnjìng** (Upper Purity True Realm),
**Jǐngshàng Xuánqīng** (Supreme Pinnacle Mysterious Purity),
The **Zhìzhēn Miàojìng** (Ultimate True Mysterious Marvelous Realm).

The **Yuánshǐ** Celestial Palace of the **Yǔyú** (Primordial Jade).

From its beginning, **qīng** (Azure) becomes **tàibái** (Great White),
where **xuán** (Mysterious) light transforms into the **miào** (Marvelous) realm of **shénhuà** (Divine Manifestation),
eternally undestroyed, towering beyond measure, with **shén yùn** (Divine Motion) boundless.
The **Sūtra** speaks of the **Yuánbái** (Primordial White) **Yǔyú** Celestial Palace.
Within the **Zǐwēi Qióngtái** (Jade Pivot Celestial Terrace),
the **miào** (Marvelous) realm is unfathomable, forever unshaken—hence the name **Zǐwēi**.
Not the **Northern Dipper** (Beihxīn) **Zǐwēi Enclosure** (yuán).
The **Qióngtái** (Celestial Terrace) **Shàngqīng** (Upper Purity) Palace radiance,
adorned with countless **bǎo** (treasures), stands within the **Qióngtái**.
Above the **Xuándū Yùjīng** (Mysterious Capital Jade Capital).
**Shàngqīng** (Upper Purity), situated beyond the **Tài Xuándū Bái Yùjīng** (Great Mysterious Capital White Jade Capital).
A single word refers to the **Yùjīngshān** (Jade Capital Mountain) above the lofty heavens—also acceptable.

It connects with the **statutes** (xì) of the **Yuánshǐ Xūhuáng** (Primordial Beginning Void Emperor),
where **xì** (系, pronounced *xì* as in "下记切") means *continuation* (to inherit).
The **Língbǎo** (Soul-Treasure) body embodies the **Yuánxíng Huà** (Primordial Conduct Transformation),
thus ascending to inherit the **Yuánshǐ Xūhuáng** **Dàotǒng Shìxì** (Dao/Way lineage and succession).

It surpasses the **roots and origins** (gēnmiáo) of the **Xīnà Yùguó** (Western Jade Realm).
The **Sūtra** examines **Xīnà Yùguó** in Shaanxi’s **Xīnà** (Western Jade),
the birthplace of the **White Sovereign** (Báidì) in the west—
**Língbǎo** precedes all **saints’** (shèng) transformations,
thus it is said to transcend the **roots and origins** of **Xīnà Yùguó**.
One must not conflate **Yuánbái** (元白) with **Báidì** (白帝).
Some say *supercedes* (chāo) should be *inherits* (shào),
but the **Celestial Sovereign** (Tiānzūn) is not the **roots and origins** of **Xīnà Yùguó**—incorrect.

Entering the **shǔmǐ zhū** (glutinous millet pearls),
absorbing the **quánzhì** (complete) essence of **Zhēn Xuán** (True Mysterious).
The **Celestial Sovereign** (Tiānzūn) enters the **shǔmǐ Xuánzhū** (glutinous millet Mysterious Pearls).
This is the **Confucian** **jiǔróng Tàijí** (nine transformations of the Great Ultimate)
and the **Buddhist** **wù zhèngfǎ yǎnzàng** (awakening to the true Dharma-eye treasury).
**Quánzhì** (挹, *to extract fully*), penetrating this **Dao** (道) alone,
like the world’s grasp of rare treasures—
sated in the **ultimate taste** (zhìwèi), hence it is said:
to exhaustively extract the **Zhēn Xuán** (True Mysterious) essence—**quánzhì** (精粹) and **huágǔ** (refined perfection).

Within the **Xiānglín Yuàn** (Fragrant Grove Garden),
frequently expounding the **mìyào** (secret) **Zhēn** (True) **significant principles** (yàojiào) in the form of **qiāntí** (fishing net) and **bǔtì** (hare’s foot).
The **Celestial Sovereign** (Tiānzūn) resides in the **Shàngqīng Miàoxiāng Bǎolín Xuányuàn** (Upper Purity Marvelous Fragrant Treasure Grove Mysterious Garden),
often elucidating the **xuánmì** (Mysterious Secret) **Zhēn** (True) **yàojiào** (significant principles) through **qiāntí** (fishing nets) and **bǔtì** (hare’s feet).
The **Dao** (道) is inherently unsaid,
but the **Sūtra** (经) provides the **path of practice** (xiūxíng jìnglù).
It is like the **fishing net** (qiān) for catching fish,
or the **hare’s foot** (tí) for trapping hares—
tools that cannot be permanently held,
hence the **Sūtra** is likened to **qiāntí** (fishing nets and hare’s feet).
The **miàodé** (Marvelous Virtue/Power) is beyond thought,
and the **shéntōng** (Divine Abilities) are beyond imitation.

The **Celestial Sovereign**’s (Tiānzūn) **miàodé** (Marvelous Virtue/Power) defies contemplation,
and **shéntōng** (Divine Abilities) cannot be replicated.

The **Great Compassion and Great Aspiration** (Dàbēi Dàyuàn) of the **Great Sage and Great Benevolence** (Dàshèng Dàcí) are boundless in liberating beings—
as previously expounded (Jiějiàn qián).

**Lingbao Tianzūn** (灵宝天尊).
At first, **Qīng** (青) reaches **Taibai** (太白),
and **Yuánshǐ** (元始) again manifests the **Marvelous Transformation** (Miàohuà).
Dwelling in **Shangqing** (上清),
**Lingbao** moves with boundless efficacy (Wúfāng),
a **treasure of the Dao** (Dàodào fǎbǎo) passed on without end.
Thus, it is **Lingbao Tianzūn** (灵宝天尊).

With **sincere reverence** (Zhìxīn guīmìng lǐ),
he pays homage to the **Supreme Purity’s** (Tàiqīng xiānjìng)
**Celestial Realm** (Xianjìng),
the **Great Vermilion Heavenly Palace** (Dàchì Tiān gōng).

The **Three Purity Domains** (Sānqīng jìngtiān) and the **Heavenly Palaces** (Gōng) are originally one,
illuminated by **Mysterious Light** (Xuánguāng) in boundless splendor (Wúqióngjìn),
hence the **Supreme Purity’s Celestial Realm** (Tàiqīng xiānjìng).
**Yuánbái** (元白) scatters **ethereal mists** (Sǎnxiá),
while **Chìxiáng** (赤祥) pervades all—
eternally unspoiled and undiminished (Yǒngwú huǐlún),
thus called the **Great Vermilion Heavenly Palace** (Dàchì Tiān gōng).
This is not merely the **red hue** (Chìhóng) of color.

The **lofty Golden Gate** (Wēiwēi Jīnquè) stands high,
and the **vast Nine Heavens** (Chóngxiāo) stretch boundlessly above.
The **Supreme Sage** (Tàishàng) dwells in **lofty immobility** (Wēiwēi bùdòng),
the **most exalted and supreme** (Zuìshàng Zhìdà).
Without peer or equal (Wúbǐlún),
his **Golden Light** (Jīnguāng) is unspoiled.
The **Mysterious Gate** (Xuànquè) stands high and vast,
difficult to fathom (Wúqióng).
He eternally resides in the **Nine Celestial Enclosures** (Jiǔchén),
**Ninefold Layers** (Jiǔchóng),
and **Nine Heavens** (Jiǔxiāo) above.
Some say: **crowned above the Thirty-Six Heavens** (Sānshíliù Tiān chóngxiāo).
Born in the **infinite kalpas** (Wúliàngshù jié),
the **Supreme Sage** (Tàishàng) traverses kalpas in **transformative activity** (Xínghuà),
without measure or end (Wúliàngshù),
unfathomable and unexhausted (Bùkē qióngtàn).
The **Mysterious Source of the Dao** (Dàodào xuánzōng) is thus born in **infinite kalpas** (Wúliàngshù jié).

He expounds the **Dharma** (Shìfǎ) across **twelve thousand heavens** (Wàn èrqiān tiān).
The **Supreme Sage** (Tàishàng) has traversed kalpas,
manifesting throughout the **Three Thousand Great Thousands** (Sānqiān Dàqiān).
This refers to his **Dharma expounding in twelve thousand heavens** (Shìfǎ wàn èrqiān tiān),
where the **Supreme Sage’s** (Tàishàng) **Dharma assemblies** (Shìfǎ guān) extend to **twelve thousand heavenly realms** (Wàn èrqiān tiān jiè).

**Five Thousand Mysterious Teachings** (Wǔqiān mìyán),
blending the **Marvelous Dao of the Three Realms** (Sān-cái miàodào);
The **Dao** (Dào) possesses **five thousand** (Wǔqiān) **Mysterious Teachings** (Mìyán),
permeating the **three realms of Heaven, Earth, and Humanity** (Tiān-dì-rén sān-cái).

**Eighty-One Transformations** (Bāshìyī huà),
guiding beings of the **Six Paths** (Liùqù) to liberation.
**Eighty-One Transformations** (Bāshìyī huà),
leading and guiding the **six classes of beings**—**celestial, human, asura, demon, hellish, and animal** (Tiān-rén-móguǐ-yùchú liù děngqù)—
or some say: the **six paths of desire**—**sight, sound, smell, taste, touch, and mind** (Yǎn-ěr-bí-shé-shēn-yì liùqù)—
or the **Six Paths of Existence**—**having, non-having, form, formlessness, cognizer, and cognized** (Yǒu-wú-sè-kōng-néng-suǒ liùqù).
Some derive it from **拯** (Zhěng),
to **rescue and awaken beings to the True Dao** (Zhěngjiù wùdào chéngzhēn).
The **Six Paths** (Liùqù) are difficult to escape,
yet the **Supreme Sage** (Tàishàng) descends in **compassionate instruction** (Cíyǐ jiàohuà),
employing **divine methods** (Shìjì) to liberate **sentient beings, ghosts, and spirits** (Shénrén guǐwù) from dust.
Hence, it is also called **拯** (Zhěng).

His **Sage’s Virtue** (Shèngdé) is exalted,
and his **Mysterious Function** (Xuán-gōng) is vast.
The **Supreme Sage’s** (Tàishàng) **Sage’s Virtue** (Shèngdé) is **lofty and revered** (Zōnggāo lónggāo),
his **Mysterious Function** (Xuán-gōng) **universally vast and profound** (Pǔguǎng bódà),
deep and unfathomable (Shēnhòu mòqióng).
Thus, it is called **Mysterious Function** (Xuán-gōng).

The **Great Compassion and Great Aspiration** (Dàbēi Dàyuàn),
the **Great Sage and Great Benevolence** (Dàshèng Dàcí),
boundless in liberating beings—
as previously expounded (Jiějiàn qián).

The **Born-in-Heaven Celestial Sovereign** (Jiàngshēng Tiānzūn).
The **Supreme Sage** (Tàishàng) manifests **infinite transformations** (Xiǎnhuà wúliàng),
his **compassionate grace** (Cí’ēn) is endless,
eternally generating without cessation (Shēngshēng bùyǐ),
hence called the **Born-in-Heaven Celestial Sovereign** (Jiàngshēng Tiānzūn).

With **sincere reverence** (Zhìxīn guīmìng lǐ),
he pays homage to the **True Realm of Marvelous Existence** (Miàoyǒu zhēnjìng),
the **Palace of Míluó** (Míluó shànggōng).
The **Palace** (Shànggōng) is the **name of the Holy Sovereign’s** (Yùdì Shèngfù) **Celestial Abode** (Gōngmíng).

In past kalpas, he was revealed as the **body of a sovereign king** (Xiàngshǐ xiànwáng zhī shēn).

In ancient times, he manifested in the radiant and wondrous **Light-Strong Joyful King** (Guāngyán Miàolè Wáng) form—
this being the essence of the **Root Sovereign** (Běnběn Dìzūn),
the very substance of the **Supreme Holy Sovereign of Ten Thousand Heavens** (Wàn Tiān Shèngdì Cízūn).

At first, his form was serene and still—
the **Holy Father** (Shèngfù), the **Origin of Dao Transformation** (Dàohuà Zōngshǐ),
his wondrous form ever pure, motionless in stillness.
Truly profound, supremely mysterious, and ineffable—
this primordial stillness, truly profound and distant,
most divine and wondrous, yet beyond speech or discourse.

In succession, he ascended the throne, transmitting the lineage—
his virtue unmatched, unparalleled, and ever succeeding.
He inherited the **Light-Strong King’s sovereign position** (Guāngyán Guó Jūn wèi),
continuing the royal lineage, his virtue surpassing all others in kind.
Following the ancestral deeds, his virtue and blessings grew ever more vast—
thus it is said: *wondrous, unmatched, unparalleled, and ever succeeding.*

The **Holy Father’s** compassionate and merciful parent,
the **Supreme Most-High** (Zuìshàng Zuìshàngzūn).
The **Jade Sovereign** (Yùdì) is called the **Compassionate Parent of All Beings** (Zhòngshēng Cífù),
his station the most exalted.
The **Holy Father** refers to the **Jade Sovereign**—
the **Light-Strong King** gave birth to the **Jade Sovereign**, thus the **Holy Father’s** compassionate and merciful parent,
the **Supreme Most-High**.

Praise is boundless, devotion endless—
the **King-born Jade Sovereign**’s merits are eternal.
Thus praise is boundless, devotion without end.

The **Great Compassionate, Great-Vowed Parent-Heaven Sovereign** (Dàbēi Dàyuàn Fù Tiānzūn),
the **Great Sage, Great-Compassionate Light-Strong Joyful King Holy Father Heaven Sovereign** (Dàshèng Dàcí Guāngyán Miàolè Wáng Shèngfù Tiānzūn).
Here, the **Holy Father** refers to the **Light-Strong King**, for he gave birth to the **Most Holy**.

With **sincere reverence**, he pays homage to the **True Realm of Marvelous Existence** (Miàoyǒu zhēnjìng),
the **Palace of Míluó’s Inner Sanctum** (Míluó Nèigōng).
The **Inner Sanctum** is the **Jade Sovereign’s** deepest palace, where the **Holy Mother** resides—
thus it is called the **Inner Sanctum**.

Her **compassionate countenance** shines like the harmonious spring sun,
her **virtuous bearing** stern as the solemn autumn frost.
Her **pure Dao-qi** (Zhēnqiàn fènqì) existed before Heaven and Earth;
her **perfect emptiness and Dao-qi** (Xūwú fènqì) subtly prefigured existence before the cosmos.
She manifested her wondrous form through successive consorts,
giving birth to the **Sovereign** in due time.
She bore the **embryonic essence of the One Qi** (Yīqì pèitāi zhī shǐ),
revealing the beginning of embryonic formation—
*embryo* (pèi), when form and qi first take shape;
*tāi*, when form and qi gradually manifest.
She embodied the **Sovereign’s** unique generative transformation,
rooted in the **Origin of Ten Thousand Transformations** (Wànhuà Zǔgēn),
the **Compassionate Mother of All Beings** (Zhòngshēng Címǔ).

Great in compassion and vow, great in sagehood and mercy—
the **Precious Moonlight Empress** (Bǎoyuè Guāng Huánghòu), the **Holy Mother Prime Sovereign** (Yuánjūn Shèngmǔ).

With **sincere reverence**, he pays homage to the **Purple-Gold Celestial Gate** (Zǐjīn Jīnquè),
the **White Jade Jade-Capital** (Bái Yù Yùjīng).
The **Purple-Gold Gate** and the **Yellow-Gold Gate** are not two—
the **Sovereign’s** celestial palace, its divine light and treasures unmatched,
a perpetual abode of purity.
The **Yellow-Gold Gate** is where he rests in splendor.
The **Purple-Gold Gate** is where he resides in majesty.
The **double splendor of gold and jade** is fitting praise.

Dwelling in the **Realm of Marvelous Existence** (Zhù Miàoyǒu zhī jìngzhōng),
[abiding in the **Heaven of Supreme Truth** (Chǔ Xuánzhēn zhī tiānshàng)].
Ever residing in the boundless, traceless true realm,
permanently dwelling in the **Supreme Mysterious True Heaven** above.
His **Dao accomplished, his virtue complete**—
thus his wondrous form surpasses all heavens.
The **Universal Teacher of Ten Thousand Heavens, the Jade Sovereign** (Yùhuáng Wàn Tiān Jiàozhǔ),
therefore crowned above all heavens.
His **heart vast, his body plump**—
thus his compassionate light pervades the Three Realms.
His **nature is boundless as Heaven**—
his wondrous body ever thus—
his heart inherently vast, his body inherently plump.
Since mortals cannot, there is no light.
When the **Jade Sovereign** attained the Dao,
his heart was as boundless as the **Great Void** (Tàixū),
his Dao-body naturally radiant—
thus his compassionate light illuminates the Three Realms.

His station is exalted, surpassing all that is supreme—
his position unmatched, hence *supreme above all supreme*.
His Dao is mysterious, profound beyond profundity—
the **Jade Sovereign’s** Dao is exalted and unfathomable,
truly *mysterious beyond mystery*.
The **True Holy Originator** (Zhēnshèng Zōngshī), the **reliance of Heaven and humankind**.

Great in compassion and vow, great in sagehood and mercy—
(as expounded in separate chapters).

The **Vault-of-Heaven Holy King** (Qióngcāng Shèngwáng),
the **Great Heaven Sovereign Jade Emperor** (Dà Tiānzūn Yùhuáng).

The **Vault-of-Heaven Holy Sovereign** is the **Clan King of All Heavens**—
this title extols the **Jade Sovereign’s** exaltation.

With **sincere reverence**, he pays homage to the **Light-Strong Kingdom within the Wondrous Joyful Land** (Guāngyán Guówèi Miàolè Tǔzhōng).
(as expounded in later annotations).

The **Holy Mother** concentrated her spirit in a dream within the void—
the **Holy Mother** dreamed the **Dao Lord** (Dàojūn) handed her an infant,
thus giving birth to the **Jade Sovereign**.
This was a **divine dream** (Shéndòng) within the void,
though its auspicious marvel was extraordinary.
The **Dao Lord** bestowed the **Jade Essence** (Yùzhì) in a hazy, distant realm.
Her **compassionate and yielding demeanor** was profound—
her benevolent affection, her gentle humility.

The **Vault-of-Heaven Holy Sovereign** does not covet the exalted honor of the **Ten-Thousand-Chariot Sovereignty**—
the **Ten-Thousand-Chariot** refers to the great realm where a state dispatches ten thousand chariots.
The **Jade Sovereign** renounced the **Kingly Position**,
thus not coveting the honor and glory of the **Ten-Thousand-Chariot Lord’s** sovereignty.
With **enduring forbearance** and **virtuous gentleness**, he bore no weariness in the **infinite kalpas** of cultivation and practice.
Enduring all humiliation with **virtue and tenderness**,
he never faltered in the **infinite kalpas** of refining his **power** and walking the **Dao**.

His **power** surpasses all comparison,
his **virtue** profound, impossible to surpass.
His **deeds** and **practice** transcend all ranks,
his **benevolent virtue** surpasses all bounds—
