do not understand its meaning,
dare not believe or follow it,
thus they slight the **Great Law** (*Dàfǎ*)
and mislead themselves.
The **Great Dao/Way**’s compassion is boundless,
unable to bear the world’s delusion,
thus it speaks of benefits to guide beings.
How can the foolish and deluded still say,
*"This **Scripture** merely contains trivial and obscure theories—
what benefit does it bring?"*

Do they not know that this **Scripture** gives birth to all **Heavens**, earth, and beings,
and cannot be separated for even a moment?
All beings, everywhere, should recite and uphold it,
throughout kalpas without end,
bringing great natural benefits,
not merely alluring people with effects.
Is it not most excellent?
This is not a word of doubt,
but a commendation of the excellent inquiry.

*"You"* (*rǔ*)—
Yuan Shi addresses the Jade Void Emperor.
*"I"* (*wú*)—
Yuan Shi refers to himself.
*"Return to your seat"* (*fù zuò*)—
a command for the Jade Void Emperor to resume his listening position.

*"I shall expound"* (*xiānshuò*)—
*broadly proclaim* (*guǎngbù wéi xiān*) and *explain* (*gàoyǔ wéi shuò*).

**Fàn** (*Brahmā*)—
pronounced as *fú* (with the tone of 扶 *fú*).

Some mistakenly write it as **梵** (*Fàn*), but this is incorrect.

This is the sincere request to expound the **Scripture**,
and the heart of universal benefit.

**Continuation of Chapter 18, following the previous ten chapters**
The Celestial Venerable spoke:

*"If within the Three Realms or the ten directions of boundless lands,
wars arise and armies clash,
or pestilential **qi** (*yìqì*) spreads,
or floods, droughts, insects, and locusts plague the land,
or calamities bring famine,
then the kings and ministers of those lands
should issue compassionate decrees,
commanding all officials in their states, counties, towns, and prefectures,
to order the **Dao/Way**’s adherents (*Dàomén zhūliú*)
to maintain purity and solemnity,
and within their **observatories** (*guàn*)
establish grand **fasting rituals** (*Zhāijiào*),
practicing the **Dao/Way** at all six times of day,
to circulate this **Scripture**,
then the land will achieve peace,
the five grains will flourish abundantly,
and the people will live in security and harmony."*

After the Yuan Shi Celestial Venerable commanded the Jade Void Emperor to return to his seat and listen to the **Scripture**,
he spoke thus:

*"If within the Three Realms—**Heavens**, earth, and humans—
or the ten directions of the four **Quadrants** (*Sìzhèng*), four **Pairs** (*Sì’ǒu*), and their upper and lower tiers,
or the limitless lands of all **Realms**,
wars arise and armies clash,
or Heavenly calamities spread, encountering pestilential **qi** (*yìqì*) rampant,
or years bring scarcity, with floods, droughts, insects, and locusts,
or disasters cause famine,
then the kings and ministers of those lands
should issue compassionate decrees,
for their **黎民** (*Límín*—**common folk**), officials, and subjects,
commanding all within the states, counties, towns, and prefectures,
to order the **Dao/Way**’s adherents (*Dàomén zhūliú*)
to maintain **清冷** (*qīnglěng*—**cool purity**) and solemnity (*yánjié*),
and within their **observatories** (*guàn*)
establish grand **齐醮** (*Qíjiào*—**fasting rituals for purification and expiation**),
practicing the **Dao/Way** at all six times of day (*báijiū xiángdào*),
to circulate this **True Scripture**,
then the land will achieve peace (*qīngpíng*),
the five grains will flourish abundantly (*wǔgǔ fēngshú*),
and the people will live in security and harmony (*Límín āntài*)."*

Some may say the Three Realms cannot be called **Heavens**,
for fear of conflicting with the phrase *lands, armies, and calamities*.
But the **Heavenly Demons** (*Tiānmó*) and Heavenly sovereigns
contend for dominion in the streets,
engaging in battles,
each with their own demarcated **Realms** (*jiè*),
thus it is known that the Three Realms refer to **Heavens**, earth, and humans.

「When wars and conflicts (*bīnggē*) erupt, it refers not to two distinct kinds of weapons rising simultaneously, but rather to hostilities breaking out in various places—each side engaging in mutual warfare. Swords, spears, and all such implements are simply weapons (*bīngqì*), no different from *戈* (*gē*—**halberds**) or *戟* (*jǐ*—**crossbow spears**). Thus, it is incorrect to say that "wars and conflicts" (*bīnggē*) arise together.

Some may argue that "wars and conflicts" (*bīnggē*) mean "soldiers and weapons" (*bīng zuò rén*—**soldiers and men**), with "men" and "weapons" (*rén gē*) arising together, but this is also not accurate.

When pestilential **qi** (*yìqì*—**epidemic qi**) spreads rampantly, the **Dao/Way** of Heaven (*Tiāndào*—**Heavenly Dao/Way**) maintains its regular order, yet calamities are termed as "variations" (*bìan*—**aberrations**). The rampant spread of pestilential **qi** (*yìqì*) is indeed a calamity (*zāiyì*—**disaster and aberration**). The same holds true for epidemics (*shíli*—**seasonal pestilence**), which are also calamities (*zāiyì*).

This **Scripture** (*jīng*—**Sutra**) serves to rescue and alleviate such afflictions.

Floods and droughts (*shuǐhàn*—**water and fire calamities**), insects ravaging crops (*chóng*—**pests**), and swarms of locusts destroying harvests (*qúnxiāng shāngjià*—**locusts harm the grain**) are all calamities (*zāiyì*).

When harvests fail (*suì bù shú*—**years of poor harvest**), causing suffering among people and creatures (*mínwù bù ān*—**the populace and living beings are unsettled**), it is termed as *凶* (*xiōng*—**harsh calamity**). When things deviate from the norm (*yìcháng*—**aberrant**), it is called *灾* (*zāi*—**disaster**); when grains are not ripe (*gǔ bù shú*—**grains do not mature**), it is *饥* (*jī*—**famine**); when vegetables are not ripe (*cài bù shú*—**vegetables do not mature**), it is *馑* (*jǐn*—**scarcity**).

All these are calamities (*zāiyì*).

*黎* (*Lí*—**common folk**), *黔黎* (*Qiánlí*—**the dark-skinned commoners**); *庶* (*shù*—**commoners**), *庶民* (*shùmín*—**the populace**).
*遍勑* (*biànli*—**to exhaustively exhort**).
*遍* (*biàn*) and *徧* (*biàn*) are the same.

*州县镇宰* (*zhōuxiàn zhènzǎi*—**regional governors and magistrates**), which may mean:
- the officials who govern states and counties, overseeing the common folk (*zhōuxiàn tǒngzhèn bǎixìng zhī guān*—**governors and magistrates who control the populace**), or
- the officials of military garrisons (*zhèn*—**military prefectures**), or
- the high-ranking officials such as the viceroys and governors-general (*duūfū*—**supervisors and envoys**).

All interpretations are valid.

These are the kings and ministers of their respective lands, just as the kings and ministers of these places [mentioned earlier].」

「The Daoists, including those of the **Quánzhēn** (Complete Reality), **Zhèngyī** (Orthodox Unity), **Qīngwēi** (Pure Mystery), and **Língbǎo** (Numinous Treasure) sects, are marked by **purity and solemnity**, both inwardly and outwardly, with their bodies and minds in perfect harmony. Their attire and ritual spaces are meticulously ordered, and they conduct themselves with **reverence, solemnity, and unwavering consistency**—thus embodying **purity and solemnity**.

*Guān* (观), meaning **contemplation**, is where the **divine presence** resides. Those who gaze upon it rise in **awe and respect**—this is indeed the **Great Vision**. Hence, it is called *guān*.

They establish **grand liturgical rites** (*dàzhài jiào*—**great exorcistic offerings**), harmonizing the inner and outer, uniting the collective will, and rectifying discord through **fasting** (*zhāi*). They **invoke and thank the divine beings** (*qíxiè shénzhī*—**pray to and give thanks to the divine**), repay the heavens and earth, **concentrate virtue upon the divine** (*hé dé yú shén*—**merge virtue with the divine**), and, following the prescribed methods, **attract blessings** (*yīkē qìfú*—**invoke blessings according to the ritual**) through *jiào* (醮).

They practice the Dao **six times daily** (*liùshí xíngdào*—**sixfold Daoic observance**), not as the common practice of wandering along roads, but simply by **following the ritual to invoke the divine** (*yīkē qìshén*—**invoke the divine according to the ritual**) and **reciting scriptures and Daoic teachings** (*zhuǎnjīng niàndào*—**turning the scriptures and reciting the Dao**).

Some say the **twelve times of day and night** (*shíèr shí*), with **odd hours** (*qíshí*) for activity and **even hours** (*ǒushí*) for stillness. The **six times** (*liùshí*) should be understood as **子, 寅, 辰, 午, 申, 戍**—the **midnight, 3-5 AM, 7-9 AM, noon, 3-5 PM, and 7-9 PM hours**. Alternatively, some interpret it as the **six daytime hours** (*báizhòu liùshí*—**six hours of daylight**). Both interpretations are acceptable.

**Turning the scriptures** (*zhuǎnjīng*) means aligning one’s mind with the Dao, holding the **authentic scriptures** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scriptures**), ensuring that **lands and beings are free from calamity** (*guótǔ wú èjiān*—**countries and beings without hardship**), and attaining **serene peace** (*dé qīngpíng*).

Rice, millet, sorghum, beans, and wheat—**the five grains** (*wǔgǔ*)—all flourish in abundance. The **common folk** (*língmín*—**people of the populace**) across all lands and realms suffer no disasters, forever dwelling in **tranquil security** (*ānrán dìng*—**secure stillness**) and **unshaken joy** (*tàirán lè*—**unfaltering happiness**).

The **merits and virtues** (*gōngdé pǐn*) continue from the previous nineteen chapters. If one encounters **venomous and ferocious beasts** (*dú è wūshòu*—**poisonous, evil, and fierce beasts**) in the mountains and forests, simply **retain a single thought** (*cúnxiǎng yīniàn*—**hold in mind a single thought**) of the **true scriptures** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scriptures**), and the **mountain deities** (*shāngshén*—**mountain spirits**) will guard and protect, while the beasts will naturally retreat, never harming the practitioner.

If one enters rivers and seas, **seeking treasures and precious things** (*cǎibǎo qiúzhēnjiàn*—**gathering treasures and seeking precious artifacts**), and encounters **malevolent winds** (*èfēng*—**evil winds**), causing the vessel to drift, then by **reciting and holding** (*shòu*—**receiving/holding**) this **true scripture** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scripture**) in accordance with the method, the winds will cease and the waves will still, allowing **safe arrival at shore** (*ānwěn dá'àn*—**securely reaching the shore**).

The blessings of the **true scripture** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scripture**) are not merely limited to **dispelling celestial calamities** (*xiāo tiānzāi*—**eliminating heavenly disasters**), ensuring **abundant harvests year after year** (*fēng suìnián*—**richness of years and harvests**), and **securing the populace** (*lìngshù ān*—**the commoners’ peace**). Even **sudden misfortunes** (*zùrán zhī biàn*—**sudden changes**), such as **mountains, rivers, winds, and waves** (*shānshuǐ fēngbō*—**mountains, waters, winds, and waves**) bringing peril, cannot harm the practitioner.

If one enters the mountains and forests and encounters **venomous and ferocious beasts** (*dú è wūshòu*—**poisonous, evil, and fierce beasts**), simply **retain a single thought** (*cúnxiǎng yīniàn*—**hold in mind a single thought**) of the **true scripture** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scripture**), never forgetting this **precious and wondrous method** (*bǎozhāng miàofǎ*—**treasured chapter and marvelous method**). The **mountain deities** (*shāngshén*—**mountain spirits**) will **guard and bestow protection** (*bǎowèi yòuhù*—**guard and protect**), and the beasts will naturally retreat, never harming the one who holds the scripture and enters the mountain.

If one enters the rivers and seas, **seeking treasures and precious artifacts** (*cǎibǎowù qiúzhēnjiàn*—**gathering treasures and seeking precious things**), and encounters **malevolent winds** (*èfēng*—**evil winds**), causing their **ships and boats** (*chuán fáng*—**vessels and boats**) to drift, then by following the **method of recitation and reception** (*rújīng zhōng shòushòu zhīfǎ*—**as the scripture teaches, the method of recitation and holding**) and **holding this true scripture** (*cúnxiǎng zhēnjīng*—**retaining this true scripture**), the great winds will subside and the waves will cease, allowing the **safe arrival of the practitioner’s vessel at shore** (*chuán wéi shāng’àn*—**the vessel’s secure arrival at shore**), with no harm befalling the one who holds the scripture.

Mountains and forests are **treacherous and obstructed** (*xiǎnzǔ*—**dangerous and blocked**), and **ferocious beasts and venomous insects** (*měngshòu dúchóng*—**fierce beasts and poisonous insects**) are **not to be approached** (*shì bùkě jìn*—**their nature forbids nearness**). If one encounters them, **injury is inevitable** (*bì zhì shānghài*—**certainly will be harmed**).

Yet, if one **retains a single thought** (*cúnxiǎng yīniàn*—**holds in mind a single thought**) of the **true scripture** (*zhēnjīng*—**true scripture**), merely **temporarily aligning with the Dao** (*bùguò zàn yǔ dào hé*—**nothing more than briefly merging with the Dao**), how can the beasts retreat so readily?

This is because **all beings—human and otherwise—originate from the same primordial *qi*** (*yuánqì*—**original *qi***), though they differ in **clarity and turbidity, completeness and partiality** (*qīngzhuó quánpiān*—**pure and impure, complete and incomplete**).

At the **beginning of heaven and earth** (*tiāndì zhī chū*—**when heaven and earth first formed**), humans and beasts coexisted in a **mixed and indistinct state** (*hùnchǔ rán*—**in a mingled, indistinct manner**), where **venomous insects and ferocious beasts** (*dúchóng èshòu*—**poisonous insects and evil beasts**) originally did not harm people.

Later, as **human hearts grew false** (*rén xīn jiàn jiǎ*—**human minds became deceptive**), the **distance between humans and beasts widened** (*qù èchóng wūshòu*—**separation from venomous insects and fierce beasts**), leading to the beasts’ harm toward humans.

If humans **constantly perform good deeds** (*cháng xíng hǎoshì*—**always do good deeds**), **nurture benevolent thoughts** (*cún hǎoxīn*—**hold good hearts**), and **revere and trust the true scriptures** (*jìngxìn zhēnjīng*—**respect and believe the true scriptures**), never forgetting them, they become **great virtuous ones** (*dà shànrén*—**great benevolent people**).

Thus, when entering mountains and forests, they **will not encounter venomous insects or fierce beasts** (*zì bù yùdú è wūshòu*—**naturally will not meet venomous, evil beasts**).

If, however, one **ordinarily indifferent and lacking in virtue** (*yōngcháng wú shàngǒng*—**habitually mediocre without virtuous deeds**), enters the mountain and **suddenly encounters venomous insects or fierce beasts** (*shìrán yùdú è wūshòu*—**unexpectedly meets venomous, evil beasts**), yet **does not covet life nor fear death** (*bù tānshēng pàsǐ*—**not greedy for life nor afraid of death**), **does not panic nor lose composure** (*bù huángjù bù sīxīn*—**not flustered nor distracted in mind**), but **trusts in the true teaching** (*wéi xìn zhèngfǎ*—**solely believes in the true law**), **remains steadfast without wavering** (*zhuān yī wú èr*—**single-minded and unshaken**), **focuses inwardly and contemplates silently** (*cāocún mòxiǎng*—**holds in mind and silently reflects**), **retaining a single thought** (*yīniàn zhēnjīng*—**a single thought of the true scripture**), their **mind and the Dao merge** (*xīn yǔ dào jù*—**heart and Dao become one**), and the **mountain deities guard and protect**, while the **venomous insects and fierce beasts naturally retreat**.

Beasts and insects are **stupid creatures** (*chǔnwù*—**dumb things**) of the Daoic path, though their **nature may be venomous and fierce** (*xìng suī dú è*—**nature though poisonous and evil**), they **kill and harm** (*hǎo shāngshā*—**love to kill and harm**). Yet, each has **objects of reverence, fears, and taboos** (*yǒu jìng, yǒu wèi, yǒu suǒjì*—**things they revere, fear, and avoid**).

Thus, **raptorial birds** (*zhìniǎo*—**fierce birds**) **revere the phoenix** (*zūn fèng*—**honor the *fèng* [august bird]**), **ferocious beasts** (*měngshòu*—**fierce beasts**) **bow to the qilin** (*cháo lín*—**pay homage to the *qílín* [auspicious unicorn]**), and **snakes, scorpions, centipedes, and other venomous insects** (*shéxiē wúgǒu zhūdúchóng*—**snakes, scorpions, centipedes, and other poisonous insects**) **fear cranes, *mànghóng* birds, herons, and *pèng* birds** (*wèi guàn mánghóng niǎo hè péng*—**dread the crane, *mànghóng* bird, heron, and *pèng* bird**), vanishing and refraining from their venom.

**Immortal Daoists** (*xiānzhēn*—**immortal sages**) **comprehend the mechanism of life and transformation** (*dá shēnghuà zhī jī*—**grasp the principle of life and change**) and **know the source of control** (*míng kèzhì zhī yuán*—**understand the origin of subjugation**). Even **a single incantation** (*yī zhòuyǔ*—**one incantation**) or **a single talisman** (*yī fúshuǐ*—**one talisman**) inscribed with water can **subdue venomous insects and serpents** (*zhì chóngshé dú*—**control poisonous insects and snakes**), **resolve the calamity of tiger ferocity** (*jiě hǔhěn è*—**alleviate the tiger’s ferocious disaster**), **reverse the winds and turn the heavens** (*fǎnfēng huìtiān*—**turn back the winds and return the heavens**), and much more. How much greater is the **power of the *Huángjīng*** (*Huángjīng*—**the *Huángjīng* [Yellow Scripture]**), which is **the sovereign of all teachings** (*wànfǎ zhī zōng*—**the root of all laws**) and **the progenitor of heaven and earth** (*tiāndì zhī zǔ*—**the parent of heaven and earth**)!

The **birth and death of all things** (*wànwù shēngsǎ*—**all beings’ life and death**) **depend upon heaven and earth**, which in turn **originate from the Great Dao** (*běn yú dàdào*—**stem from the Great Way**).

Thus, when one **retains a single thought** (*cúnxiǎng yīniàn*—**holds in mind a single thought**) of this scripture, they **need not fear beasts and insects** (*bùjù chóngshòu*—**not dread beasts and insects**). The **radiance of the scriptural treasure** (*fǎbǎo guāng*—**the light of the sacred treasure**) shines, and **all deities guard** (*zhūshén wèi*—**all spirits protect**), though the beasts may be **stupid**, their **nature still reveres the Dao** (*xìng yì zūndào*—**nature respects the Way**), **fearing heaven and revering the divine** (*wèi tiān jù shén*—**dreading heaven and fearing the spirits**), and thus **naturally retreat**.

Rivers, lakes, and seas—**winds and waves pose dangers** (*fēngbō wēixiǎn*—**winds and waves are perilous**), seemingly **the heavens’ wrath** (*tiān zhī nù*—**heaven’s anger**), and **escape seems difficult** (*shù suǒ nán táo*—**fate seems hard to evade**). Yet this scripture is **the king of all teachings** (*wànfǎ zhī wáng*—**the sovereign of all laws**), and **winds, thunder, hail, and lightning** (*fēngléi báo diàn*—**winds, thunder, hail, and lightning**) are **the heavens’ wondrous applications of divine power** (*tiān zhī miàoyòng shénwēi*—**heaven’s marvelous use of spiritual might**).

If one **holds and recites this true scripture** (*cúnxiǎng zhēnjīng*—**retains this true scripture**) in accordance with the method, they **align with heaven and the Dao** (*tóng yú tiān, tóng yú dào*—**become one with heaven and the Dao**), and **heaven itself will cease its wrath** (*tiān yì wèi zhī jìwēi*—**heaven will abate its might**), allowing the **winds to subside and the waves to still** (*fēng xī, làng zhǐ*—**winds cease, waves still**), and the **vessel to reach shore securely** (*chuán ānrán dá’àn*—**the ship safely arrives**).

**Verification and examination**: The *Yì* (易, *I Ching*) states: *"Treading upon a tiger, its jaws bare—disaster."* The Master Confucius said: *"Confronting a tiger barehanded and leaning upon a river in peril—die without regret."* Yet this scripture declares: *"If one retains a single thought and holds this true scripture in accordance with the method, beasts will retreat and winds and waves will cease."* The *Dàodéjīng* (道德经, *Tao Te Ching*) speaks: *"Those who align with the Dao: falcons do not strike, venomous insects do not sting, tigers and rhinoceroses dare not brandish their claws and horns, but hide their teeth and retreat their talons, not daring to harm."*

Many doubt that **Confucianism and Daoism contradict each other** (*rúdào xiāng bèi*—**

The efficacy of the scripture can yet deliver one from beasts and dispel venomous karmic influences—how could those who recite it be like the *Lu* and *Qi* states, where poisonous vapors arise?

**Chapter on Virtue and Power (续二十章):**
If in battle, when spears and halberds clash and blades interlock, one steadfastly retains the thought and silently recites this true scripture, all malevolent foes will retreat and disperse.

The benefits of this true scripture are not merely to dispel beasts, winds, and calamities! If in battle, when weapons are raised and spears and halberds clash, blades interlocking in the two armies’ confrontation, one steadfastly retains the thought and silently recites this true scripture—all the hostile foes assaulting our ranks will retreat and disperse.

**Verification:**
Weapons are instruments of slaughter. Battle is perilous. In the charge against enemies, arrows and stones fly, blades clash like roaring tigers—an irresolvable struggle. Yet if one steadfastly retains the thought and silently recites this true scripture, how, if one’s heart aligns with the Dao, could the malevolent foes not retreat?

The military classics say: *"The morale of three armies can be undermined; the resolve of a general can be shattered."* Silently reciting the true scripture, one seizes their spirit and subdues their vitality. This wondrous scripture’s power causes the enemy to lose their resolve, abandoning their will to fight, turning from evil to good, and naturally withdrawing and scattering.

"Battle" does not refer to armies numbering ten or twenty-five hundred—rather, when troops form ranks and confront one another in combat. "Spear combat" is not a matter of formal distinctions; "clash" and "interlock" differ little—only following the scripture’s phrasing of weapons meeting in battle. Steadfastly retaining the thought and silently reciting the true scripture is not for mere avoidance of slaughter—it is to devote one’s heart entirely, even facing death without abandoning the Dao.

*"All"* means "many." *"Malevolent foes"*—some interpret this as "malevolent" referring to evil persons, "foes" to bandits. This division is incorrect. It simply means hostile rebels.

*"Retreat and disperse"* means to withdraw and return, to scatter and depart each to their own.

**Resolving Doubts:**
The Venerable Lord transformed in Hu, besieged by the army of Yutian. The Heavenly Sovereign resided in the Celestial Palace, while the Heavenly Demon raised arms to challenge. The Buddha dwelled in the realm of Magadha, where the six kings of Kāliṅga rebelled. Confucius transformed the world, felling trees in Chen and erasing his tracks in Song. These were all great sages.

The Dao-body, the Dharma-body—constantly turning the true scripture, observing as if assailed by foes. Later, the Venerable Lord radiated the Dao-light, and Yutian submitted. The Sovereign displayed the Heavenly Light, and the Heavenly Demon withdrew. The Buddha manifested the Dharma-light, and the six kings converted. Confucius shone with virtue-light, and when he thrice plucked his lute and thrice sang in harmony, the people of Qi laid down their arms.

Thus, they retreated and dispersed.

Yet consider that many foes have sworn never to harm the virtuous. Many virtuous have faced peril without dying. Some doubt the case of the Song emperors Huizong and Qinzong, who, though devoted to the Dao, suffered humiliation in the north; or Liang Wu, who, though fond of Buddhism, starved to death in the Tai City. They assume the scripture’s efficacy is unproven.

Yet the three rulers’ devotion to Dao and Buddhism was merely in name, not genuine.

「When passions remain unsevered, one cannot govern the world with the Dao/Way, hence these calamities arise. If one truly embodies the Dao/Way and upholds faith in the scripture’s efficacy, even commoners—men and women alike—may avert such trials.

To doubt the deliverance from death and adversity or to disbelieve the scripture’s teachings is indeed erroneous. Alas, extolling unwavering integrity serves to inspire the world; reciting the scripture’s virtues stirs others to do good.

In essence, the scripture’s intent lies within the nature of our own inherent Dao/Way. When the six senses (六根) are assailed by thieves (贼) of discord, and one’s mind remains steadfast in the Dao/Way, the six thieves retreat. Thus, even in the face of armies, Heaven itself resolves the peril. Laozi proclaimed: *"Armies cannot harm."* Guanyin declared: *"The blade seeks only to sever flesh, yet justice prevails."* Their words are no deception—this is the natural efficacy of the scripture’s virtue.

**Continuation of the *Merits and Virtues* (功德品) in Chapter 21:**
If one finds oneself imprisoned in shackles (枷锁), with a purified mind and settled thoughts, yet ever mindful of this scripture, wrongs shall be redressed and liberation attained. The scripture’s benefits extend far beyond dispersing bandits and armies—even if one has wrongfully incurred guilt and lies in chains, by keeping the heart and mind clear, steadfast in reciting this true scripture, wrongs shall naturally be revealed and deliverance achieved.

**Verification:**
Prisons exist to confine the guilty. The rewards of virtue and retribution for vice are the immutable laws of Heaven. Once imprisoned for a crime, one cannot simply escape—how then does it say that mindfulness of this scripture brings immediate liberation?

The phrase *"wrongs shall be redressed"* (冤枉自伸) implies that such a person, in their ordinary life, must inherently be virtuous. Perhaps in a past existence they incurred karmic debts (宿世充愆), or in this life they face misfortune (今生运限); or they may have been wrongfully accused (误失过失, 他人挂误), or drawn into another’s crime (先亡连逮, 救人被陷). When suddenly cast into prison, all such cases are unjust.

If one neither blames Heaven nor resents others, enduring hardship with equanimity (素患难, 行乎患难), free from malice or ill-will (绝无意想), then one’s mind is purified, thoughts settled, and devotion to this true scripture is genuine. Heaven aids the virtuous—wrongs are naturally exposed, requiring no defense, and justice is swiftly rendered. There is no prolonged suffering, for Heaven does not permit enduring injustice; liberation comes at once.

**Definitions:**
Prison (牢狱): *Lao* (牢) refers to confinement; *yù* (狱) refers to awaiting trial. Modern terms like *jianyáng* (监仓, prison cells) and *pùchǎng* (铺厂, detention centers) vary in severity, but both are places where criminals reside. The two characters do not strictly differentiate—*jiā* (枷) and *suǒ* (锁) are restraints for the guilty, arising from unforeseen circumstances (变故).

Some say: *"Lao" derives from cattle (牛), "yù" from dogs (犬).* If one refrains from slaughtering cattle and dogs, prison shall be forever avoided. Yet this merely counsels against killing for sustenance (不食牛犬) and restrains the tongue (勿纵口), lest one invite calamity through gluttony (以味招祸).

Beyond the scripture’s core teachings, this is an ancillary note.

The scripture’s benefits include redressing wrongs and granting liberation—not only for those unjustly imprisoned but also for those who, in ordinary life, have committed crimes yet repent sincerely, harboring no resentment. If one steadfastly relies on the scripture’s power, without faltering, liberation shall come.

King Wen of Zhou (文王) attained sainthood through the Dao/Way. Imprisoned in *Yǔlǐ* (羑里), he studied the *Yijing* (《易经》) and was pardoned. Gongye Chang (公冶长) aspired to the Dao/Way and became a sage. Though bound in chains (缧绁), he too found release. Xu Shen Gong (徐神公) and Zhang Ziyang (张紫阳) achieved transcendence through the Dao/Way. Despite the torments of *Chāngyì* (昌邑) imprisonment and the Three Refined Ones’ (三配) afflictions, their devoted practice of the supreme Dao/Way and profound transmission of *The Awakening to Reality* (《悟真》) secured their deliverance.

It is not only sages who are liberated—even the foolish, if they cast aside worldly attachments (除去维念), place absolute faith in this scripture, shall escape the bonds of prison. The misfortunes of *lao* and *yù* shall dissolve.

**Dispelling Doubts:**
In the remote antiquity, there were no guilty criminals nor prisons. The Yellow Emperor (轩辕) captured *Chīyóu* (蚩尤), binding him with fetters (桎梏) and marking the earth to restrain him—thus the concept of prisons emerged. By the Three Dynasties (三代), the system of imprisonment was fully established.

This scripture was revealed before the age of great calamities (浩劫), when the Primordial Beginning (元始) spoke of it in Heaven. How then does it mention prisons? The truth is that in every age (劫劫), in every place, there are virtuous and wicked. The wicked naturally incur karmic retribution (孽), and the logic of prisons is already inherent.

The scripture encompasses all dharmas (万法), benefiting all sentient beings (群动) eternally. Its principles are exhaustive—it foretells the power to liberate from guilt.

The scripture declares: *"Mindful of Guanyin’s power, chains shall swiftly depart."* Confucian texts say: *"The virtuous man contemplates retribution."* The *Great Yijing* (《大易》) states: *"No calamity comes without cause."* How could these not speak of prisons? Thus, the scripture is not a teaching of recent times—it is an ancient, profound revelation (无始玄章).

In summary, a single mindful thought aligns with virtue (福堂); a single thought of selfishness invites karmic bonds (业狱). If one’s desires and delusions persist unchecked, a pit of karmic debts is dug, and prison becomes inevitable.

Mencius said: *"The difference between humans and beasts is but slight."* *Lao* (牢) derives from cattle (牛), *yù* (狱) from dogs (犬). The creator of these characters held deep meaning. Let all present and future beings exert effort and place unwavering faith in this scripture—through every age and place, prisons shall be forever avoided.

**Continuation of the *Merits and Virtues* (功德品) in Chapter 22:**
If one is tormented by malevolent spirits, demons, or thieves (邪精鬼贼), yet recites this true scripture in accordance with its methods, the malevolent shall flee, and one shall find peace.

The divine efficacy of the *Jade Scripture* (玉经) extends beyond liberating from prison—if one is afflicted by all manner of malevolent spirits, demons, or thieves (邪魔精怪鬼贼), and recites this true scripture as prescribed, all malevolent spirits, demons, and thieves shall retreat and vanish, leaving one in natural security and tranquility.

**Verification:**
*"If one is"* (若为) is equivalent to *"as one is"* (如为). Malevolent spirits, demons, or thieves (邪精鬼贼) encompass all that is not upright (不正)—spirits that exploit supernatural abilities to wreak havoc (通灵而逞妖异者为精), malevolent entities of the unseen realm (阴之灵者为鬼), and those that harm humans or things (伤人害物曰贼).

Some say *"贼"* refers to human malefactors. Yet earlier it was stated that armies and wicked bandits (军阵恶贼) all disperse. How then could *"贼"* here mean human wrongdoers? Essentially, malevolent spirits, demons, or thieves (邪魔妖精鬼怪) seize opportunities and exploit weaknesses, entering through the flaws of those who are not virtuous.

Their origins are unknown—from whence they come; their departures are unfathomable—whither they go. They strike in darkness, inflicting harm without warning, hence they are called *guǐzéi* (鬼贼, demonic thieves).」

From the celestial *Tianmo* (天魔) down to earthly *tujing* (土精), mountain *wāngliang* (山魍魉), aquatic *shuàiyì* (水怪异), arboreal *mèi* (木魅) and metallic *jīng* (金精), fiery *yāo* (火妖) and herbaceous *yì* (草异), the *jing* (精) of birds and beasts, the anomalies of ice and embers (*bīngtàn zhī guài*), and the malevolent *chīniè* (魑孽) and spectral *guīlíng* (鬼灵)—these malevolent entities are countless.

Their afflictions manifest as hurling tiles and bricks, startling fowl and canines, demanding sacrifices, and disturbing households. They may cause one to be disoriented, spiritless and dazed, raving without cause, fleeing in lamentation, bewildered and insensible, capering and vomiting, roaring in lustful depravity, drunkenly deranged, losing one’s faculties, unable to rest or eat, perpetually anxious day and night—living in perpetual unrest, dying with lingering attachments. This is the suffering of *zhòngkǔ* (众苦).

*"Jiā"* (加) means to inflict calamity upon others.

It is said: *"As the law prescribes, recite this true scripture."* Yet if these malevolent spirits and *zhòngkǔ* (众苦) afflict one, how can simply reciting the scripture as prescribed dispel them?

*"As the law prescribes"* does not mean mere ritual recitation—it is the unity of *yī* (一, singularity) with the mind and the Dao’s truth. When this scripture is chanted according to the proper method of recitation, with reverent gazing, bowing, and intoning, all malevolent spirits and thieves will retreat.

Alternatively, it is said: *"As the law prescrices, recite the true scripture"*—meaning a Daoist practitioner should recite the scripture on behalf of the afflicted. Thus, all malevolent entities will retreat, and the afflicted will naturally find peace, without need for talismans, elixirs, or exorcistic incantations. Upon hearing the scripture, they will flee, and the suffering will cease, leaving none afflicted.

It is said that the Ancestor Celestial Master subdued all demons with the law. The *Xuandi* (玄帝) cultivated the True Way, annihilating all malevolent *jingyé* (精邪) and governing both human and ghostly realms. The *Sà Zhēnrén* (萨真人) expounded the Dao, banishing evil spirits. The *Lǎojūn* (老君) subdued the celestial demon. The *Fó Fàn* (佛梵) invoked spells to conquer demons.

The scholar-official *Fàn Wénzhènggōng* (范文正公), after a night on the battlefield, heard only the crowing of a rooster—no ghosts dared act malevolently. *Chéngzǐ* (程子) subdued the *Dàtóuguǐ* (大头鬼), and even when the ghosts moved his bed, his mind remained undisturbed, and the spirits withdrew in hiding.

Thus it is said:
*"When the Dao is exalted, dragons and tigers submit;
When virtue is profound, ghosts and spirits revere."*

To recite the true scripture as the law prescribes—this secret canon, the most sacred utterance—reveals the unbreakable mechanism by which ghosts and spirits are vanquished. How could any malevolent spirit or demonic thief dare not retreat?

**Resolving Doubts:**
Essentially, within the human body, the *sānshī* (三尸), *wǔqióng* (五穷), *qīpò* (七魄), the *qīqíng* (七情), and *liùyù* (六欲), along with all manner of delusive thoughts and fantasies, and the myriad dark inclinations—all are manifestations of malevolent spirits and thieves. If one awakens to the luminous void and wields the wisdom-sword to slay demons, exhausting all desires, then malevolent spirits and thieves will retreat.

---
**Chapter Twenty-Three of the *Gōngdé Pǐn* (功德品) – Continuation:**

If one seeks descendants, and reverently upholds and recites this scripture as the law prescribes, the Celestial Sovereign commands the *Tiāncháo* (天曹), who then inspect the *Dānjí* (丹籍) of the Nine Ranks. Among the *sìguǒ xiānrén* (四果仙人), when fate and destiny align, they descend and incarnate to become their child—endowed with eloquence, wisdom, and noble status among mortals.

The efficacy of this scripture is not merely to subdue malevolent forces. If one, afflicted by childlessness, seeks descendants and upholds this scripture with reverence as prescribed, the Celestial Sovereign commands the *Tiāncháo* to examine the *Dānshū Xiānjí* (丹书仙籍). Among the Nine Ranks, the *sìguǒ xiānrén* (四果仙人), when their cosmic cycles and numerical destinies converge, descend and incarnate to become their child.

The child born to one who recites this scripture for descendants will be gifted with eloquence, wisdom, and intelligence, attaining noble status among humanity.

*"Qí"* (祈) means to pray and supplicate the gods in seeking.

Sometimes, others pray for one; other times, one seeks for oneself. Whether one has descendants or not depends on Heaven’s decree—if it cannot be sought, it cannot be sought. Of the three gravest offenses against filial piety, childlessness is the greatest. One must seek descendants, for all who possess *xuèqì* (血气) are capable of procreation.

Perhaps one has exhausted *yīndé* (阴德) or incurred Heaven’s wrath; perhaps one’s *yáng* (阳) and *yīn* (阴) are misaligned, or one’s fate clashes with solitude; perhaps the fetus is weak or one harms oneself in anger, resulting in childlessness.

Yet human resolve can reverse Heaven’s decree—through utmost sincerity and divine resonance, none will remain childless. Thus, descendants can be sought.

*"Sìxī"* (嗣息) means *"sì"* (嗣, to continue) and *"xī"* (息, breath). Some say *"sì"* means to bind, as in binding the ancestral line like a continuous thread. Others say *"sì"* means to govern, overseeing the transmission of family lineage, as recorded in ancestral tablets. *"Xī"* (息) refers to children who continue the ancestral line, like the unceasing inhalation and exhalation of breath.

Moreover, the true breath is the root of life and death—if breath ceases, *qì* (气) vanishes. Having descendants ensures the continuity of sacrifices, hence *"xī"* (息). *"Tàidǐ xī"* (太抵息) refers to the mind itself. With descendants, all concerns are fulfilled, and the mind finds rest—thus it is called *"xī"* (息).

The sages of the Three Teachings all had descendants. How can one not recognize the weight of progeny?

To uphold this scripture with reverence is to revere the scripture itself. Some say one must personally revere it—which is incorrect. The *Tiāncháo* are those who create destinies and oversee the *Xiānjí* (仙籍). The Nine Ranks consist of the upper three *shèng* (乘), the middle three, and the lower three—totaling nine.

The *Shìjìng* (释经) states: *"The Nine-Ranked Lotus is the parent."* The Buddha, Bodhisattvas, *Yuánjué* (圆觉), *Shèngwén* (声闻), and *Āluóhàn* (阿罗汉), as well as those in the four *zhān* (禅) stages, also belong to the Nine Ranks.

The *sìguǒ xiānrén* (四果仙人)—*Xūduōhàn* (须陀洹), *Sītuǒhán* (斯陀含), *Āluóhàn* (阿罗汉), and *Ānàhàn* (阿那含)—descend and incarnate. For the Daoist or Buddhist to take human form is considered descending to the mortal realm, hence *"jiàngdié xiàshēng"* (降谪下生).

*"Cái"* (才) refers to extraordinary talents; *"biàn"* (辩) refers to unparalleled eloquence.

The light shines without failing.
The wisdom awakens without obstruction.

Among mortals, the most honored are not necessarily those who become rulers, ministers, or teachers—
but those who embody **virtue** and the **Way**, perfecting themselves as exemplary sons.
No greater honor than the **Way**,
No greater nobility than **virtue**.
Even the Son of Heaven cannot make them his subject,
Nor can the feudal lords make them their friend.
They assist in governance, nurture the people,
And aid in the completion of all things.
Across countless generations, they are revered,
And across the Three Realms, they are held in esteem.
Thus, they are the most honored among mortals.

If one reveres this **sutra** as law,
Reciting it for oneself or seeking descendants through it,
Though its effects are manifest, one cannot reckon the days—
Only by truly honoring the **sutra**,
Confessing faults with sincerity,
And remaining steadfast from beginning to end,
As though gazing upon the Jade Emperor,
With utmost reverence for this sacred **dharma**,
Will divine efficacy and spiritual power unfold unseen,
Turning fate and altering destiny—
Descendants will naturally arise.

Even mortal heroes gain offspring through merit.
Those who truly believe in the **sutra** and turn the **Dharma Wheel**,
As the functional pillars of heaven and earth,
How could their descendants not prosper?
If one reveres this **sutra** yet fails to secure descendants,
It must be that their sincerity is insufficient,
Or they have not followed the **sutra** from start to finish.

Let all mortals take heed and verify the **sutra’s** divine efficacy.

**Functional Merit Chapter (Continuation, Twenty-Fourth Section):**
If a woman in her critical month of childbirth
Recites this true **sutra** according to the law,
She will give birth safely, mother and child both unharmed,
And bear children of fortune and **virtue**, beloved and respected by all.

The **sutra’s** divine power does more than merely ensure descendants.
If a woman in her critical month of childbirth
Recites this true **sutra** according to the law,
She will deliver swiftly and safely,
Mother and child both unscathed,
And bear children of auspicious fortune and **virtue**, beloved and honored by all.

Once a woman is married into her husband’s family, she is called a **wife**.
The "critical month" refers to the time of childbirth,
When life and death hang in the balance—
Thus, it is called "facing peril."
Reciting the true **sutra** according to the law:
Whether before birth, when she herself observes a pure fast and recites the **sutra**,
Or during birth, when others recite it for her,
She will deliver safely,
With no complications at the hour of birth,
The child born without harm to mother or child,
Both emerging smoothly and in good health—
A benefit to both.

**Fortune** refers to those of wealth, nobility, longevity, and auspicious appearance.
**Virtue** refers to the saintly, loyal, filial, and kind—those of moral excellence.
**Children**, whether male or female, bear **fortune** and **virtue**.
**Beloved and respected** means they are approachable yet not familiar,
Near yet not to be trifled with—
All draw near to them, praise them, and envy them.
This is called **love**.
Yet, when seen from afar, reverence arises;
When approached, laziness fades;
Without words, trust is given;
Without movement, respect is shown.
This is called **respect**.

**Clarification:**
It is fitting for a man to be beloved and respected.
But how can a woman be so?
If her **fortune** is complete and her conduct virtuous,
If she does not weep or jest,
If she is dignified, speaks little,
Moves seldom, and does not laugh,
If she is mature beyond her years,
Grave yet pure in adulthood,
And unchanging until death—
All will love her as kin,
Respect her as elders.
This love is without familiarity;
They envy her **fortune** and **virtue**—
A rarity in the world.

**Verification:**
Mother and child both safe.

The *Shijing*’s chapter *"Shēngmín"* praises Jiāng Yù in giving birth to Hòuxī, saying:
*"The firstborn was born like a strike—no calamity, no harm."*
Jiāng Yù possessed **virtue**, so her firstborn emerged as easily as a lamb—unharmed, with mother and child both at peace.
The *Exegesis* states: *"Mother and child parted early."*
The *Dao Scriptures* declare: *"At childbirth, there is joy; seated on grass, there is no peril."*
The merit of reciting the *Scriptures* responds like an echo.

Now, the *Huángjīng* spreads throughout the world, and many recite it.
Yet women in childbirth may suffer:
Some deliver prematurely before their time,
Some face calamity or peril,
Some encounter ghostly births or omens,
Some endure misfortune or familial strife—
Though many achieve mother and child’s safety, few attain both fully;
Some suffer dual harm as well.

Some say reciting the *Scriptures* may bring no benefit,
Yet the True Law is rare to encounter.
Many do not revere this *Scripture* or know its blessings;
Some hear its name but do not honor it;
Some pay hollow respect without recitation,
Some recite but begin with fervor and end in neglect;
Some omit or confuse passages,
Some recite carelessly, mispronouncing words, distorting phrases,
Misinterpreting meaning—
Though they may offer repentance, they fail to gain the full merit of the *Scripture*.
All these are self-deception, failing to meet the *Scripture*’s power,
Thus concluding that recitation is fruitless—
This is blasphemy against the Law.

Alas, the True Law must be upheld,
And filial piety is hard to repay.
Rescuing suffering, benefiting life—
This is the urgent duty of those who seek the *Way*.
If we teach the world to revere and recite this *Scripture*,
Then mothers and children will be at peace,
Childbirth perils will be averted,
And virtuous sons and daughters will be born—
All will bear marks of **fortune** and **virtue**,
And the True *Dao* will endure forever.
The merit is boundless.

Let those who study the *Scripture* take heed.

**End of Volume Six of *Huángjīng* Annotations**
**Volume Seven of *Huángjīng* Annotations**
Verified by the **Great True Person**, the **Fifty-First Heavenly Master of the Han Dynasty**, Zhāng Guóxióng.
Reviewed by the **State Scholar and Recluse of Jiangxi Jìshuǐ**, Luó Hóngxiān.
Compiled by **Zhōu Xuánzhēn**, the **Lesser Master of Jiàn** in Shāndōng Jìnán.
**Continuation of Chapter Twenty-Five: The Merit of Virtue**

If one seeks to attain office and advance in rank,
to secure noble titles and abundant stipends,
to be honored by the sovereign—
if one recites and upholds this *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then one shall be granted promotions in duty,
one’s descendants shall prosper in honor and rank,
and this lineage shall endure through the ages.

The benefits of the *Jade Scripture* extend far beyond mere prosperity in childbirth!
If one seeks to attain office and advance in rank,
to secure noble titles and abundant stipends,
to be honored by the sovereign—
if one recites and upholds this *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then one shall be entrusted with official duties,
ascend in rank and station,
and one’s descendants shall prosper in honor and rank,
enduring through the ages without cessation.

**Seeking Office:**
Even without office, one may obtain it.
**Advancement in Rank:**
*Advancement* means promotion.
If one’s station is humble, one seeks to rise to higher office and noble duty.
**Titles:**
Titles are conferred upon officials.
**Stipends:**
Stipends are the remuneration given.
**Abundant and Auspicious:**
*Heng* signifies prosperity, ease, and joy—auspicious and beneficial.
**Fulfillment:**
*Da* means to achieve one’s desires, to succeed in one’s aspirations.
**Honored by the Sovereign:**
To be distinguished is called *noble*; titles and stipends are abundant, and one gains the sovereign’s favor, administering affairs and receiving the ruler’s recognition.
The harmony between ruler and subject has always been rare.
To be noble and honored by the sovereign means the subject’s rank is not in vain—this is true fulfillment.
*Alternatively:* To be favored by a wise and enlightened ruler.

*This Scripture* is not redundant; its phrasing is deliberate.

**Official Duties:**
*Job* refers to the responsibilities of office, each with its designated tasks.
*Matter* refers to governance.
**Promotion:**
To be reassigned to a better post or relieved of trivial duties to assume a position of importance.
**Descendants’ Honor and Rank:**
Some inherit office and stipends through generations,
or receive patronage for their children and grandchildren,
enjoying wealth, security, and prestige,
illuminating ancestors and benefiting posterity—
both honored and prosperous, enduring through the ages.
Though not equal to the heavens and earth in permanence,
they endure eternally, blessing future generations,
with grace extending unbroken.
Even across many generations, this is considered enduring.

As with **Confucius the Sage’s** supreme virtue,
or the **Celestial Master’s** divine transformations,
his descendants received imperial appointments through the ages—
this is true, unbroken honor and rank.

**Titles and stipends** originate from the imperial court’s official appointments.
If they cannot be obtained through merit,
one may follow established qualifications for advancement.
If advancement is unattainable through merit,
how much more so must one study diligently—
scholars must master texts, warriors must know warfare.
Learning and achievements cannot be borrowed;
how then can one seek advancement?

Officials are appointed for their virtue,
and stipends are granted to nourish the worthy.
Those of great virtue must attain their rightful position and name.
If one upholds this *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
recites its sacred words,
and follows the Sage’s teachings,
one’s heart aligns with the heavens,
and one’s actions harmonize with the *Way*—
this is the mark of a truly virtuous person.

Some are praised in speech,
others commended in deed;
without titles, they are granted offices,
without rank, they receive stipends,
or their existing offices are elevated—
this is the natural course of employing the worthy.

By virtue, one attracts the worthy.
If they refuse such honors—
as **Broad Achievement**, **Yin Shou**, **Chao You**, or **Yan Guang**—
whether as imperial preceptors or honored guests of the state,
how can it be said that the virtuous cannot attain titles and stipends?
As with **Han’s Zhuge Liang**,
or **Jin-Tang’s Jingyang, Li Bei, and Hai Dan**,
all were men of the *Way* who held office.

The *Scripture* speaks of seeking office—
what more need be said?

**Heavenly Titles** are noble indeed,
and they belong to us inherently.
Ascending beyond the mundane to sainthood,
advancing in virtue step by step,
manifesting divine transformations to attain immortality—
this is unbroken through kalpas.

The *Dao De Jing* says:
*"To die yet not perish."*
The *Transmissions of the Immortals* declare:
*"A child is born, and the child bears grandchildren."*

The *Way* is exalted, virtue is noble,
and the transmissions of the immortals are boundless.
If one does not covet worldly fame or transient gain,
but cultivates the **Heavenly Title’s** true nobility,
transcending the ordinary to approach sainthood,
rising above the dust to attain immortality—
enduring forever without end,
this is truly to uphold the *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts.

---
**Continuation of Chapter Twenty-Six: The Merit of Wealth**

If one desires to amass abundant wealth,
and upholds this *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then treasures shall overflow,
clothing and food shall come naturally,
and blessings shall flow to descendants,
passing to future generations.

The benefits of this *Scripture* extend far beyond fulfilling worldly ambitions for office!
If one desires abundant wealth for one’s family,
and upholds this *True Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then riches, treasures, and precious curiosities shall fill to overflowing,
clothing and food shall be plentiful and refined,
naturally abundant without effort,
with blessings extending to descendants,
passing to future generations.

**Wealth:**
*Resource*—what one’s family requires.
*Alternatively:* That which one relies upon, benefiting all.
Same as *capital*.
**Treasures:**
*Wealth*—the wealth one possesses.
*Also:* Wealth as a resource.
**Abundant:**
*Yin*—fullness, completeness.
**Rich:**
When a household’s prosperity reaches its peak,
and resources are fully sufficient.
**Uphold:**
*Delight in reverence* is *uphold*;
to guard, observe, and recite.
**Treasures:**
*Wealth*—the *wealth* of goods.
*Precious*—jade, gold, silver, gems, rare curiosities,
ornaments, silks, and treasures of extraordinary value.
**Overflowing:**
*Chong*—fully sufficient.
*Yi*—abundantly full.
**Clothing and food naturally:**
Without toil, naturally abundant.
**Blessings flow to descendants:**
*Reg* signifies auspiciousness.
Grace extends far, blessing generation after generation—
thus, *blessings flow to descendants*.
**Passing to future generations:**
Not limited to one’s own children,
but transmitted through the ages,
with later generations eternally enjoying peace and honor.

**Resolving Doubts:**
**Confucius** said:
*"Wealth, if it can be sought, even a lowly driver I would serve."*
If it cannot be sought, then follow what one loves.
He strongly states that wealth is not to be pursued—
yet here it is said that if one seeks abundance by upholding this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
one shall attain prosperity and blessings for descendants.
This suggests that wealth *can* be sought.

**Zi Xia** said:
*"The Master heard: Wealth and nobility are decreed by Heaven."*
Though wealth is desirable, fate governs it,
and Heaven truly holds dominion—
how then can it be sought?
Yet though wealth is subject to fate,
the ancient scholars said:
*"Wealth and nobility are the rewards for virtue’s culmination,
a repayment for merit."*

If one upholds and recites this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
speaking the words of Heaven with reverence as though addressing the August Sky,
this is how virtue earns its blessings.

「The *Classics* say: *"Joy belongs to the virtuous gentleman,
blessings follow those who tread the peaceful Way."*
This is what is meant.

Some say: *"Great Yu was a sage,
who drank little and ate plainly,
wore coarse garments and lived in humble dwellings,
yet found sweetness only in simplicity and restraint."*
The Daoist teachings state: *"To learn the Dao, one must embrace poverty to the marrow of the bones."*
This suggests that reciting the *Scripture* can bring wealth—
a claim that may entice those who crave prosperity.

Yu’s own frugality was the heart of a sage who did not hoard virtue for himself.
The Daoists’ pursuit of poverty was to free the mind from worldly burdens.
Though wealth *can* be sought and obtained,
this is the intended effect of upholding the *Scripture*.

The *Buddha’s Scriptures* say: *"All that one seeks with sincere intent
shall be fulfilled and satisfied."*
Both teachings open vast pathways of expedience—
boundless blessings and benefits,
where requests are answered and wishes fulfilled.
If one doubts, hesitates, or falters—
beginning with diligence yet ending in neglect—
if one’s heart is not upright,
lacks steadfast faith, or is not utterly sincere,
then even seeking shall yield no result.
Let those who observe the *Scripture* understand this well.

Consider: all things are inherently complete within me.
There are those who are naturally wealthy without effort.
Yet why do people chase after fame and gain,
compete in superficial luxuries,
indulge in passions and desires,
and mistake falsehood for truth?

The poor suffer in distress,
yet cannot uphold the Great Way,
nor recite the true *Scriptures*.
The rich indulge in extravagance,
yet cannot abandon worldly wisdom and profit
to follow the teachings of the Law,
willing to age and die in their folly,
losing the wealth they were born with.

Laozi said: *"Gold and jade fill the hall,
yet none can guard them;
wealth and rank bring arrogance,
and one invites ruin upon oneself."*
This warns against pursuing externals while neglecting the inner self.

Now it is said that reciting the *Scripture* can bring wealth—
to urge people to abandon their superficial pursuit of riches
and instead honor the *Scripture*.
Ah, truly, reciting the *Scripture* has its effect.
If one lacks sincerity and reverence,
one may only invite transgression.
Let those who observe the *Scripture* be cautious.

**Chapter 27 of *The Merits and Virtues* (continued):**
If one is afflicted by malevolent stars,
suffering hardship in life and death,
and yet recites this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then these malevolent stars shall retreat,
bringing forth auspicious fortune instead.

The benefits of this *Scripture* extend far beyond mere wealth—
if one’s life or fate is troubled by malevolent stars,
if one lies in bed with restless sleep,
and yet recites this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
then these malevolent stars shall transform their ill fortune into good,
and retreat, bringing forth auspicious fortune.

The Master **Chisongzi** said: *"The people are orphaned and destitute,
each bearing a star upon their brow."*
Yet the stars that shine upon them bring either fortune or calamity—
fortune brings a thousand blessings,
while calamity portends ill omens and punishments.
Those beneath the Three Luminaries must always avoid such ill influences.
Malevolent stars are the stars of calamity—
such as **Luohe** (羅睺), **Jidu** (計都), **Tianpo** (天破), **Tianku** (天哭), **Tianbai** (天敗), and **Tianrui** (天退), among others.

**Photo** (照) refers to when stars align with one’s destiny,
fate, or home—whether at birth, during one’s lifespan,
or in the celestial divisions of one’s abode.
**Kun** (困) means one’s desires are not fulfilled,
pressed down and unable to flourish.
**Ku** (苦) refers to poverty, illness, or danger
that directly afflicts the body.
**Kun and ku in bed and pillow** simply mean
one is trapped in misfortune,
unable to rest or sleep in peace,
lying in bed with no comfort.

Another saying: *"Bed and pillow are disturbed by fear."*
These malevolent stars encompass many—
all celestial omens of calamity that align with one’s destiny,
fate, or home, and all stars of ill fortune.

**Returning and descending auspicious fortune** means
that when malevolent stars shine upon one,
misfortune prevails and no blessings follow.
Yet if one recites this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
the sacred verses shall take effect,
the ill omens shall become auspicious,
and all malevolent stars that afflict one
shall not only fail to bring misfortune,
but shall instead withdraw in silence,
bestowing blessings and fortune,
and descending auspicious fortune.

The influence of stars upon destiny and fate
is inherently fixed.
How then can reciting the *Scripture* cause malevolent stars to bring auspicious fortune?

Heaven and humanity share the same principle—
above and below are interconnected,
and the mechanism of response is swift as light and shadow.
King **Shuanggong of Song** had three sayings of a ruler,
one of which was: *"Retreat when the star **Yinghuo** (荧惑) appears."*

It is not only rulers who can move Heaven—
a filial wife, bearing grief, could bring three years of drought;
a lowly servant, pleading sincerely, could summon frost in the sixth month.
Even common folk, man or woman,
can sway Heaven and Earth,
and stir the spirits and deities—
only fearing their sincerity may not be complete.

If one’s sincerity reaches Heaven,
even a single word can win the trust of the divine.
One need not speak to influence the transformations of fate—
how much more so when the *Scripture* is the essence of Heaven and Earth,
the source from which the Three Luminaries draw their light?

If one recites this *Scripture* in accordance with its precepts,
honoring the sacred verses of the Most Holy,
and fully embracing the profound mysteries of the enlightened,
then malevolent stars shall disperse,
auspicious fortune shall arise,
and ill fate shall turn to blessing.

Humans are all the same—
those who follow the path of virtue shall meet fortune,
those who oppose it shall meet calamity.
*The *Central Admonition Scripture* (中诫经)* says:
*"When stars shine upon a person,
fortune or calamity is self-summoned—
doing great good, the star’s light shall be manifest;
doing no good nor evil, its light shall be faint;
committing minor faults, its light shall scatter;
committing great faults, its light shall vanish.
If malevolent stars afflict one,
it is because of one’s faults—
then ill fate shall respond.
If one is faultless,
the omens shall be averted.
Goodness shall drive away calamity,
and blessings shall descend."*

The *Scripture* says: *"A single thought of evil
summons malevolent stars and vengeful spirits;
a single thought of good
summons auspicious stars and joyous clouds."*
The signs of blessing or ruin
depend upon the purity of one’s thoughts.

Even in times of great peril and disaster,
if one truly upholds this *Scripture*,
the calamities shall retreat—
and yet, are there not some afflictions,
like restless sleep and sudden misfortunes,
that may not be entirely dispelled?

King **Tai Jia** said: *"Heaven creates calamities,
yet they can still be defied."*
This is the same meaning.

If one can propagate the Dao,
praise the nurturing of all things,
and silently turn the true *Scripture*,
entering its divine mysteries to reach cosmic transformation,
then one shall align with Heaven and Earth in virtue,
with the sun and moon in radiance,
with the four seasons in order,
and with the spirits and deities in fortune and calamity.
One shall guide the transformations of fate,
forever transcend the mundane,
and even the spirits and deities shall not dare to obstruct—
life and death shall have no dominion,
and stars shall not be able to confine or limit one.

Let those who observe this *Scripture* strive earnestly.

**Chapter 28 of *The Merits and Virtues* (continued):**
If one’s fate is marked by transgressions,
and they should fall into the hells,
their names recorded in the evil ledgers,
then let their parents, teachers, and elders,
their spouses and children,
recite this *Scripture* for them,
or establish a Daoist hall for their repose,
offering banners, flowers, and provisions.
Thus shall the departed’s evil record be erased,
their spirit reborn in a pure land,
and all suffering beings be liberated together,
receiving this triumphant blessing—
all shall ascend to Heaven above.»

The merits and virtues of this *Scripture* do not merely avert sins in life—
if one’s fate is marked by transgressions and they die prematurely,
their soul and spirit shall descend into the hells,
their names recorded in the ledgers of evil deeds.
Then let their parents, teachers, and elders,
their spouses and children,
recite this *Scripture* for the departed,
or establish a *Dao* hall for their liberation,
offering banners, flowers, and provisions.
Thus shall the departed’s evil records be erased,
their spirit reborn in a pure land,
and all who suffer in the same hells, the same deaths,
the same ledgers of sin—
all shall rely on the *Scripture*’s virtue,
receiving deliverance and salvation,
and attain this supreme and wondrous *Law*’s blessings,
ascending to Heaven above.

*"Command over"* (*命过*)—this means dying before one’s allotted lifespan.
*"Descend into the hells"* (*应入地狱*)—whether from sins committed in past lives or this one,
one must enter the hells and suffer retribution.
The hells include *Yingdu* (酆都), *Iron Enclosure* (铁围), the *Nine Hells*, the *Eighteen Hells*,
the *Twenty-Four Hells*, the *Thirty-Six Hells*, the *Seventy-Two Hells*,
and the *Hell of No Return* (无间), among others.

*"Recorded in the ledgers of evil"* (*注名恶籍*)—their names are inscribed
in the black registers of misdeeds for retribution.
*"Parents, teachers, and elders"* (*父母师长*)—these are the departed’s parents,
their masters, or their senior kin.
*"Spouses and children"* (*夫妻男女*)—whether the departed was a woman or a man,
they must have had a husband or wife;
if not, then their sons, daughters, or other male and female relatives remain.
*"Recite this Scripture for the departed"* (*当为亡人持念是经*)—this is for the living kin
to uphold and chant this *Scripture* on their behalf.
*"Establish a Dao hall"* (*或安置道场*)—to arrange and consecrate a *Dao* hall,
following the *Dao*’s methods to eliminate karmic sins—hence, a *Dao* hall.
*"Banners and floral offerings"* (*旛花供养*)—the *banner* (*旛*) proclaims the sacred names endlessly,
inscribed on long scrolls, hoisted on tall poles to sway the four directions,
spreading radiant light. *Flowers* (*花*) are presented—all rare blooms—to welcome the sacred spirits.
In Heaven, natural banners and flags unfurl, celestial flowers bloom in splendor,
displaying auspicious light. In the mortal world, banners are placed in the *Dao* hall
to signify solemnity and invite divine aid.
*"Provisions"* (*供养*)—*supply* (*供*) means to offer reverently;
*nourish* (*养*) means to provide food and drink in veneration.
Heavenly beings feast on pure and wondrous *Law*—the celestial kitchen’s refined offerings,
solemn and respectful. The world’s five or ten offerings
merely eliminate the five aggregates, remove five sufferings,
restrain five pleasures, abandon ten evils,
contemplate ten truths, and dwell in ten virtues—
to honor the luminous spirits,
revere the true *Law*,
and uphold sacred texts—this is true veneration.
Yet today, offering only food, flowers, fruits, and rare delicacies
without genuine reverence is but superficial.
The *Scripture*’s true offerings are those of sincere, natural devotion.

Thus shall the departed’s evil records be erased,
their spirit reborn in a pure land.
A single turning of this *Scripture*,
or the establishment of a *Dao* hall,
shall free the departed from the netherworld,
erase their black karmic deeds,
and remove their names from the ledgers of sin—
their spirit reborn in a land of purity and bliss.
All who suffer in the same hells shall be liberated,
relying on the *Scripture*’s compassionate salvation.
All shall ascend to Heaven above through this supreme blessing.

*"Command over"* (*命过*)—though Heaven’s blessings may be finite,
a single recitation of this true *Scripture*,
or the establishment of a *Dao* hall,
shall erase the departed’s sins and those of all suffering spirits in the hells,
granting them birth in Heaven.
If practiced eternally, what limit shall its merits have?

Alas! The hells have no gates—only one invites themself.
The Celestial Realm has paths—yet the ignorant struggle to walk them.
How much more so for those born with innate purity,
the *Scripture of the Imperial True One*—
if they perpetually uphold and recite it,
the hells and heavens shall never stain them,
eternally attaining the Mysterious True.

Thus it is said of those who well uphold this *Scripture*.

**Chapter 29 of *The Merits and Virtues* (continued):**
Wherever this *Scripture* resides,
the *Ten Heavenly Supreme True Saints* and the *Limitless Flying Heavenly Kings*
shall attend in reverence, offering protection.
Those who uphold this *Scripture* may rightly call themselves *Zhengyi True Persons*.
Wherever such a person dwells,
the *Ten Directions’ Supreme True Saints* and *Golden-Armed Vajra Warriors*
shall secretly guard them as their own body.
Whether in travel or repose,
all malevolent forces shall flee their path,
demons shall be exterminated,
spirits shall hide in submission,
and no calamity shall dare approach them.

When such a person’s life nears its end,
they shall not see the horrors of the hells—
instead, they shall behold Heavenly Maidens of Jade bearing flags to welcome them,
and ascend to Heaven above.

If their Heavenly blessings are exhausted and they return to the mortal realm,
they shall, across countless lifetimes,
always be reborn as kings, ministers,
sage rulers, and virtuous officials,
gathering in assemblies of the enlightened—
their lands peaceful, their people at ease in righteousness,
their innate nature ever luminous.
By following the Great *Dao*,
they shall progressively cultivate,
ultimately attaining the Dao’s shore.

Such are the blessings bestowed upon those who uphold this *Scripture*.
The *Scripture*’s merits do not merely benefit life and death—
wherever this *Scripture* resides,
the *Ten Heavenly Supreme True Saints* and the *Limitless Flying Heavenly Kings*
shall attend in reverence, offering protection.
Those who uphold this *Scripture* may rightly call themselves *Zhengyi True Persons*.
Wherever such a person dwells,
the *Ten Directions’ Supreme True Saints* and *Golden-Armed Vajra Warriors*
shall secretly guard them as their own body.
Whether in travel or repose,
all malevolent forces shall flee their path,
demons shall be exterminated,
spirits shall hide in submission,
and no calamity shall dare approach them.

When such a person’s life nears its end,
they shall not see the horrors of the hells—
instead, they shall behold Heavenly Officials and Jade Maidens bearing flags and banners to welcome them,
and ascend to Heaven above.

If their Heavenly blessings are exhausted and they return to the mortal realm,
they shall, across countless lifetimes,
always be reborn as kings, ministers,
sage rulers, and virtuous officials,
gathering in assemblies of the enlightened—
their lands peaceful, their people at ease in righteousness,
their innate nature ever luminous.
By following the Great *Dao*,
they shall progressively cultivate,
ultimately attaining the Dao’s shore.

Such is the fortune bestowed upon the *sutra*-holder.

The Ten Heavens, the Ten Directions, and all the Celestial Kings—
the Flying Celestial Kings, who are the Celestial Kings that traverse the skies in flight and guard the heavens.
They stand in attendance, bowing to shield them.

The *Zhengyi* True Person, one who is upright and unselfish, true and undivided.
The *Jin Gang* Powerful Ones, the guardians of both teachings—
all come to protect the *sutra*-holder.

In secret, they guard them,
protecting them unseen,
as though safeguarding their own luminous essence—
one can perceive the fervor of the gods’ protection.

Wherever such a person goes—
whether they emerge or retreat—
all malevolent demons, spirits, and *qi*-bound entities
flee, hide, or submit in fear.
They are utterly exterminated and removed.

*Exterminated*—meaning cut off, utterly spent.
Calamities and misfortunes cannot draw near.

When this person’s life draws to its end,
they shall not behold the myriad horrors of the hells.

The Heavenly Palace Maidens—
a variant reading mistakenly says *Heavenly Officials*—
are not the same.
The *zhang* (great banner of the *Dao*), not a *fan* (military flag) nor a *jing* (ceremonial standard),
is the banner of the Great *Dao*.
They descend to escort and guide them upward to Heaven.

Across countless lifetimes,
they shall be reborn as kings and ministers,
always held in honor,
like the Buddha’s eight thousand descendants as royal princes,
or the *Xuandi* Emperor ruling for a thousand lifetimes,
or a thousand lifetimes as a prime minister,
or the *Laojun* (Venerable Master) throughout the kalpas as the sovereign teacher of emperors and kings.

Together, they ensure enduring peace and joy,
while their innate luminous nature remains unobscured—
great wisdom and great insight,
never dimmed by the virtuous causes of past kalpas.

They uphold and revere the Great *Dao*,
repeatedly cultivating and refining,
progressively practicing and attaining,
until they reach the *Dao*’s shore.

The *Dao*’s shore—meaning attainment of the *Dao*,
as crossing to the opposite shore of the sea.
The Buddha spoke of "reaching the other shore."
The *Great Odes* say: *"They first ascend to the shore."*
This is what is meant.

One variant says: *the shore of return*.

The merit of reciting the *sutra* brings benefit at every moment—
whether aiding the living or the dead,
whether few or many,
whether near or distant,
all wishes fulfilled,
truly manifesting the power of transformation.

Or over countless lifetimes,
unwavering in devotion,
repeatedly cultivating and refining,
only then ascending to the *Dao*’s shore.

Thus, the attainment of great perfection is truly arduous.
Those who observe the *sutra* with resolute intent
may enter the highest echelon.

**Chapter 30: The Merits of the *Sutra***

If one recites this *sutra* when rain falls,
arousing great compassion,
and as prescribed, recites the three volumes of this *sutra* toward the void,
all beings touched by the rain,
in the direction of their faces,
whether committing the five heinous offenses, ten evils,
or any grave sins—
all are utterly eradicated.
All severe illnesses are spontaneously cured.

Upon their death,
these beings shall not fall into hell,
but be reborn in pure lands,
emerging from lotus flowers.
How much more so for those who recite this *sutra* themselves!

If one recites this *sutra* while traveling,
and a great wind arises, blowing against the reciter,
the dust touching their body—
wherever that dust settles,
all beings’ evil deeds are utterly destroyed,
and they shall not fall into the three evil paths,
instead being reborn in heaven.

Thus, the merit of reciting the *sutra* is unfathomable.
Its virtue extends beyond benefiting oneself alone.

If one recites this *sutra* when rain falls,
arousing great compassion to save the world,
and as prescribed, recites the upper, middle, and lower volumes of this *sutra* completely,
all beings touched by the rain,
in the direction of their faces—
whether committing the five heinous offenses, ten evils,
or any grave sins—
all are utterly dispersed and annihilated.
All severe illnesses are spontaneously cured and healed.

These beings in the direction of the reciter’s face,
upon death,
shall not fall into hell,
but be reborn in pure lands,
untainted by defilement,
emerging from lotus flowers.
How then can the merit of those who recite this *sutra* be measured?

If one recites this *sutra* while traveling,
and a great wind arises, blowing against the reciter,
the dust touching their body—
wherever that dust settles,
all beings’ evil deeds are utterly destroyed,
and they shall not fall into the three evil paths,
instead being reborn in heaven.

Thus, the merit of reciting the *sutra* is unfathomable.

**Explication of Doubts:**
The reciter’s compassion knows no bounds—
not only when rain falls or wind rises,
but with great compassion at all times.
This speaks to the efficacy of reciting the *sutra*.
Great compassion and pity extend to all beings in the world.

The *Release Teachings* say: *"A mother’s heart is too tender."*
The *Odes* say: *"Alas, this one alone is honored."*
It also says: *"Pity cannot perfect a person."*
The *Dao* scriptures say: *"Great compassion awakens the world."*
The reciter pities the suffering of worldly beings,
thus arousing great compassion.

The five heinous offenses:
disloyalty, unfilial piety, lack of kindness, discord, and injustice.
Or: disrespect for heaven, earth, sovereign, parents, and teachers;
disrespect for the Three Jewels;
failure to uphold precepts;
lack of moral cultivation;
and ignorance of true nature.

The ten evils:
killing, stealing, sexual misconduct, deceit,
slanderous speech, false speech, flattery,
harsh words, greed, anger, and delusion.

All severe illnesses are cured.
*Syuan* (痊): restored to ease.
*Yu* (愈): fully healed.

Lotus-born rebirth:
In the Buddhist tradition, the Western Pure Land’s beings emerge from lotus flowers.
In the *Dao* tradition, the *Qinghua Changle* realm’s beings are lotus-born.
It is also said: *"Desire arises from the lotus."*
Meaning that in both worldly and transcendent existence,
they remain unstained by dust,
with wondrous *dharma* perpetually arising,
free from defiled thoughts.
As at the dawn of heaven and earth,
naturally giving rise to humanity.

Confucian scholars often dismiss the two teachings as false.
Yet Yi Yin was born from a lotus—
was he not a sage of Confucian virtue?

Moreover, the human heart

The virtuous *power* of those who uphold the *Sutra* extends not only to humanity.
If the *Sutra* traverses rivers, lakes, the Huai, and the seas,
and washes over their bodies,
then all beings in that water—
fish, tortoises, *qīnghua* (鼋), *tuó* (鼉), and every aquatic creature—
shall have their past karmic transgressions utterly extinguished,
and shall exhaust their present lifetime’s retribution.
After death, they attain the wondrous fruit of rebirth,
no longer receiving bodies of birth—
whether from egg, womb, moisture, or transformation—
in all forms.

Those who uphold the *Sutra*,
when speaking all words and sounds,
even the most perverse *demons* and *external paths*,
hearers mistake them not for mundane speech or breath,
but as the pure and sacred tones of *dharma*.

Should they encounter divine shrines,
they can recite this *Sutra* to the deities,
and when the spirits and gods hear this *Sutra*,
they break free from the *karmic realm of ghosts*,
ascend to the *Way of the Immortal*,
and revere such upholders
as they would the sovereign Emperor himself.

**The *Sutra* traverses:**
The *Sutra* is the passage through;
*traverse* means to cross.
Some say: "To cross water bare-bodied is called *traverse*—*
like the Master Lü’s chanting flight over Dongting Lake,
or Bodhidharma’s lotus-stalk crossing of the river.
In essence, all crossing of water—
whether bare-bodied, by boat, or otherwise—
is called *Sutra traverse*.
Rivers, lakes, and seas are all general names for flowing water.
The Huai is the Huai River.
*To wash and bathe their bodies* means to cleanse with water.
*All beings within water* refers to every living thing in it—
scaled like fish, shelled like tortoises, *qīnghua* (鼋), *tuó* (鼉), and all aquatic life.
Their karmic transgressions are all extinguished,
and they exhaust their retribution in this very lifetime.
After death, they no longer cycle through animal rebirths—
whether feathered, furred, scaled, shelled, or insect-like—
nor receive bodies from egg, womb, moisture, or transformation.
Though humans are born from the womb,
the term *womb* here does not refer to humans alone,
but to all latent forms.

For dragons are the sovereign among aquatic beings,
yet they still speak of karmic retribution;
how much more so for the lower aquatic creatures!

True upholders of the *Sutra* emit golden radiance from their bodies and mouths,
so wherever their voice reaches,
all perverse *demons* and *external paths* who hear it
believe it to be the pure and sacred tones of *dharma*.

To recite the *Sutra* for the deities
is to liberate them from their ghostly *karmic realms*.
Though deities are subtle and radiant,
displaying their might and manifesting retribution,
they still possess *karmic inclinations*.
Hearing this true *Sutra*,
they sever their *cognitive roots*,
uproot their *karmic tendencies*,
and dissolve all past habits.

To ascend to the *Way of the Immortal*
is to attain the highest path of true transcendence.
The distinction between gods and immortals lies in their ranks.
Even great gods, though possessing virtue,
still retain visible deeds and traces,
like eminent sages who have not yet dissolved their forms,
or those who have entered sainthood but remain unequal.

Immortals, however, transcend the Five Aggregates,
purify the Nine Consciousnesses,
dispel subject and object,
and harmonize phenomena and principles.
Though divided into Five Grades,
they far surpass the gods and ghosts.

When the Sage arises,
all things flourish,
mountains do not overflow,
rivers do not run dry,
birds and beasts, fish and tortoises,
all thrive in accord.
The lawful waters of the *Sutra*’s upholders,
which touch the aquatic beings,
are no less than the transformative *power* of a sage-emperor.
Dragons, enlightened by the law,
equally touched by the *Sutra*’s waters—
who could fail to transcend?

This is how the *wild fox* attained the law
and regained its human form.

If one recites the *Sutra* to deliver gods and ghosts
from their *karmic realms*—
like the Master Sa’s deliverance of King Lingguan,
or the Venerable Puxian’s instruction of Guan the Great Sage—
they will revere the divine might,
forgetting all past afflictions.
Thus, even to this day,
the reverence for these two sages does not wane.

**Continuation of the Virtuous *Power* of the *Sutra* (Thirty-Second Chapter):**

If a person in this world
does not honor their parents,
does not revere the Three Treasures,
and commits grave offenses—
slaying life, theft, licentiousness, falsehood,
and all manner of most heinous crimes—
when their life is about to end,
if a virtuous *Dao*-hearted man or woman,
with pure faith and great compassion,
