recites the august name of the Jade Emperor
seven times, or fourteen, twenty-one, twenty-eight,
up to a hundred or thousand repetitions
at the dying person’s head before their *qi* is severed,
all the unwholesome deeds they committed in life
are utterly extinguished,
and they will not fall into any evil *karmic realm*.
Their spirit ascends to the Nine Heavens—
how much more so for those who receive and uphold this *Sutra*?

Or if there be one
who, from past *kalpas* down to this very body,
has cycled through human and heavenly realms,
drifted in the world’s domains,
and accumulated countless faults and myriad offenses
within their own being—
should they encounter those who uphold this *Sutra*,
even if their shadow briefly touches the upholder’s body,
or if they are caught within the sovereign Emperor’s radiant light,
or share a word, or hear the voice,
as though receiving the Emperor’s lawful speech
to soothe and guide them,
their karmic obstacles are permanently erased.

The *Sutra*’s virtuous *power*
does not merely extend downward to beings,
but upward to gods and ghosts as well.

If a person in this world
does not revere the Three Treasures,
and commits grave offenses—
slaying life, theft, licentiousness, falsehood,
and all manner of most heinous crimes—
when their life is about to end,
if a virtuous *Dao*-hearted man or woman,
with pure faith and great compassion,
recites the august name of the Jade Emperor
once seven, twice three-four times seven,
up to hundreds or thousands of repetitions
at the dying person’s head before their *qi* is severed,
all the unwholesome deeds they committed in life
are utterly extinguished,
and they will not fall into any evil *karmic realm*.
Their spirit ascends to the Nine *Qi* Heavens—
how much more so for those who receive and uphold this *Sutra*?

Or if there be one
who, from past *kalpas* down to this very body,
has cycled through human and heavenly realms,
drifted in the world’s domains,
and accumulated myriad faults and countless offenses
within their own being—
should they encounter those who uphold this *Sutra*,
even if their shadow briefly touches the upholder’s body,
or if they are caught within the sovereign Emperor’s *Dao*-radiance,
or share a word, or hear the voice,
as though receiving the Emperor’s lawful speech
to soothe and guide them,
their karmic obstacles are permanently erased.

**The Three Treasures:**
The *Way*, the *Sutra*, and the Master.
The *Way* is the root of the Three Teachings,
the progenitor of all existence;
the *Sutra* is the ferry and sustenance for crossing the world.

The Master is the eye of humankind and the heavens—
to disrespect thus incurs one offense.

Slaying, stealing, licentious lust, and false speech—
great transgressions bring great guilt,
and even a fleeting thought carries sin.
Countless offenses—
not all can be enumerated in words.

**Right Faith** is the utmost sincerity,
untainted by ulterior motives.

Reciting **one, seven, twenty-three, forty-seven, or a thousand hundred times**—
or as it is said, *"completing the Dao’s celestial circuit of transformation"*—
this too is valid.

They do not fall into the evil realms,
for they bear good roots and harbor no wicked thoughts—
thus they do not descend into evil.

They cycle through human and heavenly realms,
or enjoy the blessings of mortal or celestial life.
Some say: *"Human blessings are the blessings of both human and heaven."*

They drift in the world’s domains,
subject to the impermanence of birth and death,
like floating reeds on water,
entangled in karmic bonds they cannot escape,
as though submerged in deep waters.

**Worldly domains**—the boundaries of the mortal realm.

**A fleeting shadow’s touch**—
the form and shadow of the *Sutra*-holder
briefly illuminate the sinful one’s body,
as though ensnared by the Emperor’s radiant light.
*"Receive"* or *"authored"*—
it is the Emperor’s light that bestows,
not the Emperor Himself.
When the light descends upon a person,
they stand in solemn reverence, unburdened by thought—
thus it is said to *"ensnare and receive."*
I receive the lawful benefits of that light.

**Shared speech or heard voice**—
the sinful one may converse with the *Sutra*-holder
or hear their voice.
*"Dao-speech"*—the profound utterances of the Great Dao.
Or as some say: *"The speech of the Dao Ancestor"*—
too restrictive a claim.

**Comfort and instruction**—
*"Comfort"* is the soothing of kind words;
*"instruction"* is teaching and command.

**Karmic obstacles erased**—
all past and present sins are released,
all past and present impediments removed.

The *Sutra’s* divine power
benefits both the living and the departed,
its blessings extend to all—
only those of **right faith** attain such merit.
Thus, **utter sincerity** must be the foundation.

**Benefiting the departed**—
if one’s blessings extend to others,
how then can the merit of those who uphold this *Sutra*
be measured?
Let the observer take heed.

**Continuation of the Merits Chapter (Thirty-Three)**
If one who upholds this *Sutra* crafts a long banner,
inscribing the Emperor’s sacred name upon it,
and hangs it upon a tall pole—
whether in the temple hall or within the household—
wherever the winds direct that banner,
all beings in that direction
shall partake in supreme blessings,
and all evil deeds shall be utterly eradicated.

If one who upholds this *Sutra* inscribes the Emperor’s sacred name
upon all resonant objects—
whether bells, chimes, gongs, drums,
or any Daoist ritual implements—
whether struck in ceremony, played in practice,
or set in motion by the wind,
when their sound emanates—
near or far—
all beings who hear it
shall have their karmic obstacles purified.

This further expounds the merits of upholding the *Sutra*.

**Long banner inscribed with the Emperor’s name, tall pole**—
as previously explained.

**Temple hall**—the halls before the temple’s main sanctuary.
**Temple**—a place of solemn contemplation,
where the numinous resides without ulterior intent,
thus called *"Temple"* (*guàn*).

**Household courtyard**—before one’s home.

**The direction indicated**—
the aspect toward which the wind-blown banner points.

**Supreme blessings**—as previously defined.

**Bells, chimes, gongs, drums, and *tá*—**
all are ritual instruments of metal.

**All Daoist implements and ritual objects**—
including those of gold, stone, silk, bamboo, gourd, clay, leather, and wood,
and all resonant objects,
or any implements used in Daoist rites.

**Ritual grounds**—
when the sacred name is struck upon ritual instruments,
it is permissible.

**How can playful striking also bear merit?**
This *"play"* is not reckless revelry or frivolous jest—
it may be the practice of ritual music,
or the unintentional striking by the young or the ignorant,
or the casual ringing of resonant objects in leisure.
**Inscribed sacred name**—
not the Emperor’s personal name,
but the **Eternal Name**, unchanging across *kalpas*,
the abiding Great Name—
thus called *"sacred name."*

**Wind-struck sound**—
when the wind causes resonant objects to chime.

**Near and far, all beings who hear the sound**—
their karmic obstacles are utterly purified.
Without distinction of distance,
all who hear the sacred name’s resonance
shall have their sins dissolved and be cleansed.

**Investigation:**
Ancient music was crafted to harmonize the divine and human,
to unite heaven and earth.
How much more so when the sacred name—
the honored title of the Primordial—
is heard, inspiring awe?
When the lawful sound resounds,
its divine efficacy is boundless.

**Emperor Shun’s music** made even beasts dance in rhythm—
how much more so for humans?
Hearing martial instruments inspires awe,
hearing playful toys brings delight,
hearing the *qin* brings harmony—
how much more so the sacred sound?

All resonant playthings are irrelevant.
Ritual instruments and musical tools
are used to honor the numinous and unify the will of the assembly.
Moreover, since the sacred name is inscribed,
those who hear it in reverence shall have their sins erased.

For **karmic obstacles** are the retribution for evil deeds.
When the lawful sound is heard,
goodwill arises spontaneously—
thus all karmic obstacles are annihilated,
and purity is attained.

Even now, a single thunderclap
fills listeners with reverence and fear—
this suffices as proof.

**Clarifying Doubts:**
In this age, many hang banners
and inscribe the sacred name upon ritual instruments and resonant objects,
yet those who see or hear them
do not have their karmic obstacles removed—
why is this?

Those who inscribe lack **true, sincere faith** in upholding the *Sutra*,
and those who hear or see it treat it as mere custom,
their stubborn hearts unrepentant,
even to the point of contempt, frivolity, or blasphemy—
without genuine devotion,
how can sins be absolved?

Alas! The *Sutra’s* sacred name—
its merits are immeasurable.
The ancient sages first upheld the *Sutra* to transcend themselves—
without movement, they inspire reverence;
without speech, they command faith.
Then, with the sacred name, they bless others—
thus their own blessings endure eternally.

**Continuation of the Merits Chapter (Thirty-Four)**
If one who upholds this *Sutra* attains enlightenment on birth and death,
retreats into deep mountains and forests to cultivate the True Way,
and at times ascends to overlook the peaks,
wherever their gaze extends—
across mountains, forests, streams, and valleys,
all living beings—
visible and invisible,
conceived in womb, egg, moisture, or transformation,
creeping, flying, swimming, or dormant—
all classes of existence,
their sins and karmic bonds shall be eradicated,
their bodies and minds purified,
and upon death, they shall be reborn in heaven.

How much more so for those who uphold this *Sutra*?
Know that such a person is already the embodiment of the Dao藏’s virtue/power.

Here, it further expounds upon the efficacy of upholding the *Sutra*—
**Enlightenment on birth and death.**
Birth and death are profound matters, their essence most difficult to fathom.
Dependent upon the vital essence and blood of parents,
receiving the *li* and *qi* of Heaven and Earth,
life—this is how one comes to be, yet its origin is unfathomable.
When the essence is exhausted and the *qi* dissipates,
when the spirit departs and the form withers—
death—this is how one ceases to be, yet its end is unfathomable.
Not knowing life, not knowing death,
though one may grasp the changes of affairs,
observe the principles of things,
and speak with clarity while acting without delusion—
this is not yet enlightenment.

If one who upholds the *Sutra* abandons the sacred and forsakes wisdom,
eliminates the two obstructions,
severs all delusions,
fuses innate nature,
attains great awakening,
realizes the Three Primordials,
ascends to the highest state,
and penetrates the root of birth and death—
this is what the Buddhist school calls *perfect enlightenment*.

**Retreating into deep mountains and forests.**
The ancients said: *"The small hidden one resides in the mountains."*
Since one has attained enlightenment,
whether high mountain or level plain—
all are Dao-fields.
Why must cultivation necessarily be in mountains and forests?
The great hidden one resides in the marketplace—
this is also true in principle.
Famous peaks and scenic wonders,
where the land’s *ling* is potent and sages abound—
true cultivators,
though they have no inclination for mountains and forests,
find that secluded peaks and lush groves
are naturally formed as immortal realms.
Thus, the recluse enters them.

**Cultivating the True Way and learning the Dao.**
Human nature’s original purity is utterly true, without falsity.
The Way of nature is spontaneous, needing no study or inquiry.
Yet as desires grow daily,
one is seduced by external transformations,
and the true gradually becomes false,
the Way of nature obscured.
Those who attain enlightenment,
in mountain or forest glades,
silently refine their cultivation,
restoring the Heavenly True,
partaking in the Great Dao,
and transcending birth and death.
*The Dao De Jing* says: *"Cease learning, and you will have no worries."*
Yet here it says *"learning the Dao"*—why?
There, *"cease learning"* refers to abandoning the names, forms, and thoughts of learning.
Here, *"learning the Dao"* means learning the boundless, effortless Way.
The Buddhist school holds enlightenment as supreme.
Yet here, enlightenment is but the beginning—
only then does one enter the mountains to cultivate the True Way and learn the Dao.
Thus, the ranks of these two paths are clear.

At times, those who learn the Dao ascend heights, overlook waters,
travel through wondrous landscapes,
and from mountain peaks survey all four directions.
Wherever their gaze extends—
whether mountains, forests, streams, or valleys—
*valleys*, the hollows and deep chasms of mountains—
all living beings, both manifest and latent,
those already born and those yet unborn,
including those born unseen—
whether womb-born, egg-born,
or generated from moisture and filth,
or spontaneously arising from nothingness,
all creeping, flying, swimming, or dormant—
the myriad classes of created life,
their past and present sins and karmic bonds,
all are eradicated.
Their bodies and minds are purified,
free from all entanglements,
and at death, they are reborn in Heaven.

The merits of a True Cultivator’s gaze extending to all things are thus—
how much more so for those who uphold this *Sutra*?
Know that such a one’s virtue/power is boundless,
the very essence of the Dao’s profound藏,
incalculable,
a body of supreme virtue/power.

The cultivator’s heart is vast in compassion and love,
never without benevolence.
Though unseen by sight or hearing,
their gaze encompasses all things,
and in silent reverence, they extend their spirit to rescue all sentient beings,
delivering them from the world.
Thus, they save all beings.

As the Confucian classics say:
*"Achieving harmony, all things are nurtured."*
*"Establishing the Spirit Platform, they observe the encroaching mists,
discerning calamities and omens,
and through subtle means, complete and assist all things."*
What Heaven and Earth cannot reach,
they enable humanity and spirits to receive their natural fate,
returning to the source of transformation—
what sins or karmic bonds could remain?

Those who praise Confucius say:
*"In a single lifetime, one cannot exhaust his learning;
across generations, one cannot fully grasp his depth."*
The ineffable is called divine.
Now, praising those who cultivate the True Way and learn the Dao,
we say: *"the embodiment of the Dao藏’s virtue/power."*
This speaks to its boundless embrace,
its unfathomable depth—
praise that cannot be exhausted.
Those who study the *Sutra* will understand this meaning.

**Continuation of the Merits Chapter (Thirty-Five)**
At that time, the Celestial Sovereign addressed the Jade Emptiness Emperor:
*"Now I have spoken briefly, yet the mysteries remain unfathomed.
If I were to expound fully,
those with errant views, doubts, and disbelief
would never exhaust the *Sutra*’s merits across kalpas."*

At that time—
*(as previously explained)*
The Celestial Sovereign refers to the Primordial Sovereign of the Beginning.
*"To speak"* means to address the Jade Emptiness Emperor of the Supreme Brightness.
*(Alternatively, the Jade Purity Emperor of the Void.)*
*"Now I"* refers to the Primordial Sovereign speaking at this moment.
*"Briefly"* means to outline the essentials.
*"Unfathomed"* means the Dao’s supreme mysteries and highest merits remain unexhausted.

If one were to expound fully upon this *Sutra*,
its merits—merits of reciting and upholding the *Sutra*,
benefiting sentient beings and all things,
benefiting existence and non-existence,
benefiting the formed and the formless,
benefiting self and others,
benefiting heaven and earth—
are already vast indeed.

Yet even so, if one were to expound fully,
those with errant views and disbelief
would still remain unconvinced.

What is spoken of here encompasses:
all beings in one world, past and present,
the existence and destruction of heaven and earth,
as well as the three thousand great thousand worlds,
from kalpa to kalpa, countless kalpas,
one future age, all future ages,
from the beginning without beginning,
to the end without end,
whether knowing or unaware,
whether perceiving or not perceiving,
whether conceptualizable or inconceivable,
whether finite or infinite—
all merits, both within this *Sutra* and for those who uphold it,
if widely proclaimed and expounded in their profundity,
would still leave the common folk—
the vulgar and the ordinary—
with errant views, doubts, and disbelief.

*"Vulgar"* refers to the common people of the world;
*"flow"* refers to those of ordinary inclinations.

Like water flowing, it cannot extract the finest grains.
*"Evil views"* are partial and crooked, not upright and vast.
*"Doubt"* arises when wisdom does not prevail—ambiguous, undecided.
*"Delusion"* stirs from private thoughts, tangled and confused, unable to discern right from wrong, a chaotic jumble of misguided perception—thus they disbelieve this *Sutra* holds boundless benefits.

The *Sutra*’s virtues exhaust even kalpas in speech,
countless kalpas beyond reckoning—still, they cannot be fully spoken.
Some say: "Exhausting the kalpas in recounting leaves speech still incomplete."
Fundamentally, the Primordial Origin endures eternally,
kalpas are endless, the *Sutra*’s virtues unfathomable,
the Great Dao immeasurable—
yet speech can never exhaust it.

The Great Dao is beyond words,
the Marvelous Law beyond form,
the True Scripture beyond letters—
what can be applied and received,
seen and heard,
spoken and attained,
are all but second meanings.

Thus, the Most High Sage manifested across countless kalpas,
preached to twelve thousand heavens,
traveled distant realms,
composed countless *Sutras*,
one manifestation lasting seventeen hundred years,
expounding the *Sutra* over ninety thousand times—
yet still declared, *"I do not know its name,"*
and by force named it *Dao*.

Confucius, inheriting the past and opening the future,
enlightening the ages to come, said, *"I know nothing."*
The Śākyamuni Buddha spoke for forty-nine years,
expounding the *Sutra* in over three hundred assemblies,
composing the Three Baskets of *Sūtras*, *Vinaya*, and *Abhidharma*—
yet still said, *"I now speak briefly, unable to exhaust it."*

Yán Zǐ stood alone, his heart in quietude, said, *"Though I wish to follow, I cannot find the way."*

This *Sutra* is the root of all teachings—
its virtues, if spoken, cannot be exhausted,
the highest of virtues.
Spoken of, it cannot be fully grasped.
Spoken, people still cannot truly understand.

Thus, the Confucian *wuwei* governance,
the Daoist true and profound virtues,
the Buddhist offering of life and body—
the righteousness of the Western import—
are all beyond what can be transmitted in words.

Ah! The wonder of the Wheel-turning Sage—
heart and hand in perfect accord.

Zhuangzi, the master of the Three Teachings,
thus beyond the six directions—
preserved without discussion,
sank without debate—
not that he could not speak,
but words easily stir confusion—
better to remain silent.

Even the Master rarely spoke of fate,
for the Nature and Dao are beyond hearing.

The Buddha spoke of countless worldly scenes,
dividing them into matters and principles—
setting aside their boundless, unverifiable vastness,
even if grounded, what cannot be spoken remains much.
Those who follow his teachings assume the Buddha spoke what no one else could—
foolishly deeming it lofty—
yet he was born in a distant land,
among strange peoples and customs,
a rugged, remote place,
surrounded by many,
and the Buddha accommodated their views.
China did not know.

Foolishly claiming the Buddha’s vision was vast—
observe China alone: within a hundred *li*, customs differ.
Yan, Yue, Tai, and Qi—
mountains and rivers shift the winds—
those who do not traverse them cannot know.
How much more so the distant Western Regions?
Even with historical records, they are but hearsay and miscellany—
how can they be trusted without error?

Men love the strange and unusual,
without investigating truth—
if the Buddha truly knew all,
why did his scriptures not enter China in Tang texts,
translated three times before becoming coherent?
Since they did not know Tang speech,
what he spoke must have been of neighboring lands—
or perhaps, like Zhuangzi’s parables, some were allegorical.

People do not examine closely,
erroneously judging superiority—
how their love of the strange exceeds!

Alas, not speaking of all realms
prevents further confusion—
briefly speaking of virtues and transformations
to awaken the ignorant,
revealing true intent,
manifesting the correct Law—
this is why the Dao brings real benefit.

Scholars should diligently investigate further.

*(End of the "Virtues" Chapter, continuing the thirty-sixth section.)*

At that time, the Jade Emptiness Celestial Sovereign, upon hearing this, felt boundless joy, unable to contain his exultation. Gazing upon the benevolent countenance, he bowed in reverence and exclaimed in praise, composing this hymn:

*"Above the Nine Heavens lies the Great Luo,*
*Jade Capital of golden gates, its cloud-layers towering.*
*Within dwells the Heavenly Emperor,*
*Renowned for mercy and harmony,*
*His Dao unmatched, subduing all demons.*

*His celestial treasures and sacred talismans,*
*Jade laws and golden decrees,*
*Myriad gods and immortals in attendance,*
*With banners and flags in countless array.*
*Those who hear his name see sins erased,*
*Forever freed from the River of Love."*

Thus is he called the Jade Sovereign—
*The True Elder of the Azure Vault,*
*Perfect and pure in wondrous roundness,*
*Endowed with wisdom and eloquence,*
*Supreme in Dao and majesty,*
*Teacher of the Three Realms,*
*Primordial Ancestor of the Chaos,*
*Unsurpassed Master of all,*
*Compassionate Father to the Fourfold Birth,*
*The Highest Saint of the Celestial Heights,*
*Great in Mercy and Benevolence.*

Ten names complete his glory,
A thousand virtues manifest in his essence,
Boundless in his salvation of beings,
Liberating all from suffering’s cycle.

When the Jade Emptiness Celestial Sovereign had finished reciting this hymn and the ten names,
All the celestial saints spoke as one in astonishment,
*"Never before heard!"*—
For this sacred law and its exalted titles
Are rare even across eons.

At the moment the Heavenly Lord concluded this chapter on the divine incantations and virtues,
The Jade Emptiness Celestial Sovereign, upon hearing these words,
Felt overwhelming joy and delight,
Unable to restrain his rapture.
Gazing upon the Jade Emperor’s benevolent visage,
He bowed in reverence and composed this hymn of praise:

*"Above the Nine Heavens lies the Great Luo,*
*The Jade Capital’s golden gates,*
*Its cloud-layers rising in majestic tiers—*
*Lofty peaks beyond measure.*

*The Great Luo’s golden gates,*
*Where auspicious clouds and radiant light enfold,*
*Layer upon layer, boundless in height,*
*Towering and sublime, vast beyond reckoning.*

*The Heavenly Emperor within,*
*The Jade Emperor, sovereign of ten thousand teachings,*
*His mercy boundless, his benevolence profound,*
*His kindness not for selfish gain,*
*But nurturing all beings across endless kalpas,*
*Ensuring their sufficiency—*
*Thus called ‘incalculable grace.’*

*His Dao’s might and virtue unrivaled,*
*Subduing all demonic forces.*

*His celestial treasures—*
*Sacred talismans of the heavens,*
*Not mere curiosities,*
*But divine seals of the Mysterious and True.*

*His jade laws and golden statutes,*
*The celestial precepts and golden decrees.*

*Myriad gods and immortals in attendance,*
*Serving the august presence,*
*Numberless as the sands of time,*
*Flanked by banners and flags in endless array.*

*Those who hear his sacred name and law*
*See their sins utterly extinguished,*
*Forever freed from the River of Love—*
*For all karmic bonds are severed.*

*Thus is he called the Jade Sovereign—*
*As previously explained.*

*The True Elder of the Azure Vault,*
*The boundless expanse of heaven,*
*Vast and measureless,*
*The Primordial One without beginning.*

*Perfect and pure in wondrous roundness,*
*Mystically complete and utterly clean.*

*Endowed with wisdom and eloquence,*
*Great in insight and wisdom,*
*Possessing marvelous oratory and boundless talent.*

*Supreme in Dao and majesty,*
*His Dao without end,*
*His eminence unmatched.*

*Teacher of the Three Realms,*
*The sovereign guide of heaven, earth, and humanity.*

*The Primordial Ancestor,*
*Before heaven and earth divided,*
*Before worlds arose,*
*The Imperial True One eternally present,*
*The true root across all kalpas.*

*Thus called the Ancestor of the Chaos.*

*Unsurpassed Master of all,*
*For all teachings and sages,*
*None can rival his stature—*
*All acknowledge him as sovereign.*

*Compassionate Father to the Fourfold Birth,*
*The Fourfold Birth—womb-born, egg-born, moist-born, and metamorphic—*
*All owe their existence to his virtue,*
*From birth to completion,*
*Guided by his Dao to their end,*
*Thus called the Compassionate Father.*

*The Highest Saint of the Celestial Heights,*
*For no heaven surpasses the Great Luo,*
*No immortal or Buddha his equal in rank—*
*Thus called the Highest Saint.*

*Great in Mercy and Benevolence,*
*His mercy and benevolence without measure.*

*Ten names complete his glory,*
*From the True Elder of the Azure Vault to the Benevolent One,*
*His ten names are fully realized.*

*The Heavenly Emperor’s virtues and divine powers*
*Are all perfectly complete as such.*

*A thousand virtues manifest in his essence,*
*Though spoken briefly,*
*His virtues are boundless.*

*Boundless in his salvation of beings,*
*Liberating all from suffering’s cycle.*

When the Jade Emptiness Celestial Sovereign had finished reciting this hymn and the ten names,
All the celestial saints, in unison, exclaimed,
*"Never before encountered!"*—
*For this wondrous law and its sacred titles*
*Are rarely met even in ages past.*

*Or as some say,*
*"Never before seen in this world!"*

*If such are the Emperor’s virtues,*
*Those who study this scripture shall attain true enlightenment,*
*And thus shall not be ashamed.*

---
**End of Volume Seven of the *Imperial Scripture Collection with Commentaries***
**Volume Eight of the *Imperial Scripture Collection with Commentaries***
**Lower Scroll of the *Scripture of the Jade Sovereign’s Original Conduct***
**Chapter Four: The Chapter on Protection**
**The Protection Chapter**

---

At that time, the Celestial Sovereign of the Boundless Sky, upon hearing the scripture’s teachings, rose from his seat and knelt long before the Emperor, humbly declaring:
*"I pray that Your Sacred Benevolence universally benefit all assemblies, all celestial beings, and all who uphold and proclaim this scripture for their welfare."*

Then, the Jade Sovereign Emperor, moved by compassionate intent, opened the gate of benefit and proclaimed the *Yùkuì* [玉匮] ordinances, transmitting the *Língbǎo* [灵宝] sacred law, and addressed the Celestial Sovereign of the Boundless Sky:
*"Now, listen with utmost attention—I shall expound upon the virtues of receiving and upholding this scripture: its power to rescue the perilous, alleviate suffering, benefit the living and the dead, and perform divine and wondrous deeds."*

The assembled Celestial Worthies bowed in reverence and spoke in unison:
*"Today, we are fortunate to hear the *Zhànrán Chángzhù* [湛然常住]—the ever-abiding law. It bestows blessings upon all celestial realms, permeates the Three Realms, and annihilates the Three Woes and Five Sufferings. We humbly beseech Your Compassion to expound this sublime doctrine."*

After the celestial saints had extolled the virtues of the divine incantations and the Emperor’s sacred titles, the Celestial Sovereign of the Boundless Sky—who, though previously addressed as *Hàotiān* [昊天], is now properly named the *Hàdà Gāoxuán Tiāndì* [昊大高玄天帝]—heard the Celestial Worthy’s exposition of the scripture. Rising from his own seat, he knelt long before the Jade Emperor and respectfully declared:
*"I pray that Your Most Exalted Benevolence universally extend mercy to all assemblies—whether the celestial saints who hear this scripture, or the worldly multitude, though the heavens contain no worldly folk, for this scripture spans the Three Realms across boundless kalpas. It benefits all celestial beings and mortals, and all who uphold and proclaim its teachings, granting them boundless welfare."*

At that moment, the Jade Sovereign Emperor, moved by compassionate intent, awakened the boundless wisdom of deliverance, opened the gate of eternal benefit, and proclaimed the *Yùkuì* [玉匮] sacred ordinances—this scripture being the *Yùbì Lánghán* [玉笈琅函], treasured in the heavens, hence the phrase *"proclaim the Yùkuì ordinances."* He then transmitted the *Xuánlíng Miǎobǎo Dàfǎ* [玄灵妙宝大法], the profound and sacred law, and said to the Celestial Sovereign of the Boundless Sky:
*"Now, listen with utmost discernment—I shall speak to you of the virtues of receiving and upholding this scripture: its power to rectify all perilous straits, rescue all from suffering, and benefit all living and departed through divine and wondrous means."*

The assembled Celestial Worthies bowed in reverence and spoke in unison:
*"Today, we are fortunate to hear the *Zhànrán Chángzhù* [湛然常住] law—the ever-abiding, untainted, unspoiled, unchanging, neither ascending nor descending essence of human nature. Though entangled by external afflictions, we ourselves bring ruin, drifting through the wheel of existence in blind ignorance, unable to abide in this ever-present truth. Even spirits with attachments and gods with sentience, though their karmic retributions end and they return to the cycle, still cannot abide in this ever-present truth. Now, hearing the scripture’s virtues and benefits, our innate nature is purified, the roots and dust of defilement are exhausted, karmic deeds and perceptions are extirpated, sins and obstructions are removed, and perfection is firmly established. This is the hearing of the ever-abiding law—a rare encounter in the ages, how could we not be fortunate? Its power extends blessings to all celestial realms and beings, permeating the Three Realms, as previously explained."*

The Three Abysses—Heaven’s Abyss, Earth’s Abyss, Water’s Abyss—
The Five Sufferings: the suffering of form bound by color, the suffering of spirit bound by desire, the suffering of body bound by greed, the suffering of soul bound by physical burdens, the suffering of essence bound by the realm of adornment.
All are thus extinguished.
Only by the Most Venerable’s boundless compassion and pity for my subjects—
*Pity* being compassionate mercy and tender concern—
does this wondrous meaning unfold.

For this scripture is the supreme and wondrous Dao, hence its such virtues.
Though the Celestial Sovereign of the Azure Sky does not seek its profound intent, yet he requests its blessings—not to flatter like one offering drink to a man.
Even a single word or stroke of this scripture is an immeasurable treasure.
Knowing its efficacy and holding it with true sincerity, one will not fail the compassion of its proclamation.

**Chapter One: The Chapter of Protection**

The Jade Emperor declared:
*"If any being reveres and nurtures their parents, honors the Three Treasures with respect, exhausts loyalty to their ruler, commits no killing nor theft, indulges in no lust nor jealousy, harbors no wrath nor resentment, no arrogance nor deceit, upholds precepts and observes pure fasting, merges their heart with the Great Dao, nurtures a reverent mind toward life, and recites this scripture, I shall command the law to permeate all realms, spreading across the ten directions of the boundless world. I shall order the Eastern East-Hua Emperor with his green cavalry, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Southeastern Fu-Sang Grand Emperor with his divine soldiers and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Southern Zhu-Ling Grand Emperor with his red cavalry, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Southwestern Tai-Hua Elder with his divine soldiers and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Western Hao-Ling Sovereign Elder with his white cavalry, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Northwestern Celestial Sovereign with his divine soldiers and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Northern Zi-Wei Emperor with his black cavalry, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Northeastern Chong-Xu Heavenly Lord with his divine soldiers and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Supreme Heavenly Emperor of the Upper Realm, the Kunlun Elder with his yellow cavalry, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture; I shall order the Lower Realm Lai-He Heavenly Lord, the mountain-grove deities, divine soldiers, and countless hosts to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture."*

The Jade Emperor declared:
*"Upholding the scripture is not merely reciting it aloud. If any being in the world reveres and nurtures their parents, honors the Daoist scriptures and the Three Treasures with respect, exhausts their strength and heart in loyalty to their ruler, refrains from killing, stealing, lust, jealousy, wrath, resentment, arrogance, or deceit, receives and upholds the pure and mysterious precepts of the Dao, observes true fasting with sincerity, neither neglectful nor hasty, tranquil and unhurried, surrendering to nature, nurturing stillness, aligning with Heaven and congealing the True—merging their heart with the Great Dao, revering it as the Azure Sky—if they hold this scripture with solemn devotion, I, the Jade Emperor, shall command the law to permeate all worlds, spreading across the ten directions of the boundless realm. I shall order the Eastern East-Hua Emperor with his green cavalry, the Southern Zhu-Ling Grand Emperor with his red cavalry, the Western Hao-Ling Sovereign Elder with his white cavalry, the Northern Zi-Wei Emperor with his black cavalry, the Southeastern Fu-Sang Grand Emperor, the Southwestern Tai-Hua Elder, the Northwestern Celestial Sovereign—these are the four cardinal directions—the Northeastern Chong-Xu Heavenly Lord, the Supreme Heavenly Emperor of the Upper Realm—this is not the Gou-Chen Celestial Sovereign, but the deity who governs Heaven. The Buddha called this the realm of the *Devadatta* (帝释天主). The Kunlun Elder with his yellow cavalry, the Lower Realm Lai-He Heavenly Lord, the mountain-grove deities, and their divine soldiers and countless hosts shall all descend to shield and protect those who uphold this scripture."*

*Shield and protect* means to cherish and uphold.
Those who uphold the scripture, revering the Emperor’s words of the Dao, harmonizing with virtue, aligning with Heaven and the Dao in truth—these are the bodies of the Great Dao.
Where the Dao resides, both gods and mortals hold it in reverence, hence the Emperor commands the ten-directional holy hosts to shield and protect.

Yet this is only for those who are loyal, filial, respectful, and abstain from lust, killing, theft, and falsehood.
Upholding the scripture must be rooted in virtuous conduct, merging the heart with the Dao—then the Dao itself will return to them.

Some say, *"The Dao withdraws from the world, avoiding rulers and kin, thus not practicing filial piety or loyalty."*
They do not know the Dao’s profound precepts are most strict—guarding, preserving, and refining, never daring to violate precepts or bring shame to their bodies or kin.
With utmost sincerity and firmness, they first repay the Four Graces—how could they ever forget their rulers and kin, or be unfilial or disloyal?
Thus, the True Lord composed *The Scripture of Pure Clarity on Filial Piety and Loyalty*, to reveal the Dao’s true filial piety and loyalty.

**Chapter Two: The Chapter of Protection**

I command all the Golden Immortals of the ten directions, the Four Assemblies and Eight Divisions, and their attendants, to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture.
I command the Heavenly True Saints of the ten directions, the Flying Heavenly Kings, the Three Officials and Four Saints, the Two Luminaries and Nine Stars, the Northern Dipper and Southern Dipper, the Eastern Dipper and Western Dipper, the Central Dipper, the Twenty-Eight Constellations, the Celestial Hosts, the Vajra Warriors, and the Divine Kings—each with their hosts—to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture.

**Chapter Three: The Chapter of Protection**

I command the ten-directional celestial hosts, the Four Assemblies and Eight Divisions, and their attendants, to descend and shield all who uphold this scripture.

I command the ten-directional worlds of all Golden Immortals. The Golden Immortals are the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas. The Four Assemblies are not the Four Assemblies of the secular world, but the Four Assemblies of the yin and yang deities and their celestial troops. The Eight Divisions are explained in the second volume. The attendants are the kinsmen and affiliated beings of the Four Assemblies and Eight Divisions.

The Heavenly True Saints of the ten directions are the True Saints of all the celestial beings in the ten directions. The Flying Heavenly Kings are explained previously. The Three Officials are Heaven, Earth, and Water. The Four Saints are Tianpang, Tianyou, Yisheng, and Yousheng. The Two Luminaries are the Sun and Moon. The Nine Stars are: Jin (金), Mu (木), Shui (水), Huo (火), Tu (土), Yue Mo (月孛), Zi Zhi (紫炁), Luo Hou (罗喉), and Ji Du (计都).

North, South, East, West, and Central are the Five Dippers. The Twenty-Eight Constellations are: Jiao (角), Keng (亢), Shi (氏), Fang (房), Xin (心), Wei (尾), Ji (箕), Dou (斗), Niu (牛), Nü (女), Xu (虚), Wei (危), Shi (室), Bi (壁), Kui (奎), Lou (娄), Wei (胃), Mao (昴), Bi (毕), Zhi (觜), Shen (参), Jing (井), Gui (鬼), Liu (柳), Xing (星), Zhang (张), Yi (翼), Zhen (轸)—all the stars of the celestial circuit.

The Vajra Warriors and Divine Kings are all the generals and troops. Each with their subordinates and attendant hosts.

The *Scripture* is the Emperor’s decree, proclaimed by the court command. The Three Ministers, Four Officials, the Two Capitals’ Nine Ministers, all officials and attendants, nobles of different surnames, and the myriad common folk—none dare fail to revere and uphold it.

The Jade Scripture is guarded and sustained by myriad deities, for the Emperor’s command honors the virtuous and aids those of power. Within the human body are the Three Primordials, Four Symbols, Two Qi, Nine Orifices, Five Phases, and the degrees of the Twenty-Eight Constellations—encompassing the celestial circuits. Water, Fire, True Will, Great Wisdom, Cultivation, Vigorous Practice, Marvelous Dharma, and Meritorious Deeds align with the deities, so that within a single body—its hair and skin, flesh and blood, sinews and bones, spirit and qi, essence and meridians—all support the True Nature’s authentic qi, preserving the vital treasure.

This True Nature’s authentic qi is the Emperor’s True Scripture: thirty-six thousand divine qi and eighty-four thousand fine-pored true lights, manifesting the Ten Directions’ Immortals, Vajra Warriors, and Stellar Divine Kings and their hosts. The *Sutra of Disaster Dissipation* states: *"There are the Heavenly True Saints and Vajra Warriors, each numbering hundreds of billions, guarding this Scripture"*—this is its meaning.

The Scripture is not confined to words and letters; its true intent lies within our heart. The deities are not bound to the Ten Directions’ worlds; they reside within our single body.

「Cultivate the mind and refine the body—this is not achieved through mere chanting and reading, but through sincere, silent practice, with utmost sincerity and selflessness. When spirit and *qi* are complete, the Sage can be emulated, Heaven can be aspired to, the Dao/Way can be entered, and all actions will bring auspicious results; the deities will surely protect you.

When the three medicines are depleted and the True Nature is lost, one’s own spirit weakens, *qi* falters, and essence fails to circulate fully—this defies Heaven’s order. How then could the deities protect you?

Alas, all humans share the same essence, but the virtuous who cultivate it thrive in auspiciousness, while the petty who defy it meet disaster. Thus the Scripture says: *"Those who cover and protect this Scripture will know the blessings of Heaven through virtue."*

The Emperor’s virtue is boundless, and the benefits of this Scripture are supreme—how greatly do people respect and receive it?

The *Chapter of Protection* decrees: The Vajra Warriors who command life and death, the Four Heavenly Kings of the gates, the Five Sacred Mountains and Four Great Waters, as well as all named mountains, the Four Seas and Nine Rivers, the Twelve River Sources, forests, valleys, streams, and marshes—all their ruling deities and their retinues—shall cover and protect those who receive and uphold this Scripture. In all perilous and treacherous places, they shall grant safety and stability.

The Emperor’s decree extends to all local deities of the lands, including those of ditches and canals, as well as all great-power ghostly kings, commanding them to cover and protect those who receive and uphold this Scripture.

The Twelve River Sources are now recorded as thirteen names, for two waters share the same source—thus it is called the Twelve River Sources. The decree commands the Subduing Kings and Heavenly Vajra Warriors. The Four Heavenly Kings of the gates are the Eastern, Western, Southern, and Northern gatekeepers. The Five Sacred Mountains are: the Eastern **Tài**, Southern **Héng**, Western **Huá**, Northern **Héng**, and Central **Sōng**. The Four Great Waters refer to the deities of the **Jiāng**, **Hé**, **Huái**, and **Jì** rivers.

All named mountains in the world are included. The Four Seas are the Eastern, Western, Southern, and Northern seas. The Nine Rivers include: **Yángzǐ**, **Qiantáng**, **Hànyáng**, **Huìyáng**, **Hùntóng**, **Jǐn Jiāng**, **Xiāng Jiāng**, **Wūlóng**, and **Yālù**, encompassing all rivers.

The Twelve River Sources are the origins of the Yellow River, the world’s vital vein: such as **Kūnlún**, **Yǔmén**, **Xīngxiù Hǎi**, **Huǒdūn Nǎo’ér**, and its tailing streams, **Fāxiè** and **Fáxiè**, along with the roots of other rivers that flow into it. Another account states that when discussing the Yellow River’s sources, **Kūnlún** has nine wells and seven springs, not just twelve. The Twelve River Sources pertain to the nine rivers—**Túhài**, **Tàishǐ**, **Mǎxiá**, **Fùfǔ**, **Húsū**, **Jiǎnjié**, **Gōu pán**, **Gēlín**, **Rǔ**, **Hàn**, **Huái**, and **Sì**—as well as the **Rǔ**, **Hàn**, **Huái**, and **Sì** waters, totaling twelve.

The Yellow River is the supreme deity of all rivers. Rivers like **Jīng**, **Wèi**, **Yí**, **Wèn**, **Shēn**, **Wéi**, **Hùtuó**, **Xīngxié**, and **Ruòshuǐ**, along with all other rivers, are its subordinate deities. The forests and mountains encompass all terrestrial groves and peaks. The streams and marshes are all the world’s flowing waters and wetlands. *川* refers to moving waters; *泽* means stagnant waters. All ruling deities of mountains, forests, streams, and marshes, along with their retinues, are commanded to cover and protect those who uphold this Scripture.

In all hazardous and difficult places, let them have no worries and find stability—this refers specifically to those who hold the Scripture. Wherever the Emperor’s decree reaches, all local deities and responsive spirits of the lands shall heed it. *沟* (gōu) are dry channels, either in mountains or earth; *渠* (qú) are waterways. *等神* (děngshén) includes all minor deities beyond ditches and canals.

All great-power ghostly kings are likewise commanded to cover and protect those who uphold this Scripture.

The essence of this Imperial Scripture aligns with the treasures of all Immortals, the teachings of all Buddhas, the practices of all Heavens, the reverence of all deities, and the recitations of all people. Demons and malevolent spirits submit themselves. Indeed, mountains are steadied by it, and waters flow endlessly—its protection is strict and unyielding.

If those who uphold the Scripture are its very guardians, how then could they dare to be negligent? A single moment of carelessness brings grave sin and deep consequences.

Truly, Confucius said: *"The petty do not know Heaven’s decree and do not fear it."* They mock the great, scorn the words of the Sage—this is the petty. Even in observing this Scripture, one must still guard against arrogance and exert diligence.

The *Fifth Chapter of Protection* concludes.»

The **Scripture** commands all **demons (魔)** and **external heretics (外道)**—whether **Heavenly Demons (天魔)**, **Earthly Demons (地魔)**, **Demon Kings (魔王)**, **Demon Folk (魔民)**, or **Demon Women (魔女)**—to tremble and submit, vanish their forms and flee their traces, soar high beyond the seas, and retreat far to distant realms.

Thus, all **mountain spirits, forest deities, ancestral shrines, and temple guardians (山林社稷祠庙之属)**, as well as **every ghost and spirit (一切鬼神)**, shall **self-destruct and vanish (自消灭)**.

The **Five Directions’ Plague and Epidemic Demons (五方行病瘟疫鬼帅)**, **all malevolent ghosts and spirits (诸恶鬼神)**, including the **Wind King (风王)** and **water monsters (水怪)**, the **sinful retributive dragons (孽音业龙)** and **malevolent deities (妖神)**, **earthly spirits (土精)** and **water sirens (水魅)**, shall all **self-destruct and vanish (尽自消灭)**.

The **Five Empties (五虚)** and **Six Depletions (六耗)**, **unusual dreams (梦寐乖常)**, **sorcery along wild paths (野道咒咀)**, and **poisonous hexes (蛊毒之类)** shall likewise **self-destruct and vanish (皆自消灭)**.

For those who **uphold the Scripture with a devout heart (持经人心欲愿者)**, all **whims shall be fulfilled (一切如意)**, and **every desire shall be satisfied (皆得满足)**.

**Astonishing and resounding (慑音聂)!**

The **Scripture commands (令)**—by **imperial decree (勅命)**, **prohibition (禁令)**, and **extermination (剿除)**—all **demons (诸魔)** and **external heretics (外道)**:

**External heretics (外道)** are those who indulge in **lewd speech (淫辞)**, **perverse doctrines (邪说)**, **deviant practices (僻行)**, **miscellaneous techniques (杂法)**, **side-door sorcery (旁门)**, and **petty occult arts (小术)**, including **private methods (私技)** numbering **three thousand six hundred, ninety-six kinds, or thirty-six thousand (三千六百、九十六种、三万六千等)**.

The **Scripture commands (令)**—by **imperial decree (勅命)**, **prohibition (禁令)**, and **extermination (剿除)**—that they **all tremble and submit (悉皆慑伏)**.

All **demons (诸魔)**—**trepidation (慑)** is the **submission of the heart in awe (惊畏心服)**, **subjugation (伏)** is the **retraction and surrender (收敛归伏)**. They **conceal their forms and flee their traces (潜形遁迹)**—**concealment (潜)** means to **hide their likeness (藏其形象)**, daring not to reveal themselves; **flight (遁)** means to **evade their traces (逃其影迹)**, daring not to linger.

Though the forms of these **demons (诸魔)** may outwardly appear **bewitching (妖艳)** and their illusory shapes **strange and beautiful (幻象奇美)**, their true nature is **obstructed (阻)**, unseen by mortals. This **Scripture’s true teachings (真法)** shatter the **ghosts’ resolve (破鬼之胆)** and **shatter the demons’ hearts (碎魔之心)**. No demon can escape its scrutiny—**awe-struck by the profound and potent decrees (玄律丹劲)**, they dare not linger, lest their **ugly essence (丑质)** be exposed.

The **external heretics (外道)** seek to **obscure the truth (乱真)** with their words. When the **True Dao (正道)** prevails, **deviant doctrines (邪说)** fade; when the **Great Dao (大道)** is honored, **side-paths (傍门)** are abandoned. Once the **imperial decree (帝命)** is proclaimed, they dare not persist.

To **soar beyond the seas (高飞海外)**—their **demonic deeds (魔行)** leave no trace—**a metaphor for utter disappearance (飞言)**. How could **external heretics (外道)** be said to **fly (飞)**? To **restrain the heart and ease the mind (格心易虑)**, to **turn toward transformation and abandon selfishness (向化忘私)**, to **ascend beyond the seas (高腾海外)**—this is the **common phrase (俗语言)** for **the soul fleeing to the heavens (魂飞天外)** and **the spirit dispersing into the nine heavens (魄散九霄)**. They flee to distant lands, **daring not to remain in their former places (不敢居其故地)**.

Thus, all **mountain spirits, forest deities, land gods (社), grain gods (稷), temple spirits (祠), and ancestral shrines (庙)**—those that demand **blood sacrifices and offerings (血食)**—**every ghost and spirit (鬼神)** shall **self-destruct (自消灭)**.

**Mountains and forests (山林)**—as previously explained. **Land gods (社)** are **earth spirits (土神)**; **grain gods (稷)** are **harvest deities (谷神)**. **Temples (祠)** are **overseers (司)** and **sacrificial rites (祀)**—where deities **oversee and are invoked (神之司临)**. **Shrines (庙)** are **places of worship (朝)**, where **ancestral spirits are honored (妾神於庙)** and **sacrifices of blood, grain, and wine (血食享牲醴)** are offered.

All these **spirits (鬼神)** are **worthy of veneration (宜祀者)**—how then can they **self-destruct (自消灭)**? If **spirits are summoned without proper rites (神邀祭祀)**, they will **act unjustly (为不直)**; if **the people flatter ghosts and spirits (民谄鬼神)**, they will **act corruptly (为不正)**.

Thus, the **Master Sa Zhengren** subdued the **King of Spirits (王灵官)** and reformed the **City City God (禁城隍)**; **Ximen Bao**, governor of **Jizhou**, cast the **shaman into the water** to restrain the **River Spirit (河神)**. How much more so when **evil spirits feign divinity to deceive people**, and **people revere falsehoods to mislead the common folk**?

Therefore, **Hu Ying** in his governance of **Guangdong** destroyed **illusionary Buddhas** and slew **demonic serpents**, punishing monks to free the ignorant masses. Now it is said that **all ghosts and spirits shall self-destruct (消灭)**—following the **Scripture’s decree**, they **no longer bestow blessings or calamities**, and their **threat and influence vanish**.

The **Five Directions’ Plague and Epidemic Spirit Generals (五方行病瘟疫鬼帅)**—these **malevolent ghosts and spirits (诸恶鬼神)** are not the **Plague Spirit Generals (行病鬼帅)**, but rather **the world’s malevolent and powerful ghosts (世之厉鬼强神)**. Alongside them, the **Wind Sovereigns (并行风之王)**, **water monsters (水中之怪)**, **violent and sinful dragons (作孽暴龙)**, **portentous and malevolent spirits (妖异邪神)**, **earthly sprites and wood demons (土精木魅)**—all shall **self-destruct**.

The **Five Emptinesses and Six Depletions (五虚六耗)**—the **emptiness of spirit, qi, blood, and body (精神气血身五虚)**, the **withering of the six pulses (六脉衰耗)**—lead to **dreams contrary to nature (梦寐乖常)** and **restless soul and spirit (魂魄不宁)**.

It is also said that the **Five Emptinesses and Six Depletions (五虚六耗)** are like **heaven’s weeping and ruin (天哭破败)**, the **stars of calamity (丧门、太岁、大耗、小耗、飞康、空亡、黄旛、豹尾、九果、赤口、白舌)**—**malevolent omens, killing stars, and malevolent deities (恶厌神杀凶星、作祸神鬼之属)**—all **malevolent affairs (一切辱事)**, **wild Daoist rites (野道)**, **evil spells (邪法)**, **curses and incantations (咒诅妖语)**, whether **curses or oaths (或咒或誓)**, and **poisonous hexes and bewitchments (及蛊毒魇昧之类)**—all shall **self-destruct**.

For those who **hold this Scripture with sincere desire (持经人心欲愿者)**, all **schemes and aspirations (谋望)** that align with their hearts’ wishes (趁心如意) shall be **fulfilled without obstruction (皆得满足，无有违逆)**.

The **virtuous and moral (道德之士)**—ghosts and spirits **revere and hold them in awe (鬼神钦重)**—and all **malevolence and evil shall vanish (凶邪尽消)**.

When **Xiang Sang died**, **Zi Tong drove away the plague (梓橦驱瘟)**, **Jing Yang subdued the river dragon (旌阳伏蛟)**, **Master Zu’s ancestor subdued demons (祖天师伏魔)**, and **Master Sa restrained ghosts (萨祖禁鬼)**—all had **clear and manifest effects (皆有明效)**.

Ah! **Wang Yanzhang** was a **hero of integrity (烈士)**—though he **stole the wish for execution (盗愿刑戮)**, he **did not allow Yanzhang to know of external Dao (外道)**, truly a **man of virtue (诚有德之铃然者)**.

Yet, **human beings’ Three Corpses (三尸)**, **Five Burdens (五累)**, **Seven Emotions (七情)**, **Six Desires (六欲)**, and **Nine Consciousnesses (九识)**—**lower evil (下恶)** harms them, and **they deceive themselves (欺不能正己)**. If one **subdues evil and eliminates calamity (伏邪除凶)**, and **advances on the Dao (正进道)**, **severing the Three Corpses (斩三尸)**, **eliminating the Five Burdens (除五累)**, **extinguishing emotions and desires (情欲尽)**, and **removing malevolent consciousness (识恶除)**, then **one’s own wishes shall be fulfilled (己愿尽)**, and **external evils shall vanish while auspiciousness arrives (外邪消，凶散吉临)**.

**Protection and Upholding of the Six Chapters**
Even if one **cannot follow the prescribed rituals (未能遵依科教)**, **observe fasts (修崇斋醮)**, but only **maintains purity and upholds precepts (清净持戒)**, **devotedly accepts (专一信受)**, **honors and reveres (尊重敬慕)** this Scripture, and **participates in fasting rites (并同修斋)**, those who **uphold pure precepts (护持净戒)** shall have **unobstructed merit (功德坦然无碍)**, **freedom and ease (自在消遥)**, and are called **"Saints Among Men (人中圣)"**, with **enduring virtue and wisdom (德慧长新)**, equal to the **True Persons (诸真人)**.

Those who **receive and uphold the Scripture according to its law (如法受持经者)** shall have **merit beyond measure (功德莫量)**.

Even if one **cannot follow the esoteric rituals and precepts (未能遵依玄科教典)**, **observe grand fasts (修崇大斋醮)**, but only **remains pure and unstained (清净无染)**, **upholds precepts with singular devotion (持戒专一)**, and **adheres to the Daoist precept codes (持守道门戒律)**—whether the **Five Precepts, Eight Precepts, Twelve Provisional Precepts, Eighteen Precepts, Twenty-Four Precepts, Thirty-Six Precepts, Seventy-Two Precepts, One Hundred Twenty Precepts, One Hundred Eighty Precepts, Three Hundred Great Precepts, or the Six Hundred Pure Precepts of the Celestial Maidens (女冠六百净戒)**—if one **concentrates with wholehearted sincerity (专心致志)**, **devotes oneself to this precept chapter with unwavering resolve (持此戒品专一，坚固无二)**, **accepts and reveres it in faith (信受尊重)**, **accepts and practices it sincerely (信受奉行)**, **holds it in solemn awe (钦严尊重)**, and **reveres and admires this Scripture (诚敬仰慕是此经典)**, then even if one **only maintains purity, upholds precepts, and accepts them with singular devotion (或作但能清净持戒，专一信受，尊重敬慕读者)**, all are included.

They shall **participate in fasting rites together (并同修斋)**, and those who **uphold pure precepts (护持净戒者)** shall have **equal merit (功德一般)**. All **deities shall respect and protect them (诸神敬佑)**.

It is also said that **if one maintains purity and singular devotion (自己清净专一)**, **upholding the pure precepts they have taken (护持所守净戒)**, their **merit shall be unobstructed (是人功德，坦然无碍)**.

*"Tan"* means **level (平)**, *"kuang"* means **broad (广)**. If the **heart is divided (心有二)**, then **merit is not genuine (功德不实)**. If **precepts are not upheld (戒不持)**, they **taint merit (於功德有玷)**. When **mind and body are pure (心身清净)**, **precepts are upheld with singular devotion (持戒专)**, **acceptance is sincere (信受切)**, and **the Scripture is honored with reverence (尊敬经典)**, with **no attachment in the heart (心无染)**, **no division in the heart (心无二)**, and **no deficiency or obstruction (无有亏欠萦击)**, then **merit is truly genuine (功德真实)**, and **how can there be any obstruction (自是坦然，又有何碍)?** One shall **dwell in freedom and ease (自在逍遥)**.

---

From birth, human nature is **unbound and unrestrained (无拘无困)**. Yet when **encumbered by external influences (客感物累)**, one is **busy and labored (忙忙苦苦)**, losing **one’s innate harmony (无复自如)**, and **how can true joy (快乐) be found?**

When **the heart is pure and faith is true (清净正信)**, **external burdens are cast aside (无复物累)**, and **great freedom (大自在)** is attained, **joy becomes everlasting (常乐逍遥)**. Such a person is called **the Sage among mortals (人中圣)**, not merely one who **wanders freely (逍遥之人)**.

**Pure and true (消净正信)**, **transcending common humanity (高出人俦)**, this is the **Sage among mortals (人中圣人)**. **Virtue and wisdom are ever renewed (德慧常新)**, **practice aligns with insight (习与智长)**, and **transformation harmonizes with the heart (化与心成)**. When **perception and understanding are true (闻见真)**, **intellect merges with intuition (智虑融)**, and **external burdens are forgotten (物累忘)**, **true nature shines undimmed (性真湛)**.

**Virtue is daily renewed (德日新)**, **wisdom ever brightened (慧日明)**—this is the **ever-renewing virtue and wisdom (德慧常新)**. Those who **share in the true way (同诸真人)** are those who **hold scripture and attain the Dao (清净正信者同持经得道)****,** the **true beings of the heavens (诸天真人)**.

The **pure and true (清净)**—**upholding precepts (持戒)**, **singular in devotion (专一)**, **sincere in acceptance (信受切)**, **reverent in honoring scripture (尊重敬慕)**—**do so without calculation of merit (非有计功之心)**, nor **for human intent (为人之意)**. Their **actions are without ulterior motive (无所为而为)**, **utterly free from deceit or interruption (绝无虚假间断)**.

This is as the **Master Kong (孔子)** spoke: **"In haste or at leisure, no deviation (造次终食，颠沛无违)."**
This is as the *Zhōng Yōng* (《中庸》) states: **"None enter without finding their own fulfillment (无入而不自得)."**
Zhuangzi expounded the **essence of *Xiāoyáo* (逍遥)**, and **Bai Jianchuan (海蟾)** sang the **ode of *Kuàihuó* (快活)**.
The **Buddhist teaching of Great Freedom (大自在)**, the **Confucian principle of Daily Renewal (日新)**, and **"Revering the old and knowing the new (温故而知新)"**—all are **natural manifestations (自然之效)**.
**How could there be any contrivance or imitation (假借)?** **How could there be any forced adoption (勉强袭取)?**

Ah! **Pure and true (清净正信)**, even **without ritual instruction (不依科教)**, nor **observing fasts and offerings (修斋醮)**, **such natural merit (自然功德)** still exists. **Thus, the Dao’s profound essence (道旨玄科)** is **found only in the true substance of scripture (实体经义)**.
**Ritual instruction, fasts, and offerings (科教斋醮)**—the **Universal Law (普法)**—**are but means to propagate the Dao’s transformation (以演道化)**.
Chen Xiyi (陈希夷) **mocked the *Dù Rén Jīng* (度人经)**, yet **his attainment of the Dao (成道)** was **true adherence to scripture’s essence (盖真持经旨)**.

**Today’s fasts and offerings (斋醮)** lack **clear efficacy (无明效)** because **there are elaborate rites (有盛仪)**, yet **no true cultivation (无真修)**.
If **one is pure and true (清净正信)** and **further observes fasts and offerings (更修斋醮)**, then **merit is greatly enhanced (功益大)**.
Without **fasts and offerings (无斋醮)**, yet **with true sincerity (有真诚)**, merit **is still divine (功亦神)**.
If **sincerity is absent (无真诚)**, then **fasts and offerings (斋醮)** are **mere formalities (文具)**—**how much greater the fault (宁无过乎)!**

**Chapter on Protection (护持品七章)**
At that time, the **Celestial Sovereign, Emperor of Heaven (昊天上帝)**, upon hearing these words, **bowed in reverence (稽首)** before the **Celestial Sovereign (帝)** and sang:

**Great is the Supreme Dao (大哉至道)!**
**Formless and nameless (无形无名).**
**Vast through countless eons (渺渺亿劫),**
**The Yellow Way (黄道) opens in purity (开清).**

**Divine purity shines radiant (神清朗耀),**
**The Nine *Qi* (九炁) exhale their essence (吐精).**
**The Jade Void (玉虚) glows clear (澄辉),**
**The Great Mists (太霞) ascend in brilliance (高明).**

**The Jade Sovereign (玉皇) initiates transformation (开化),**
**Universally nurturing (溥度) all heavenly and human beings (天人).**
**The Three Primordial Forces (三元) nourish the Dao (道养),**
**The Two Symbols (二象) encompass all life (摄生).**

**Decayed trees and ancient roots (朽树故根),**
**Though withered, are made to flourish anew (已枯使荣).**
**Creeping and crawling beings (蠢动蜎息),**
**Attain eternal life (长生) and transcend their forms (化形).**

**Those who bear in womb or conceive (怀胎含孕),**
**All achieve birth and growth (俱得生成).**
**The departed whose life has passed (亡者命过),**
**Their spirits return to the Three Pure Ones (魂归三清),**
**Their *pò* (魄) undergo refinement and liberation (受炼度),**
**Ascending to the Southern Palace (南宫飞升).**

**Today is a great auspice (今日大吉)!**
**All are granted radiance (皆得光明).**
**The Five Emperors (五帝) reflect and mirror (鉴映),**
**Proclaiming to all sentient beings (普告万灵).**

**Heavenly deities and earthly spirits (天神地祇),**
**And all river sources (及诸河源),**
**The Five Sacred Peaks and Four Great Waterways (五岳四渎),**
**And all named mountains (及诸名山),**
**The Mystic Void (洞玄), the Mystic Emptiness (洞虚),**
**The Mystic Abyss (洞空), the Mystic Immortals (洞仙),**
**The Boundless Greatest Sage (无极大圣),**
**The Supreme True Venerable Deity (至真尊神),**
**The Endless and Boundless (无穷无极),**
**All oversee and liberate beings (溥监度生).**

**Evil roots are severed (恶根断绝),**
**The Mystic Register records their names (玄都记名).**
**All true beings gather in ranks (众真班列),**
**Attending to the Celestial Sovereign’s decree (成听帝言).**

**The Scripture is the Sovereign’s commandment (经是帝勑),**
**Preserved and chanted by those who uphold humanity (保诵持人).**
**To the utmost degree of the Dao’s shore (至度道岸),**
**No calamity shall intrude (无使灾侵).**

**I bear the Sovereign’s mandate (我奉帝命),**
**All shall heed (一切咸听).**

At that time, the **Vision of Understanding (解见)** appeared as before. The **Celestial Sovereign, Emperor of Heaven (昊天上帝)**, upon hearing these words, **pointed to the merit of protection (指上护持功德言)** and **bowed in reverence (稽首)** before the **Jade Sovereign (玉帝)** while singing in praise:

**Great is the Supreme Dao (大哉至道)!**
**Its magnitude is beyond measure (大莫可量),**
**Its reach is beyond attainment (至不可及).**

**Formless and nameless (无形无名),**
**Unseen and unheard (不见不闻),**
**Its name is but a forced designation (名亦强称).**

**Vast through countless eons (渺渺亿劫),**
**Without beginning or end (无始无终),**
**Spanning innumerable ages (历劫无数),**
**A hundred million is called *yì* (亿), yet truly it is beyond number (要之举大数言，实无数耳).**

**The Yellow Way (黄道) opens in purity (开清),**
**Marking auspicious times and joyous gatherings (吉时庆会),**
**The Heavenly Dao (天道) is made clear and open (开通).**

**Divine purity shines radiant (神清朗耀),**
**The divine wind is ever pure (神风永清),**
**Its brilliance is undimmed (朗耀光明).**

**The Nine *Qi* exhale their essence (九炁吐精):**
**The Nine *Qi* are *yān* (炎), *yǎn* (演), *hào* (昊), *jǐng* (景), *dào* (道), *hún* (混), *dòng* (洞), *hào* (浩) and others (等).**
**Exhaling essence (吐精)**—the **Yellow Way opens to dispel death and celebrate rebirth (黄道开死庆消)**,**
**The Nine *Qi* display their radiance (九炁呈辉),**
**Exhaling essence in dazzling splendor (吐精炫瑞).**

**The Jade Void (玉虚) glows clear (澄辉),**
**The Jade Light (玉光) is pure and luminous (虚明),**
**Its clarity is undimmed (澄然清辉).**
**Some say the Jade Void (玉虚) manifests the Heavenly Radiance (天呈辉).**

**The Great Mists (太霞) ascend in brilliance (高明),**
**The Great Mystic Light (太玄霞光),**
**Lofty and supremely bright (大高至明).**

**The Jade Sovereign (玉皇) initiates transformation (开化),**
**Liberation and instruction (度教化).**
**Universally nurturing (溥度) all beings in heaven and on earth (天上地下人).**

**The Three Primordial Forces (三元) nourish the Dao (道养):**
**Heaven generates (天生), earth perfects (地成), and humanity is transformed (人教化),**
**These are the Three Primordial Forces (三元) nurturing the Dao (道养).**

**The Two Symbols (二象) encompass all life (摄生):**
**The *qián* (乾) and *kūn* (坤) create and transform (造化),**
**Generating all beings and things (生成人物).**
**Thus it is said, the Two Symbols encompass all life (终始宰制，故云二象摄生).**
**Some say the yin and yang mold and refine (陶铸) are the Two Symbols encompassing all life (二象摄生),**
**Both are correct teachings (俱是正论).**

**Decayed trees and ancient roots (朽树故根):**
**Decayed (朽), ruined (坏);**
**Ancient (故), dead (死).**
**Though withered, they are made to flourish anew (已枯使荣):**
**Withered (枯), dried (槁).**
**Already dried and withered (已乾枯), yet they are made to bloom once more (使再发荣).**

**Creeping and crawling beings (蠢动蜎息),**
**Long-lived and transformed in form (长生化形):**
**The crawling and flying of insects (蜎飞蠕动蠢类),**
**Not perishing young (生不夭折),**
**All escape their original forms (俱得脱其本形).**

**Those who bear in womb or conceive (怀胎含孕),**
**All achieve birth and growth (俱得生成):**
**The gestation and birth of beings and things (人物胎孕),**
**Without harm or loss (不伤不堕),**
**All are granted safe and natural growth (俱得安然，生长而成).**

**The departed whose life has passed (亡者命过),**
**Their spirits return to the Three Pure Ones (魂归三清):**
**The dead do not pass through the underworld (死者不经地狱),**
**All ascend to the heavens (皆归天上).**
**The *pò* (魄) undergo refinement and liberation (受炼度),**
**Ascending to the Southern Palace (南宫飞升):**
**The seven *pò* (七魄) of the dead are refined by the Great Compassionate True Beings (大慈真人),**
**Their spirits fly upward to the Southern Palace (魂神飞上南宫).**

**Today is a great auspice (今日大吉)!**
**All are granted radiance (皆得光明):**
**All beings are saved (人物咸济),**
**Darkness is dispelled by light (幽暗开光).**

**The Five Emperors (五帝) reflect and mirror (鉴映):**
**The Five Emperors of the five directions (五方五帝) illuminate and reflect (照鉴光映).**

**Proclaiming to all sentient beings (普告万灵),**
**Informing all ghosts and spirits (遍告一切鬼神).**

**Heavenly deities and earthly spirits (天神地祇),**
**And all river sources (及诸河源),**
**The Five Sacred Peaks and Four Great Waterways (五岳四渎),**
**And all named mountains (及诸名山),**
**The Mystic Void (洞玄), the Mystic Emptiness (洞虚),**
**The Mystic Abyss (洞空), the Mystic Immortals (洞仙),**
**The Mystic and the Void, the Abyss and the Emptiness (玄虚空洞),**
**All immortal sages, deities, and Buddhas, along with ghosts.**

**The Boundless Great Sage, the Most True and Noble Deity,**
**Limitless and without end, measureless in extent.**
**All-pervasively guiding and saving sentient beings,**
**Universally overseeing and transforming the multitude of life.**
**Cutting off evil roots, eternally eradicating the wickedness of all beings.**

**Recorded in the Mystic Capital, the Mystic Dan Platform,**
**Recording deeds and virtues of merit.**
**Assembled ranks of all True Ones,**
**Standing in orderly attendance.**
**All heed the Imperial words—**
**The words of the Jade Emperor.**
**This is the Imperial Edict; this scripture is the Jade Emperor’s sovereign decree.**
**Protecting those who recite and uphold—**
**Guarding those who chant and preserve the scriptural law.**
**Ascending to the Dao’s shore,**
**Reaching the Dao’s heights.**
**No calamity shall intrude,**
**All disasters shall be averted.**

**I bear the Emperor’s command,**
**The command of the Jade Emperor.**
**All shall heed it—**
**All beings, ghosts, and spirits, are thus virtuous.**

**This is the full proclamation of the scripture’s merit.**

---

**Chapter on Protection and Upholding**

At that time, the Celestial Sovereign of the Vaulting Heaven spoke these words and declared to the great assembly:
*"This is the Jade Emperor’s wondrous law, the secret speech of the Saints.
The path is severed, the Dao is cut off—
Subtle and unfathomable, its grandeur beyond measure,
The true essence of the divine, the root of all numinous power,
Guarding and pacifying the land, liberating beings from birth and death."*

When the Celestial Sovereign of the Vaulting Heaven had spoken these wondrous words—
*"The assembly of the law, the pure gathering of saints, all revered the Dao’s speech,
And universally attained enlightenment."*

At that time, the Celestial Sovereign of the Vaulting Heaven bowed in homage and praised the Jade Emperor.
After speaking these words, he declared to the celestial sages, true deities, and the great assembly:
*"This is the Jade Emperor’s wondrous law."*

All the Saints and Holy Ones possess their own laws—
Some vast yet measurable, transmitted with limits,
Some knowable in their beginning and end,
Some benefit the living yet neglect the dead,
Some aid humans yet abandon things,
Some are known to ghosts and spirits,
Some are not subdued by demons,
Some are formless and unknown, unable to universally save.
These are not wondrous.*

But this scripture’s transformative power is boundless,
Its efficacy immeasurable—
All who gain its benefit are of an extraordinary order.

Thus, the Jade Emperor’s wondrous law,
The secret, profound speech of the Saints and True Ones.
When the Primordial began to expound the scripture,
How could the Saints and the Most True Ones, upon hearing it,
Not treasure it and dare not lightly reveal it?
Hence, it is called the *Secret Speech of the Saints.*

The path is severed, the Dao is cut off—
The highest vehicle of all.
A law not commonly heard,
The essential path to True Cultivation,
The cyclical practice of the Saints.
Emotional desires and illusions are uprooted here,
Love and mundane thoughts are extinguished without remainder.
The wheel of rebirth is severed in two—
Thus, it is said: *The path is severed, the Dao is cut off.*

Another saying: *The Seven Saints were all deluded; this is a path few can tread.*
Subtle and unfathomable—
Deep and profound, beyond mortal thought,
Difficult for the mind to grasp,
A mystery even gods cannot fathom.
Its grandeur is vast—
A wondrous range of celestial chapters,
The true essence of divine enlightenment.

Another explanation: *The Jade Emperor’s Dao-range is the ultimate divine teacher.*
Too rigid a constraint.

Guarding and pacifying the land,
Liberating beings from birth and death.

At that time, the Celestial Sovereign of the Vaulting Heaven,
Having spoken this wondrous law—
*"The assembly of the law, the pure gathering of saints,*
*All revered the Dao’s speech—*
*Some take it as revering the Vaulting Heaven’s wondrous law,*
*And universally attained enlightenment."*

**Verification:**
*"The Master’s words on nature and the Dao cannot be heard by all."*
*The Scripture of the Beginning of Writing* says:
*"The wise create delusion; even ghosts and spirits do not recognize it."*
The Buddha spoke on Vulture’s Peak, and the bodhisattvas cupped their ears to listen.
The Jade Emperor’s law-speech—
*The path is severed, the Dao is cut off,*
*Subtle and unfathomable—*
What cause is there for doubt?
It is the root of all divine power,
Pacifying the land, liberating beings from birth and death—
This is its natural effect.

**Dispelling Doubts:**
There is no one outside the Dao, nor is there a Dao outside humanity.
All beings, bright or obscure, are the Dao itself.
Human nature is fully true;
All things are complete within it.
All transformations and nurturing,
The beginning and end of the world—
All are the true essence of my nature.

The Jade Emperor is the Dao-body;
The scripture is the Dao’s intent.
Only through the Dao is divine efficacy and transformation complete,
Mystery and nature inherently perfect.
Humans share the same essence—
How could they not uphold the scripture?

Know that the Dao resides within—
With a single mind, embodying the Dao,
Through all lifetimes without division,
Then the Saints and True Ones are already within me.

---

**Chapter Nine of Protection and Upholding**

Then, the Celestial Worthy spoke this gatha:

*The Jade Emperor’s merit is vast,*
*The Mystic Principle profoundly deep.*
*Born before the Great Calamity,*
*Transforming through ancient and modern times.*
*Now I expound this wondrous scripture,*
*Out of compassion for all sentient beings.*
*This is indeed the most wondrous law,*
*The merit of merits supreme.*
*The name is the highest vehicle,*
*Unmatched, the first of all.*

*The Radiant Sovereign of Great Light,*
*Whose virtue and power are rare in the world,*
*Can shatter violent evil demons,*
*And make all hearts submit in surrender.*
*Can extinguish the gravest crimes,*
*And grant all purity.*

*If one hears this scripture,*
*Or hears the Emperor’s wondrous name,*
*And bows in reverence,*
*All sins are annihilated.*

*The Ten Evils and Four Grave Offenses,*
*Even matricide and patricide—*
*With sincere faith, a single invocation,*
*All vanish with the sound.*

*Protecting humans and celestial beings,*
*The Four Calamities and Five Decays,*
*The Three Realms’ gravest sufferings,*
*Mundane human misfortunes,*
*Years of famine, pestilence, and death,*
*Poisons, nightmares, and malevolent spirits,*
*Lawsuits, wrongful accusations,*
*Warfare and battlefield torments,*
*Perils in mountains and forests,*
*Tigers, leopards, wolves, and their kind,*
*The venomous red seas and dragon-kind,*
*Swift lightning, wind, hail, and storms,*
*Fires, floods, thieves, and robbers,*
*Internal poisons and treacherous plots,*
*Madness and loss of reason,*
*Snakes, scorpions, and venomous insects,*
*Malevolent demons and monstrous spirits,*
*Those who lurk for human harm—*
*By holding this true scripture,*
*All such evils universally disperse and vanish.*

*Chronic illnesses, lingering and tormenting,*
*Even in dreams, no peace is found,*
*Unnatural desires that drain life—*
*These perish without blame.*

*Through encountering this scripture,*
*One attains security and freedom.*
*All desires and aspirations—*
*Wealth, treasures, and noble status—*
*Through this scripture’s merit,*
*All are fulfilled as one wishes.*

The Celestial Sovereign of Divine Might and Freedom,
The Eleven Luminaries of the Celestial Hosts,
The Thirty-two Heavenly Lords,
The Twenty-eight Constellations of Stars,
The Spirit Consorts and Jade Maidens and their kind,
Celestial Deities and Earthly Spirits,
The Gods of the Three Realms and Void,
The Dragon Kings of rivers and seas,
The Spirits of Water, Fire, and Wind,
Palaces and dwellings, mountains and forests,
Trees and all their kind,
The Spirits of ditches, canals, wells, and springs—
By holding this true scripture,
All shall protect and defend.

Clothing and food come naturally,
Children and descendants attain wealth and nobility.
Words spoken are rare and revered,
Wherever one goes, all honor and respect.

If one seeks sons or daughters,
By reciting this true scripture,
An imperial edict descends to the Celestial Bureau,
Registering them as Heavenly Immortals,
Descending to be born in their family,
To become their sons or daughters.

Nobles and the eminent hold them in high regard,
The Seven Ancestors ascend in rank.
The family’s glory shines brightly,
Extending blessings to parents and kin.
Constant auspiciousness thrives unceasingly,
Disasters and calamities cannot intrude.

Thus, I now proclaim—
The assembly must listen with earnest attention.
With boundless compassion, all are led to the Highest Purity.

The following verses were spoken by the Primordial Celestial Venerable:

*The Jade Emperor’s virtue is vast,*
*The Mysterious Principle profound and deep.*
*Born before the Great Calamity,*
*Manifesting through ancient and modern ages.*
*I, the Primordial, now speak this wondrous scripture,*
*Out of pity for all sentient beings,*
*The highest virtue among virtues,*
*The unparalleled wondrous law,*
*The foremost Mysterious Mechanism.*

*The Radiant Sovereign of Great Light,*
*Light infinite, the Awakened King Supreme.*
*Might and virtue rare in the world,*
*Mysterious Might and Marvelous Virtue—*
*The world cannot compare.*

*The Ten Evils and Fourfold Heavy Sins,*
*The Fourfold Heavy Sins—some say: Demon, Prison, Ghost, Beast.*
*Others say: Struck by lightning, plague, thieves, and prisons.*
*The Five Grievous Offenses against parents.*
*As Mencius said, the Five Unfilial Acts:*
*Laziness in limbs, indulging in gambling and drink,*
*Greed for wealth, favoring one’s own wife and children,*
*Following ear and eye desires,*
*To the point of killing one’s parents,*
*Or reckless bravery endangering them.*
*Others say: Lack of sincerity, filial piety, obedience, and propriety—these are the Five Offenses.*

*With faith, invoking the Emperor’s name,*
*Crimes vanish with each utterance.*

*The Five Decays:*
*The crown of pearls shatters, the body bends,*
*The head bows, eyes dim, nose leaks,*
*The body loses luster,*
*The Celestial Robe is tattered,*
*The shadow is exposed,*
*The spirit’s movement becomes sluggish.*
*These are the signs of fate’s convergence.*

*Kluster (克家): When past karma meets its due.*
*Derzhin (迅): Swift as lightning.*
*Bao (雹): Hail, icy rain.*
*Si (伺): Lurking in darkness to harm others.*
*Those who harm themselves through unnatural desires—*
*They perish utterly, not as misfortune.*

*The Four Directions, the Eight, and the Thirty-two Heavenly Lords.*
*Those who hold this scripture speak in Mysterious Marvels,*
*Words rare and revered,*
*Wherever they go, all honor them with sincere respect.*

*The Seven Ancestors:*
*The father, grandfather, great-grandfather, high-ancestor,*
*The ancestral root, the ancestor who opened the forest,*
*The ancestor who established the surname—these are the Seven Ancestors.*

*Fluxing Victory (炽胜): Great radiance and display.*
*With boundless compassion, all are led to the Highest Purity,*
*The Great Luo Realm.*

*This verse extols the Jade Emperor’s virtue in the Jade Scripture,*
*Urging all to revere and uphold it.*

**Chapter Ten: Protection and Upholding**

Thus, the Celestial Venerable addressed the Four Assemblies:
*"For mortals who hold and recite this scripture,*
*Who receive and invoke the Emperor’s name,*
*All are rooted deeply in the Dao,*
*With past merits of kindness.*
*This scripture is sublime and noble,*
*Universal salvation for Heaven and humanity.*
*With sincere devotion, families and nations prosper,*
*Life is preserved, disasters averted,*
*All inauspiciousness is swept away.*

*When kings and nobles uphold it,*
*The land achieves great peace,*
*Bandits and rebels are subdued,*
*Borderlands remain undisturbed,*
*The people sing in joy,*
*All under Heaven thrives,*
*Fate’s cycles turn favorably,*
*The True Way prevails.*
*Those who possess it are held in reverence by the Celestial Worthies.*
*It is a treasure to be guarded in secrecy."*

Thus, the Primordial Celestial Venerable addressed the Four Assemblies:

*"All mortals in this world who hold and recite this scripture, receiving and invoking the Sacred Emperor’s name, are deeply rooted in the Dao—just as the Confucian sage speaks of innate endowment pure and profound, or as the Buddhist speaks of favorable roots and capacity. They bear past merits of kindness, having in former ages and past kalpas broadly cultivated hidden virtue, already possessing auspicious connections.

For the True Way is difficult to hear, the Dharma Assembly rare to encounter, and the blessed night even rarer to meet. Some have lived through ages without hearing the True Dharma; some hear yet do not believe or awaken, failing to grasp it fully or reap its true benefit. These are those whose roots and capacity are shallow, whose karmic connections are thin.

Now, in this Dharma Assembly, hearing the True Dharma and receiving its true benefit—all have through countless kalpas cultivated the Dao, their roots deeply established, their past merits profound. This scripture is sublime and noble, universally saving Heaven and humanity. But with sincere devotion, reverent offering, and humble veneration of this scripture, families and nations achieve peace, life is preserved and disasters averted, longevity secured and calamities dispelled.

The ancient sages and worthies had birth and death, faced disasters and misfortune—how could they claim to preserve life and avert disasters?
