Rather, they preserved the Heavenly Mandate and maintained true *qi*, enduring trials with daily ease, meeting death with serenity, finding no distinction between joy and sorrow. This is the true meaning of preserving life and averting disasters through the scripture.

It sweeps away all inauspiciousness—where the scripture’s power resides, all calamities vanish in secret. The virtuous receive Heaven’s favor, and all disasters are forever removed, leaving no trace of ill fortune.

As for kings and nobles: the sovereign of all under Heaven is called the *Son of Heaven* (天子), the *Emperor* (皇), or the *Sage Emperor* (帝). In the Zhou, they were called *Kings* (王). In later times, a feudal lord ruling a single state is called a *King* (王), and a vassal holding a fief is called a *Marquess* (侯). In antiquity, a marquess ruled over a hundred *li*.

Those who uphold this scripture bring their nation’s lineage to great peace. Bandits and rebels are naturally subdued—*subdued* meaning pacified. When a land follows the Dao, internal harmony and external might prevail; wicked rebels and bandits do not rise, and the four borderlands submit in tribute, all under Heaven at ease, with no wars on the frontiers. The common folk sing in joy, the land prosperous and at peace, all under Heaven flourishing.

The celestial cycles turn favorably, the *Zhenyuan* era’s auspicious rotation complete, the natural order restored. Those who possess this Dharma and embody its transformative power are held in reverence by the Celestial Worthies. It is a treasure to be guarded in secrecy—though the Great Dao universally saves all, the unworthy should not be given it lightly. The Buddha’s *True Dharma Eye Treasury* is not casually revealed to all. Confucius said: ‘Those of mediocre or lesser capacity cannot be taught the highest truths.’ True understanding must come from the heart. To treat it lightly is to profane the Heavenly.

The scripture says *guard it in secrecy*—let those who observe it understand its meaning on their own.

---

**Chapter Five: The Manifestation of Retribution and Verification**

At that time, the Four Venerable Ones—Compassionate Transcendence of Calamities, Seeking-Voice Savior of Suffering, Life-Saving Death-Transcending, and Ten-Thousand Blessings Body-Protecting—all rose from their seats, stepping beyond their ranks, and together addressed the Celestial Venerable:

*'In the latter ages, though mortals may bear past merits and encounter this scripture, if obstructed by malevolent influences—whether from their own heretical views, others’ deceptive teachings, perverse natures, or the hindrances of circumstance and principle—they remain doubtful from beginning to end, unable to believe in this scripture’s virtues. Such persons, in this life and future lives, will suffer what retributive punishments in the hells? We humbly pray the Saintly Compassion may explain the agonies of their retributive realms of suffering.'*

The Four Venerable Ones—Compassionate Transcendence of Calamities, Seeking-Voice Savior of Suffering, Life-Saving Death-Transcending, and Ten-Thousand Blessings Body-Protecting—all rose from their seats, stepping beyond the ranks of the gods, and together addressed the Primordial Celestial Venerable:

*'In the latter ages, though mortals may bear past merits and encounter this scripture, if obstructed by malevolent influences—whether from their own heretical views, others’ deceptive teachings, perverse natures, or the hindrances of circumstance and principle—they remain doubtful from beginning to end, unable to believe in this scripture’s virtues. Such persons, in this life and future lives, will suffer what retributive punishments in the hells? We humbly pray the Saintly Compassion, the Celestial Venerable, may explain the agonies of their retributive realms of suffering.'*

All beings bear karmic consciousness, each drawn to their own inclinations—whether good or evil, endlessly cycling through rebirth, unable to escape. The Great Saints and Perfect Ones transcend past habits, uproot defilements, purify consciousness and karma, sever all realms of existence, and with all obstructions removed, suffer no retribution or rebirth.

The great bodhisattvas, minor immortals, minor saints, divine generals, and ghostly spirits—those of virtue take cultivation as their path, those of vice are bound by their deeds. Virtuous beings need no further mention; the wicked, however, sink into their karmic prisons, their retributions endless, with no escape or remedy. When their karma is exhausted, they are reborn elsewhere, only to be dragged again by karmic ties, lost in delusion, wandering through kalpas without end. Such is their karmic fate—truly pitiful.

The Four Venerable Ones, moved by great compassion, implored the Celestial Venerable to speak of these retributive sufferings.

Now, regarding the teachings on retribution: Confucian scholars deny it not. *Tai Jia* said: *"When Heaven inflicts calamity, it may still be averted; when a man brings calamity upon himself, there is no escape."* The classics say: *"Reward the virtuous, punish the licentious."* And again: *"The responses of Heaven and man are swift as echoes."* How could they deny retribution?

The Master said: *"The gentleman cherishes the penal codes."* And again: *"Fear the Heavenly Mandate."* Thus, he does not himself do evil. When Dao and righteousness delight the heart, there is no other path.

In past dynasties, at the *xiangyin* and archery rites, they taught the people through lectures on law and order, guiding them not by coercion but by nurturing their inherent goodness.

「The teachings of both Dao and Buddhism on retribution and penal codes serve only to uproot their karmic inclinations and lead them toward great virtue. Alas! Only the sage, through divine instruction and governance, commands the reverence of all.

The Jade Emperor’s merit and virtue are supreme, hence the scriptures clearly demonstrate retribution to rescue beings from evil paths, never deceiving the multitude. If one does not cultivate the True Dao, but merely dazzles others with talk of reward and punishment, this is to deceive them. Those who study the scriptures must renounce desire and attain the True Dao to escape personal retribution and suffering, only then can they save and guide the world.

The *Yingying* [應驗] chapters continue with twelve more sections. At that time, the Heavenly Sage addressed the Four True Ones [四真人], saying: *"If there are beings in the world who are obstinate, fierce, and cruel—unbenevolent creatures whose speech and deeds harm all beings—who day and night face the Daoist images without reverence, uttering blasphemous words, they shall incur the crime of falling into the Five Boundless [五無間] Prisons.*

If they encounter one who holds this scripture, who employs all means to persuade, guide, and rescue them, then such beings—able to extinguish their evil thoughts, take faith in this scripture, and purify all their crimes without remainder—shall be redeemed. At that time, the Original Heavenly Sage addressed the Four True Ones of Compassionate Salvation and Deliverance [慈悲度厄等四真人], saying:

*"If there are beings in the world who are obstinate, fierce, and cruel—those bold and coarse in name, unbenevolent beings whose speech and deeds harm all beings—who day and night face the Daoist images without reverence, uttering blasphemous words, they shall incur the crime of falling into the Five Boundless [五無間] Prisons. The Five Prisons are the great penal realms of the Underworld; non-sages have no recourse, thus they fall into these crimes. Observe the solar laws [陽律] for blasphemous slander, and you shall know the gravity of slandering the divine.

If they encounter one who holds this scripture, who employs all means to save and guide them, then those who defy the divine and slander the scriptures have deep-rooted karmic tendencies, clinging stubbornly to their delusions, lacking faith. The scripture-holder, through boundless compassion and skillful means, awakens, persuades, and leads them, revealing their true nature, fostering benevolent thoughts. Thus, those who defy the divine and slander the scriptures, if they extinguish all their evil thoughts, take faith in this scripture, and devote themselves wholly to it, shall have their crimes purified without remainder. Their karmic debts shall be erased, retribution fulfilled, and they shall forever be free from transgression, never returning to cyclic suffering, always pure and clear, with evil retribution forever removed and no unresolved karmic debts remaining.

The Five Boundless [五無間] hells—where crimes are difficult to purify—if one steadfastly takes faith in the True Scriptures, the evil roots shall be severed, all defilements extinguished, and what bonds remain? The roots and defilements shall be utterly destroyed, with no karmic residue. The divine virtue and scriptural efficacy are the greatest benefits; both Dao and Buddhism emphasize crimes of retribution, sternly warning against defying the divine and slandering the scriptures.

Confucian scholars often admonish irreverence toward spirits and gods—does this mean Confucians do not revere the divine or honor scriptures? The *Book of Odes* states: *"Do not disgrace your birth."* Master Zhang [張子] says: *"To not fear the gods peering through the roof beams is to disgrace your birth."* Again, it says: *"Cultivate the heart and nurture the nature, without negligence."* The teachings of both Dao and Buddhism speak of revering the divine, honoring the scriptures, and fostering the heart to cultivate the Dao, never falling short in devotion to Heaven, Earth, and the divine, and embodying the scriptures’ truth.

Confucians teach that one should not flatter the gods, warning only against seeking rewards through improper reverence. Serving Heaven means fearing Heaven’s mandate, aspiring to Heaven’s will, and honoring the teachings of the ancient kings, with solemn respect like a swift-chariot race or a galloping steed—Confucianism and the two teachings are one in this regard. If sacrifices bring no benefit, reverence is insufficient, and the mandate of Heaven is not to be feared, these are hollow words. Confucian scholars also condemn them sternly—why single out the other two traditions?

Alas! Benevolence and malevolence, reverence and neglect, all arise from the heart. If one can sever emotional desires, abandon worldly perceptions, empty the Five Aggregates [五蘊], and remove the Five Fetters [五累], then one shall not be bound by the Five Elements [五行], nor by Heaven and Earth, and the Five Boundless [五無間] Prisons shall not touch them. The Buddha says: *"To chant the Buddha’s name transforms the fiery pit into a lotus pond."* Mencius says: *"To recite the words of Yao and follow Yao’s deeds is to be Yao himself."* Thus, the true efficacy of virtue and goodness is immediately manifest.

The *Imperial Canon with Commentaries* [皇經集注] concludes Volume Eight and begins Volume Nine.»

**Chapter Thirteen of the *Verification Section* (Continued)**

If there be one with perverse views, foolish obstinacy, and malevolent intent—who, upon seeing this scripture held, gives rise to all manner of hostility—with sidelong, malevolent glances, even to the point of harboring a single evil thought or uttering a single evil word, and falsely slandering those who uphold this scripture, then his guilt is profound and grave. When his life expires, he shall fall into the Great Earthly Prison, with no hope of release.

Not only is the crime of blaspheming the sacred and slandering the scripture grave. If there be one with perverse views, foolish and muddled, ensnared in delusion—who, upon seeing those who recite this scripture (for *sight* is *seeing*), harbors doubt and disbelief—then he fails to recognize that this scripture is the Dao’s true words, its laws, and its teachings. He holds it in contempt, belittles it, and in aversion, slanders and defames it. He gives rise to transgressions and rebellious deeds, casting sidelong, askew glances, taking no pleasure in seeing the scripture or those who uphold it. He lacks the steadfast, pure gaze of right observation, but instead fixes his gaze with malice, scorns and despises it, even to the point of harboring a single evil thought or uttering a single evil word, falsely slandering those who uphold this scripture.

*Slander* is both praise and defamation. To uphold the scripture and do good cannot be defamed. Yet those with perverse fixation and malice, ignorant of the karmic causes of guilt and merit, unaware of the virtue of holding this scripture, falsely give rise to slanderous, abusive words against those who uphold it. Their guilt is profound and grave.

When his life is *exhausted*—for *exhausted* means *ended*—

Falling into the Great Hell—**Avīci**—the **Uninterrupted Prison**, with no term for release. *Permanent* means *eternal*, *endless*. Through false slander of the True Dharma, the karmic roots are profound and heavy; thus, one falls into hell and finds it difficult to escape.

For **cognition** is singular. If perception is not upright, it becomes perverse. Humanity is singular; if one clings in delusion and fails to awaken, one becomes **foolish**, becomes **evil**. The heart is singular; if it gives rise to malevolent thoughts, it becomes **rebellious**. The eyes are singular; if they gaze askew, it becomes **transgression**. A single thought, though minute, is singular—if one harbors a single evil intention, it becomes the root of karmic cause. A single word, though few, is singular—if one utters a single evil speech, it becomes the origin of sin.

The **Noble One** perfects the singular virtue, praises others’ goodness, and those who uphold the scripture should be commended. Yet to falsely give rise to slander is to invite calamity upon oneself. Human life originally has no inherent karmic debt—one incurs guilt through self-inflicted transgression, and this is truly lamentable.

When life is *exhausted*—for *exhausted* means *ended*—one returns to the cycle of transformation, bound by no fixed constraint. Yet even a single instance of slandering the Dharma casts one into the Great Hell, where death itself brings no peace. How then can one escape without end?

Heaven’s heart is benevolent and loving; the **Supreme Sovereign** cherishes life, and the **Divine** is just, not drowning the people. Yet those who commit crimes with no hope of release—is this Heaven’s imprisonment? The calamity is self-made; fixed karma cannot be evaded. To eliminate one’s own karmic debt, one must rely on self-rectification. If one steadfastly pursues the utmost goodness, the karmic roots will be severed.

Alas! The punishments of hell are Heaven’s retribution; the law is impartial—no father can shield his son, nor a filial child spare his parent. The Divine is utterly just; how could it erase self-inflicted karmic consequences?

If one takes refuge in the scripture and turns toward the Dharma, sincerely repents past transgressions—just as a worldly person who surrenders in truth may be spared their crime—then one may escape.

In this mortal life, the wise and foolish differ not in essence. If one cannot speak with measured words, let one’s voice conform to the **Laws**; yet do not utter falsehoods as **evil speech**. If one cannot act without fault, let one’s body be the **Measure**; yet do not commit **evil deeds** and incur bodily karmic debt. If one cannot keep the mind free from delusion, guarding the **Ultimate Truth**, then do not give rise to malevolent intentions and incur mental karmic debt.

If one does not know the **Great Dao**, do not slander the **Way**; if one does not understand the scripture, do not contradict it; if one cannot recite and uphold it, do not slander others; if one does not comprehend the **ghostly**, **life and death**, **cause and effect**, do not give rise to destructive speech. With a single mind of upright faith, one will gradually illuminate the **One Dao**, becoming a **Sage of Truth**—what karmic guilt could then remain?

---
**Verification Chapter (Continuation of the Fourteen Chapters)**

As for men and women in this world who encounter this scripture yet do not generate reverence, defiling it with unclean hands, reading aloud with a **polluted mouth**—one who has consumed the **Five Impurities** and **Five Spices**, or who places it upon an impure bed or seat—such treatment is utterly improper. Or if one recites this scripture while engaging in idle conversation, laughing and jesting as if it were a mundane text, treating it as a common classic—such a person, after death, falls into the **Uninterrupted Prison**, with no term for release. Their suffering extends to their **Nine Ancestors**, subjecting them to the **Tribunal of the Underworld**, entangling their descendants and harming future generations.

In hell, they endure unimaginable torments across countless **kalpas**. Even if they encounter sacred teachings and are repeatedly rescued, their sins diminish only slightly. If they then meet the **Supreme Sage’s special grace**, they may escape hell and be reborn as a **Hungry Ghost**, enduring for thousands of millions of **kalpas** without even hearing the name of **porridge**. Once their ghostly karmic debt is exhausted, they are reborn among **Animals**, and upon fulfilling that debt, if they are reborn as humans, they are cast into **barbaric lands**, reduced to **female form**, plagued by poverty, suffering, deformity, and countless diseases. They endure unbearable torments, despised by all, neither able to live nor die. This is the retribution for treating this scripture with contempt.

This is the **uttermost consequence of disrespecting the scripture**. To fail to generate reverence means to lack **respect, admiration, and veneration**. To defile it with unclean hands means to handle or point to the scripture with impure hands. To recite with a **polluted mouth** is to read while one’s mouth is tainted by the **Five Impurities** and **Five Spices**, or by the **Three Taboos**. To place it upon an impure bed or seat means to rest the scripture upon an unclean couch, table, or platform. Or to recite this scripture while speaking in **vulgar language**, laughing and jesting as if it were a trivial text—such a person not only incurs their own karmic retribution but also brings calamity upon their **Nine Ancestors**: the **First Ancestor**, the **Four昭 (Zhāo)**, and the **Four穆 (Mù)**.

They are subjected to the **Tribunal of the Underworld**—either **investigated for their transgressions** or **tortured**—as lesser spirits punish the household head for offenses. Their suffering extends to their descendants, entangling future generations. A family burdened with misdeeds faces additional calamity, enduring great torment and boundless affliction. Even if they encounter sacred teachings and are repeatedly rescued, their sins diminish only slightly—this is the merit of the scripture’s power reducing their guilt. If they then meet the **Supreme Sage’s special grace**, the **Divine’s pardon**, they may escape hell’s torments. As **Hungry Ghosts**, they suffer for thousands of millions of **kalpas**, their throats too narrow to swallow even the name of **porridge**. Once their ghostly karmic debt is exhausted, they are reborn among **Animals**, their karmic burden still unresolved.

Though humanity is singular, one may struggle to be reborn in **China**, let alone as a **male**. Instead, they are cast into **barbaric lands**, reduced to **female form**—the least favored state among humans. They endure **poverty, cold, hunger, and hardship**, **deformity, disease, and endless suffering**, despised by all. They neither attain birth nor escape death, all because they treated this scripture with contempt. To incur such grave karmic guilt—how lamentable!

Human life is a participant in the **Three Powers of Heaven and Earth**, this body precious, relying on it to honor ancestors and benefit descendants, transmitting the **Dao** and sustaining what is entrusted—its weight is not slight. Yet to disrespect the scripture and the Dharma brings suffering upon oneself, entangles one’s ancestors, and dooms future generations. To endure such karmic retribution—how utterly foolish!

Again, examining the scriptures of the **Three Teachings**, it is said that the **fundamental nature** of male and female is undifferentiated—everywhere, in all places, they are lands of **bliss**. The *Zhongyong* states:

*"In wealth or poverty, in high or low station, in peace or adversity,
To act in accordance with one’s proper place—
Then one finds contentment in all circumstances."*

Yet now it speaks of those in **foreign lands** as female forms, bearing bodies of **sickness and hardship**, despised by all—why is this so?

It is because the **undifferentiated** attain **self-realization**—this is the **Dao**.
To distinguish by ranks and speak of **guilt and reward**—this is **retribution**.
When retribution is clear, then people will strive to do good.

Alas! Humans are all the same—all may become virtuous beings.
Strive earnestly to advance the **Way**, avoid **karmic offenses**, lest you become an object of hatred.

**Continuation of the *Yinying* Chapter (Chapter 15):**

There are yet others who, though initially **faithful and receptive**, later grow **neglectful and careless**. The **Children of Virtue and Vice** then report them to the **Three Officials**, their names recorded in the **Black Ledger**, their merits subtracted from the **Blue Register**. After death, they are confined to **dark prisons**, wandering the **Three Realms** without escape.

Some, in this very life, suffer **various diseases**—**scabies, leprosy, carbuncles, and ulcers**—as their **fruit of retribution**. They are tormented by **grief and anguish**, day and night.

Or they are **slain by violence**, or imprisoned in chains, or meet **untimely death** by poison. Some are devoured by **tigers, wolves, venomous snakes**, or dragged by **grievous debts**. Some, wandering in forests, are **murdered by bandits** and cast into ravines. Others are **harmed by malevolent spirits and demons**, or perish in **fires and floods**, or are **slaughtered by blades and weapons**.

Because they **despised this scripture**, their lives are cut short in **premature death**, reaping such **fruit**, such **retribution**—how can one not grieve?
How can one not lament?

The **benefits of this scripture’s law** are not merely for those who **utterly reject faith**. There are also those who, though initially **faithful without doubt**, later grow **remiss and careless**. The **Children of Virtue and Vice**—those who record the **good and evil deeds of mortals**—report them to the **Three Officials**, their names inscribed in the **Black Ledger**.

The **Black Ledger** records **transgressions**.
It records the **guilt of neglecting sacred scriptures**.
The **Blue Register** subtracts the **merits** of those who **despise the scriptures**. After death, they are **imprisoned in dark dungeons**, bound in **judicial chains**, wandering the **Three Realms** in endless suffering, with no means of liberation.

The **karmic fruits** of this life may manifest as **various afflictions**—**scabies, leprosy, festering sores, and malignant diseases**—as **retribution for past misdeeds**. **Anxiety, sorrow, and torment** assail them day and night, **grinding them in despair**. Or they may suffer **sudden calamities and misfortunes**, **imprisonment in chains**, or **untimely death by their own hand**. Or they may be **maimed by poison**, **devoured by tigers, wolves, or venomous serpents**. Or they may be **dragged into ruin by creditors**, or **slain by bandits in the wilderness**, **thrown from cliffs**, their bodies and lives shattered. Or they may be **harmed by malevolent spirits and demons**. Or they may perish in **fires or floods**, or be **slaughtered by blades and spears**. Through **neglect of this scripture**, they **meet a premature end**, **cut down in their prime**, **dying without fulfillment**.

To suffer such **karmic consequences**, to endure such **retribution**—how can one not grieve? How can one not lament?

When one **laments their suffering**, one also **regrets their folly**—this is the **great compassion of the Celestial Sage**.

**Verification of Doubt:**
He who **later grows remiss and careless** toward this scripture shall face **endless punishments**. Thus, one must **revere the Dao and uphold the scriptures**, **treasuring constancy**. When the **Dao’s transformation is complete**, the **scripture’s efficacy is fulfilled**, and all shall **reap its virtue**, **attaining its effects**.

Yet humans lack constancy—**diligent at first, slack at last**—so it is no wonder that **guilt and misdeeds befall them**. From ancient times to now, the **unworthy have always existed**; many **do not uphold the scripture**, many **have never heard it**, yet those who suffer **guilt and calamities are countless**. Are they all **those who despise the scripture**?

The scripture **speaks of the Dao**; if one **does not believe in the Dao**, they lack **virtue**—this is **despising the scripture**. Without virtue, there is **guilt**—this is the **sin of despising the scripture**. To **honor the scripture and dissolve guilt**, one must **advance in the Dao and cultivate virtue**.

**Continuation of the Verification Chapter (16):**
You must **earnestly follow** this and **practice it diligently**, **generating no wicked thoughts**. If **all thoughts cease**, all **worldly ties are extinguished**; **dust-like malevolent deeds** vanish with the mind, and **all disasters and demons are naturally eradicated**.

This scripture’s **merits and virtues are beyond measure**—**truly the supreme, matchless, wondrous law**, the **king of all scriptures**, with **great benefit**. **Do not reveal it to the unworthy.**

The Celestial Sage said to the **True Ones**:
*"The retribution for despising the scripture is as such. You must **earnestly and sincerely** follow this scripture’s law without fail, **generating no wicked thoughts.** If **all impure thoughts do not arise**, neither **good nor evil**, neither **non-thought nor non-non-thought**, all **worldly ties are extinguished**—

**Emptying the Five Bonds**, **clearing the Nine Consciousnesses**, **transcending the Four Symbols**, **severing the Hundred Defilements**, **emptying the Ten Thousand Phenomena**, **annihilating the One Mind**—**external ties, internal ties, karmic ties, ties of fortune**—all **empty, pure, and wondrous**—**past lives, present lives, clinging to the future**—**all are severed**. **All roots and dust are exhausted**; **dust-like malevolent deeds** vanish with the mind.

The **dust of the world**, like the **sands of the Ganges**, is **incalculable**. Thus, **all such deeds**, with the **faith in this scripture**, **are all dissolved**. **All disasters and demons are naturally eradicated**; **all calamities and demons are utterly destroyed**.

This scripture’s **merits and virtues are beyond measure**—**truly the supreme, matchless, wondrous law**. **All Three Teachings, all laws—none can compare**. This is **truly the supreme, wondrous law**, the **king of all scriptures**, the **scripture of the Two Gates**. **All other books—even those of the Confucian scholars—fall short**. It is the **king of all Three Teachings’ scriptures**, with **great benefit**. **Do not reveal it to the unworthy.**

Though the **Dao may be learned by all**, it **cannot be transmitted to those without faith or reverence**. **Do not reveal it to the unworthy**; **do not transmit it to those who do not hold the Dao in high regard.**

**Resolution of Doubt:**
The **Confucian scholars do not instruct the self-destructive**. The **Buddha does not enlighten the unworthy**. The **Dao’s law is most exalted**—how could it be **forced upon the faithless?**

Alas! **Faith is the foundation for advancing in the Dao**; **true resolve is essential for attaining sainthood**. Without faith, one **cannot be entrusted with the scripture**. **Humans must strive with utmost sincerity**, making it the **root of receiving the scripture and entering sainthood.**

**Continuation of the Verification Chapter (17):**
If **celestial beings and humans**, facing the **Five Decays and Four Phases of Decline**, are **beset by the wheel of rebirth**, yet **abandon all delusions** and **uphold this scripture**, they will **naturally attract blessings**, **fortifying their celestial fortune**, **transcending the Three Realms**, and **abiding with the Dao eternally**.

This scripture is **most exalted**—**it should not be recklessly revealed to all**.

If **celestial beings and humans** of the **Six Desire Realms** still **cling to sensual pleasures**, those of the **Eighteen Color Realms** **retain colored forms**, those of the **Four Formless Realms** **find bliss in emptiness**, and those of the **Four Great Brahmas**—though **knowing emptiness and non-existence**, lacking **hopes of delight**—yet **enjoy tranquil blessings in measure**—all these **celestial realms**, though **differing in kind**, are **inferior to the Four Celestial Kindreds**, who **know no rebirth or decay**.

The **Five Decays** have been explained before. The **Four Phases** refer to:
- The **decline of non-humans, humans, beings, and long-lived ones** in **fortune and virtue** (four phases).
- Or **birth, vigor, old age, and exhaustion** (four phases).
- Or **lack of dignity, lack of supernatural powers, lack of joy, lack of vitality** (four phases).

The **wheel of rebirth presses upon them**—the **thirty-two heavens of Desire, Form, Brahmas, and Formlessness**, differing in **duration**. When their **celestial blessings are exhausted**, they **reincarnate into the mortal world**, each with **fixed destiny**—hence, **"rebirth."**

**Abandoning all delusions** means:
Delusion arises from **clinging to worldly ties**—whether **coveting blessings, wisdom, longevity, emptiness, meditation, ascension, or descent**. What the **eyes cannot see**, what the **mind cannot exhaust**—all are **delusion**. To **abandon all thoughts**, to **let no single tie arise**, to **be empty of emptiness**—this is **abandoning illusory thoughts**.

When **delusion is abandoned**, one **naturally attracts blessings**; **celestial fortune is fortified**—**without seeking, blessings come naturally**.

The **Four Realms**—Desire, Form, Formless, and Brahmalokas—each **allows one to transcend from their own abode**.

**No longer subject to rebirth**, they **suffer no ruin or decline**, achieving **great firmness and stability**, never entering the cycle of rebirth.

**Liberating the body from the Three Realms**:
To **exit the Desire Realm**, ascend to the Form Realm, and further reach the Formless and Brahmalokas—**transcending the Three Realms of existence** (samsara)—one **soars beyond the forms of heaven, earth, and humanity**, attaining the **lofty, mysterious heights**.

**Eternal alongside the Dao**:
In **harmony with the Dao**, they **endure through boundless ages**. Observing the **transformative power of celestial and human scriptures**, one may **grasp the truth**.

**Exhortation**: The **Eighteen Chapters of the *Yingpin* Sutra** are this very scripture—**unmatched and unsurpassable**, possessing **great awe-inspiring virtue and power**, a **mighty divine spell**—capable of **reviving withered branches and leaves**, making **flowers and fruits flourish abundantly**. It can **banish the most profound suffering and afflictions of all beings**, and **grant long life to those with short spans**.

This scripture’s **merits and virtues are beyond reckoning**, praise **cannot exhaust them**.

For those who **do not believe in this scripture**, their **karma is thus**; for **celestial and human beings who trust it**, its **effects are thus**. This scripture is **unmatched and unsurpassable**; all other **sutras and teachings** fall beneath it, **none equal**, **none superior**. All benefits of other scriptures and teachings **cannot compare** to this, **none surpass it**.

This is **great awe-inspiring virtue and power**—**either eliminating evil or supporting the true**. If a teaching **cannot both eliminate evil and extinguish sins while upholding the true and perfecting virtue**, it **does not qualify as awe-inspiring virtue and power**. Yet this scripture’s **law both eliminates evil and eradicates offenses**, **strengthens the true and fulfills virtue**—its **divine efficacy and wondrous merits are immeasurable**, hence it is called **awe-inspiring virtue and power**.

As for its **mighty divine spell**, see the earlier explanation. It can **revive withered branches and leaves**, making **flowers and fruits flourish abundantly**. All **grasses, trees, rare flowers, uncommon vegetables, auspicious fungi, and sacred incense**—whatever **cannot thrive and grow naturally**—and all **dried, withered, or damaged plants**, this scripture **restores to life, sprouting branches and leaves**, **blossoms and fruits**, **flourishing and multiplying abundantly**.

It can **banish the most profound suffering and afflictions of all beings**. This scripture **dissolves all karma**, benefiting **living beings**; **extracts all sins**, benefiting **the dying**. It **removes demonic calamities**, **secures human happiness**. Through **countless ages of karmic retribution and desire**, or **lifelong vexation and torment**, the **heaviest suffering endured across generations**—this scripture **eradicates their very roots**.

It can **grant long life to those with short spans**. Among mortals, **seventy years is rare**. This scripture **preserves life and extends vitality**, enabling **those who die young or live briefly** to **calculate and prolong their years**, achieving **long life**.

Some say, **"Yanzi, the second Sage, lived only thirty years—this proves that Daoist virtue/power (德) brings no benefit. Why claim that this scripture extends life?"** Yet **true longevity is not dying**. Yanzi, **suddenly enlightened**, **did not die**. The scripture speaks of **extending the life of those with short spans**, meaning it **allows beings to attain enlightenment and thus not die**.

This scripture’s **merits and virtues are beyond reckoning**, praise **cannot exhaust them**. Its **glory is endless**.

Ah, the loyalty and righteousness of Lord Ke—his virtue stands like bamboo groves after the axe;
the filial piety and brotherly love of the Tian clan—his descendants revive like chaste plants reborn.

When the Sage rules above, even common households may be ennobled—life and death bring swift joy.
To attain the fullness of the Great Dao is to encompass all beings in virtue and power without distinction.

Let those who study this scripture strive earnestly—its highest merit is self-attained.

**The Chapter of Manifestations (续十九章):**
If one has not in past lives cultivated the Dao’s root,
or sown fields of merit broadly,
even the name of this scripture may go unheard—
how much less could one hope to see it?

The scripture’s virtue and power are boundless.

If one has not in past lives cultivated the Dao’s root—
the root is like the foundation.
The gentleman attends to the foundation,
for when the foundation stands, the Dao arises—
thus it is called *Dao-ben* (道本).
Some mistakenly call it *Dao-zhong* (道种)—this is incorrect.
*Host* (宿) means *previously* or *in advance*;
*plant* (植) means *establish*, *nurture*, or *sow*.
The Dao’s root is the gradual cultivation of the fundamental path.

The Dao scriptures say: *The Great Dao is nameless—*
through precise cultivation, it is perfected.
Confucius said: *Study the lesser to attain the greater.*
The Buddha scriptures say: *From hearing and reflection to meditation,*
entering *samādhi* (三摩地).
The Three Teachings all emphasize learning—
this is the foundation for attaining the Dao.

Yet though enlightenment may come suddenly,
it requires gradual practice—
not all can be accomplished in a single step.

If one has not in past lives or this life
prepared through cultivation,
or planted the Dao’s root and sown fields of merit broadly—
*Fo-tian* (福田), where deeds bear fruit like cultivated fields,
is thus named.

**External practices** include:
refurbishing Daoist halls, Buddhist temples, hermitages, shrines, ancestral halls, pagodas, community altars,
building bridges, roads, and administering medicine to heal the sick—
assisting the state, saving lives, casting talismans for relief,
praying for blessings, ensuring progeny, benefiting all beings,
exorcising evil, averting calamities, relieving suffering,
and rescuing the poor.

**Inner cultivation** encompasses:
compassion and mercy, joy in giving, endurance of insults,
harmonizing brilliance, universal benefit without selfishness,
and unshakable, perfect fulfillment.

**Coarse practices** involve:
donating wealth, clothing, and food.
**Secret practices** include:
meditating on the Dao, contemplating the True One,
abstaining from desire to nourish the spirit,
accumulating essence and refining qi.

The path to sainthood and transcendence varies endlessly—
countless fields of merit await cultivation.

Sowing the fields of this world, the seasons bring drought or flood,
human affairs are uneven—sometimes the harvest fails.
But sowing the fields of merit, even a little yields results,
and great efforts bring great rewards.

The hidden virtues are countless—
unknown to others, unspeakable in full,
their merit is boundless.

If one does not sow the fields of merit,
even the name of this scripture may not be heard.
Without virtue or fortune, one does not hear its name.
The scripture says: *"The True Law is rarely encountered"*—
this is what it means.

How much more rare to actually see this scripture?
To see this true scripture is to open the Dao-eye.
Without virtue or fortune, how could one hear its name,
let alone see it?

Mortal fates differ—some receive blessings, others wisdom.
The wealthy may be foolish without virtue;
the poor may be sage-like without fortune.
When virtue and fortune align, one gains rank, wealth, and longevity.
If one encounters the True Law, insight dawns—
without eons of cultivation, its merit would not be so vast.

The Buddha’s assembly of a hundred million,
the True Law entrusted to Kāśyapa;
Confucius’ three thousand disciples,
the single thread passed to Zēng Sān.
The Dao’s multitude—countless myriads—
inheriting the Supreme Mystic’s heart-law,
beginning with Wénshǐ.

Observe and strive accordingly.

**Continuation of the *Yīnyìng* Chapter (Twenty Chapters)**
This scripture follows the Three Caverns’ true pattern,
transmitted once every eighty thousand kalpas.
It is treasured by the Most High True Sage of the Pure Celestial,
hidden in the Jade Capital’s Golden Gate,
exceedingly subtle, rarely encountered.

If one has innate Dao-bones in a past life,
they shall become a True Immortal of the Nine Heavens.
Encountering this text, inheriting this fate—
later, bearing gold and jade, they shall pledge allegiance to a master,
then ride the moment, align with destiny,
and only then may it be entrusted.

Do not reveal it lightly—revere it, guard it carefully.
This scripture is not lightly transmitted.
It follows the Three Caverns’ true pattern:
*Cavern of Truth, Cavern of Mystery, Cavern of Spirit*—
these three divisions bear the celestial laws in gold.
*True Pattern* refers to the natural order.
*Eighty thousand kalpas*—spanning the great cycles of the universe.
One kalpa: born in the Year of the Tiger, dying in the Year of the Rooster.
Eight times eight thousand six hundred forty years—
eighty thousand years in grand reckoning.
Each year’s growth and harvest counts as one kalpa.
*Sand* refers to dust-numbers—
eighty thousand kalpas is the rare transmission of this universal law.
What was said earlier is closer to the truth.

This is the treasure of the Most High True Sage of the Pure Celestial.
*Upper Pure, Mystic Capital*—
hidden in the Jade Capital’s Golden Gate,
not the abode of the Jade Emperor,
but the pavilion of the Supreme Mystic’s treasure-scripture.
Exceedingly subtle—praising this scripture is rare.
If one has innate Dao-bones from past lives,
refined through cultivation, bearing the marks of immortality,
they shall become a True Immortal of the Nine Qi-Heavens.
Encountering this text, inheriting this fate—
later, bearing gold and jade, they shall pledge allegiance to a master,
not merely offering worldly wealth, but swearing to the heavens,
a heart pure as the sun and moon, untainted by dust,
true gold that does not decay.
Only then may they ride the moment, align with destiny,
and be entrusted with its transmission.
Do not reveal it lightly—
*leak* means to betray its essence;
do not transmit it to the unworthy.
Revere it, guard it with care.

Ah! Knowing this scripture’s weight,
all should cultivate auspicious fate
as the foundation for receiving it.
Once received, it must be cherished for eons—
treasure it, strive with it.

**Continuation of the *Yīnyìng* Chapter (Twenty-One Chapters)**

Thus, the Celestial Sovereign solemnly proclaimed this meaning
and spoke in verse:

*If the Yangtze’s waves could bear lotuses,*
*If ravens’ feathers turned white,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If turtles grew fur for clothing,*
*If moonlight could melt ice,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If mosquitoes’ legs built bridges,*
*Bearing all burdens,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If young crows could carry mountains,*
*Hurl them to distant realms,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If a single leaf could bear Kunlun,*
*Float across the great sea,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If leeches grew elephant tusks,*
*As vast as jade,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If broomstraw leaves could shade the boundless,*
*Cover Kunlun’s peaks,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If owls and crows shared nests,*
*Nurturing each other,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If rabbits grew horns for ladders,*
*Reaching the heavens,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If shrews climbed rabbit-horns,*
*Devouring the moon,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If donkeys’ lips turned red as *pīngpó* fruit,*
*And sang and danced,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

*If flies could drink *zhōngshí* wine,*
*Lost in drunken stupor,*
*As rare as this scripture’s encounter.*

Thus, the Primordial Sovereign solemnly proclaimed the scripture’s merit
and spoke in verse:

*If the Yangtze’s waves could bear lotuses,*
*The deep currents, surging—*
*Ravens’ feathers never white.*
*This scripture’s encounter is beyond compare.*

Tortoises are born without fur, the moon belongs to the Dark Yin.
Now to say that tortoise fur is woven into robes,
and that the night moon melts ice—
this is merely to illustrate the utter impossibility
of encountering such a scripture.

As for mosquitoes and gnats building bridges with their feet,
carrying heavy loads;
or yellow-beaked sparrows carrying great mountains
and hurling them to other realms;
or small boats bearing the Kunlun divine mountain
across the great sea,
or leeches growing elephant-tusk teeth—
*Leech: a small water-dragon insect.*
As for *peng-hao* leaves covering boundless realms,
shading the Kunlun peaks;
or owls and crows nesting together,
mutually nurturing and repaying kindness—
*Owls and crows are both detested by true owls.*
Or rabbits growing horns as ladders to heaven,
or shrews climbing rabbit-horn ladders to devour the moon;
or donkeys’ lips turning the color of *pīngpó* fruit,
and singing and dancing;
or flies drinking *zhōngshí* wine,
lost in drunken stupor—
all these are things that must never exist,
that reason itself denies.

Each is recounted to show how rare this scripture’s encounter is.

The Great Dao belongs to all,
yet this true scripture is complete in every individual.
Even the foolish and brute creatures possess inherent virtue,
all capable of transformation and guidance—
why compare this scripture’s rarity to such impossible things?
Could it truly never be transmitted?

The teachings vary in rank—
this scripture is supreme.
Those who transmit it may not be as true as the Primordial Sovereign,
and those who receive it may not grasp the Jade Emperor’s secrets.
Obstinate and rigid minds cannot fathom the whole.
Some hear and see nothing,
others hear and see only superficially—
its merit and efficacy remain obscure.
Without full benefit, it is indeed rare to encounter.

Fear not the difficulty of difficulty—
with utmost sincerity, the scripture’s merit will manifest itself.

**Continuation of the *Yīngyàn* Chapter (Twenty-Two):**
At that time, the Celestial Sovereign having finished reciting the verse,
addressed the Four Assemblies universally:

*"In this world, if any who uphold this scripture*
*are called the *Gōngdé* Body—*
*for all sentient beings are sheltered by its grace.*

*If any who uphold this scripture*
*are called the *Shéntōng* Body—*
*for all auspiciousness gathers to them.*

*If any who uphold this scripture*
*are called the *Qīngjìng* Body—*
*for no evil deed can harm them."*

At that time, the Primordial Sovereign having finished reciting the verse,
addressed the Four Assemblies universally.
*Universal: pervasive. Four Assemblies: as previously explained.*

*"In this world, if any uphold this scripture,*
*they are called the *Gōngdé* Body.*
*To benefit the multitude is *gōng* (function),*
*to benefit all is *dé* (virtue).*
*To benefit both people and things,*
*fully and without omission,*
*is the *Xuángōng Miàodé* Body.*

*All sentient beings—*
*the living, the vegetal,*
*even the inanimate, so long as they possess essence and spirit—*
*are counted as sentient,*
*and thus are all sheltered by its grace.*
*The sages of the Three Teachings universally guide and benefit them eternally.*

*‘Covering and sheltering’ is called *yìn* (imprint).*
*Those who uphold the scripture*
*benefit themselves, benefit others, benefit all beings—*
*whether knowing or unaware,*
*universally bestowing compassionate shelter.*

*If any uphold this scripture,*
*they are called the *Shéntōng* Body.*
*Though humans are most refined,*
*they lack *shéntōng* (supernatural penetration).*
*The scripture’s wondrous laws are supremely profound and divine,*
*unobstructed and vast—*
*thus, those who truly uphold it are called the *Shéntōng* Body.*

*All auspiciousness truly gathers to them.*
*The sages of the Three Teachings eternally fulfill their destiny unbroken.*

*‘All’ is *xiān* (every),*
*‘reach’ is *zhēn* (attain),*
*‘gather’ is *jí* (converge).*
*For oneself, it brings harmony and auspiciousness;*
*for others, it brings love and impartiality;*
*for the world and state, it is never misplaced.*
*Self-attained blessings converge in myriad auspicious signs.*

*The heavens do not hoard the Dao,*
*the earth does not hoard treasure—*
*yet when humans submit to its transformation,*
*all things respond with their innate numinous power.*
*All auspiciousness gathers.*

*If any uphold this scripture,*
*they are called the *Qīngjìng* Body.*
*‘Unstained’ is *qīng*,*
*‘unburdened’ is *jìng*.*
*Those who uphold the scripture*
*extinguish all entanglements,*
*leaving no blemish—*
*thus, no evil can assail them.*

*‘Assail’ means to oppress and harm.*
*Self-made deeds invite celestial retribution,*
*past offenses now manifest,*
*ancestral sins extend to descendants,*
*calamities of the times,*
*blockages of fate,*
*astral malpositions,*
*demonic and ghostly oppression,*
*slander and malevolent influences—*
*all these evil deeds*
*are transformed from malevolent to auspicious,*
*and cannot harm.*

*Those who practice the Dao encompass heaven and earth,*
*fulfilling the needs of all things,*
*their blessings and auspiciousness unending.*
*The heavens protect them, never failing.*
*True auspicious beings suffer no calamity or harm—*
*this is the *Zhēngōngdé Shéntōng Qīngjìng* Body.*

*Though humans have bodies,*
*they are not the *Gōngdé Shéntōng Qīngjìng* Body—*
*nor do they truly uphold the scripture.*
*Strive earnestly,*
*and you may verify its efficacy yourself."*

**Continuation of the *Yīngyàn* Chapter (Twenty-Three):**
*"If any uphold this scripture,*
*they are called the *Wēidé* Body—*
*for celestial demons and heterodox paths cannot ensnare them.*

*If any uphold this scripture,*
*they are called the *Wǔděng* Body—*
*for the Celestial Sovereign sings praises from afar,*
*and all spirits revere them.*

*Those who uphold this scripture*
*are not only called the *Qīngjìng* Body*
*but also the *Wēidé* Body—*
*as previously explained.*

*Celestial demons and heterodox paths*
*include celestial demon kings,*
*demonic men and women,*
*obscure and malevolent ghosts,*
*as well as Asuras,*
*Lūshīluó,*
*and the *xiāo*, *mèi*, *wāng*, *liǎng*—*
*precise, malevolent, monstrous, and taboo entities.*
*As well as deceitful humans,*
*heretical sects,*
*and demonic, seductive, and aberrant paths.*
*They cannot ensnare them.*

*‘Ensnare’ means to subdue and bring into servitude.*
*When demons intrude,*
*people are ensnared without awareness—*
*this is called *shè* (ensnarement).*

*As in the Buddhist tradition,*
*when Ānanda was ensnared by the seductress Móluódéngjiā*
*in the chamber of lust,*
*caressed and fondled,*
*nearly violating his vows.*
*Now, those who uphold the scripture*
*have penetrated the heart-seal,*
*are without selfishness or action,*
*silently recite the true scripture,*
*their law-power complete,*
*their Dao lofty and virtue profound,*
*their awe-inspiring virtue vast and immeasurable.*
*Demons and spirits lose courage,*
*malevolent entities vanish,*
*and all evil demons*
*dare not approach the righteous.*
*Thus, celestial demons and heterodox paths cannot ensnare them.*

*Ānanda was not without precepts—*
*his mind was moved by a single thought toward Móluódéngjiā,*
*indicating he had not yet awakened to the heart-principle.*
*Had he questioned and severed [the illusion] through the scripture,*
*she would not have ensnared him."*

If not for the *Lengyan Sutra*’s power,
how could his body remain whole?

This *Huangjing*—the sovereign of all scriptures—
its received virtue and awe surpass all others ten thousandfold.

Those who uphold this scripture
are not merely named "virtue and awe in body."
Their name transcends equality in body,
a body without peer or equal in kind.

Truly, the highest without compare.
As the *Release of the Scripture* declares:
*"None surpass the Buddha."*
The Confucian texts say:
*"The Master’s excellence is beyond reach—*
*like ascending heaven without a ladder."*

The Celestial Sovereigns chant from afar—
not the Jade Emperor, but the Sovereigns of all heavens.
*"Afars"* means distant;
*"chant"* refers to the celestial harmonies that praise those advancing in the Dao.
Some say *"chant"* means *"to sing in song,"*
but this is illogical and rejected.

For when mortals give birth to a son,
the myriad spirits chant in reverence;
to a daughter, they chant in homage.
The Celestial Sovereigns delight in life,
and the heavens rejoice.
Those of the Dao, in sincerity aligning with Heaven and Earth,
move spirits and gods,
harmonizing with Heaven’s virtue—
the Celestial Sovereigns rejoice in celebration.

Yet the Sovereigns are most exalted,
differing from lesser spirits,
and their abodes in the celestial palaces
are distant—
their voices heard afar in praise.
Otherwise, why say *"Celestial Sovereigns chant from afar"*
and then *"myriad spirits respect"*?
The *"myriad spirits"* are not one—
they encompass all.
Though high or low in rank,
they all revere the Dao’s teachings.
When encountering true scripture-holders of the Way,
none fail to show reverence.

Mankind’s nature is firm, bright, and balanced—
comparable to Yuan Shi,
inherently possessing great virtue and awe,
without equal in kind.
Yet, unchecked desire allows evil to enter,
and the spirits grow disrespectful.

Ah! Zixia was a sage,
yet seeing the dazzling beauty of finery and delighting in it—
how could he, not a true Confucian disciple,
have become the Master’s foremost student?

If one remains true without deceit,
the Dao is forever complete.

---
**Continuation: Chapter Twenty-Four of *Application and Verification***

Those who uphold this scripture are named *"Firm-Body"*—
for great calamities cannot harm them.

Those who uphold this scripture are named *"Dao-Hidden-Body"*—
for when they speak, spirits bow in reverence.

Those who uphold this scripture
are not merely named *"Firm-Body"*—
they are named *"Dao-Hidden-Body."*

Mortals’ lives are impermanent, their cycles unknown.
Some achieve minor merit and virtue,
their blessings limited to this life;
some possess minor roots and small vehicles,
their fruits confined by bounds;
some are enlightened yet incomplete,
easily obscured, easily deceived;
some practice yet remain unfinished,
easily swayed by doubt;
some save others and aid beings,
yet their capacity is exhausted—
their bodies like floating reeds or flickering candles,
unable to withstand winds and waves.
This is not firmness.

True scripture-holders do not retreat—
their bodies are firm.
Great calamities, great disasters cannot harm them.

Whether small, medium, or great *kalpas*,
whether *yuanhui* cycles or worldly transformations,
when the Three Realms are destroyed and reborn,
when all beings perish and the earth tilts while the heavens shatter,
when the Four Wheels collide and the Five Phases clash,
when floods, fires, and winds ravage the world,
when all phenomena vanish and all teachings end—
even the Four *Dhyana* Realms, the Three Stages, and Nine Grades,
the officials, gods, and celestial attendants,
all enter the cycle of rebirth,
facing the hardship of renewed creation—
true scripture-holders attain great firmness,
transcending the *kalpas*,
forever unretreating.

Even in the *kalpas* of evil and ruin,
in the host of past karma and demonic disasters,
in unforeseen great calamities—
none can harm them.
Their constancy endures through all changes,
eternal as the ages—
unshaken.

Those who uphold this scripture
are not merely named *"Firm-Body"*—
they are named *"Dao-Hidden-Body."*
*"Hidden"* means concealed, stored.
The Dao encompasses all without exclusion,
goes everywhere with goodness.
The Dao-Hidden contains nothing unrecorded,
nothing unused.
Though the human body has limits,
its nature is fully endowed.
Yet, if the Dao is not fully realized,
the Dao-Body remains incomplete.

True scripture-holders store the depths like the sea,
contain the vast like the ocean—
their law-treasury holds countless worlds,
thus they are named *"Dao-Hidden-Body."*
When they speak, spirits bow in reverence.

*"Answering"* is called *"utterance,"*
*"self-expression"* is called *"speech."*

The human may speak, yet ghosts and gods do not revere—
for their words lack sincerity,
and idle speech brings misfortune.
Even more, they cannot escape blame—
how then can they move the hearts of humans, gods, or spirits?

The true scripture-holder’s words become faith,
uttered with measured grace—
neither hasty nor suppressed,
never failing in human truth,
never failing in sacred speech.
Sometimes a single word sustains the pulse of a thousand *True Ones*,
sometimes a single word opens the transmission for ten thousand generations,
sometimes a single word rescues beings from drowning,
sometimes a single utterance shatters the barrier between life and death,
sometimes a single word exhausts the Dao of heaven and earth,
sometimes a single utterance encompasses the mysteries of all *dharma*,
sometimes a single word reveals the very nature of ghosts and gods,
sometimes a single utterance illuminates the rise and entanglement of *kalpas* and retribution.

A single word may extinguish sin and merit,
a single utterance may reveal the elixir of gold.
The *True Essences* of the Three Teachings reside in the scripture—
a single word holds the shared treasure of all beings,
a treasure even ghosts and gods cannot perceive.
Who would not hold them in awe?

Ghosts and gods revere—
that is all.

The Three Teachings’ great sages endure through countless *kalpas* without retreat,
their words revered by heaven and humans alike,
and the steadfastness of the Dao-Hidden is now evident.
How then does one swiftly attain this?

For one gain is eternal gain—
this is the empirical truth of principle.
Only those who do not truly uphold the scripture fail to see it.
How does one truly uphold it?
Mindful abstinence is the foundation,
and divine transformation brings it to fulfillment.

*End of Volume Nine of the Imperial Canon’s Commentaries*
*End of Volume Ten of the Imperial Canon’s Commentaries*

**Chapter Twenty-Five: The Manifestation Section (Continued) – The Compassionate Body**

Those who uphold this scripture are named *Compassionate Body*,
for all beings of the Six Paths rely upon their virtue.

Those who uphold this scripture are not merely called *Dao-Hidden Body*—
they are named *Compassionate Body*.
Great kindness and boundless mercy,
saving and liberating without end—
this is called *Compassionate Body*.

Humans alone harbor divergent thoughts of self and other,
distinguishing between near and distant in their minds.
Not only do they fail to universally benefit and eternally aid,
but even when they show kindness or liberate others,
their aid is limited and cannot endure—
this is not the *Compassionate Body*.

Thus, distributing wealth to others is called *benevolence*,
teaching virtue is called *loyalty*.
Small acts of private kindness are not universal salvation.
Only those who truly uphold the scripture attain this *Compassionate Body*—
the Great Compassionate Body,
the Great Merciful Body.

How is this known?
For all beings of the Six Paths rely upon their virtue.

The worlds encompass the Six Paths.
The Six Paths are teeming with beings.
The multitude of the Six Paths is boundless.

**The Heavenly Path**—high above, its blessings pure and enduring,
yet unseen in birth—
how can it be said to be numerous?
Though heaven is exalted, it still contains the Three Realms:
Desire, Form, and Formless—
all subject to arising and decay.
Even if blessings have long or short durations,
only those who truly follow the Dao endure.
All other heavenly beings,
with their transient ranks and forms,
arise and perish—
all are called *beings*.

**The Human Path**—humans are the most enlightened of all creatures.
Though they praise cultivation and propagate the Dao and Law,
they differ in noble and base stations,
male and female forms,
yet teem in countless multitudes—
billions upon billions, beyond reckoning—
this is called *beings*.

**The Asura Path**—demonic kings, demonic peoples, demonic women,
spirits of malevolence, monstrous apparitions, and unnatural calamities—
these are the demonic *beings*.

**The Hellish Path**—the Five Hells of Retribution,
the Nine Dark Prisons,
the Eighteen Great Prisons,
the Thirty-Six Prisons,
the Seventy-Two Prisons—
all suffering in the netherworld’s torments—
these are the prison-bound *beings*.

**The Hungry Ghost Path**—in the yin abyss and murky depths,
great-force ghost kings, ghostly messengers,
with elongated limbs, vast bellies, and parched throats—
for countless *kalpas* they hear no sustenance.
Such are the hungry ghost *beings*.

**The Animal Path**—those born from wombs, eggs, moisture, or transformation,
with feathers, fur, shells, or scales,
crawling or burrowing—
all creatures, great and small,
rely upon the compassion of those who uphold the scripture,
transcending their sufferings and shielding them from harm.
They secure the blessings of heavenly and human beings,
relieve the calamities of mortals,
prevent the descent into demonic prisons,
and extinguish the retributions of ghosts and beasts.

In one world, a thousand million worlds,
in the three thousand great thousandfold universes—
all beings of the Six Paths,
free from karmic bondage and enriched with virtue,
rely upon their goodness.
This is called *Compassion*.

Speak of the Six Paths, and all classes are exhausted.
Speak of *beings*, and all multitudes are encompassed.
All realms are thus.
From beginningless time to endless future,
beyond conception or measure—
all rely upon the virtue of those who truly uphold the scripture.
Truly, this is Great Compassion.

Alas! First liberate oneself, then others—
to save all beings of the Six Paths,
one must eternally uphold the true scripture,
achieving supreme goodness before it is possible.

---

**Chapter Twenty-Six: The Manifestation Section (Continued) – The Great Dao Body**

Those who uphold this scripture are named *Great Dao Body*,
for they fear nothing in all their comings and goings.

Those who uphold this scripture are not merely called *Compassionate Body*—
they are named *Great Dao Body*.
The Dao is formless, yet the human body has form.
Human nature encompasses the fullness of the Dao,
obtaining the principles of Heaven and Earth,
the *qi* of Heaven and Earth.
If one speaks of *Dao Body*,
every person possesses the Dao,
yet no person exhausts it.
Thus, the body given by parents is called *human body*.
The Four Great Elements are fleeting—
it is called *illusionary body*.
Untransformed by things—
it is called *common body*.
Drunk in life, dead in dreams—
it is called *ignorant body*.
Busy from dawn to dusk, sweetly hastening to old age and death—
it is called *karmic body*.
Uncultivated and unlearned, bound in endless cycles—
it is called *sinful body*.
Fragrant flowers fade swiftly, the willow’s branches are few—
it is called *impermanent body*.
Male and female differ in form, old and young in appearance—
it is called *suffering body*.
When the final hour arrives, not even kin can be spared—
it is called *lonely body*.
Wind, rain, cold, and heat assail the flesh—
it is called *suffering body*.

This is the state of mortals—
none possess the Dao.

Those who truly uphold the scripture attain the Law and become real—
this is the *Dao Body*,
not the common body,
named *Great Dao Body*.
In all their comings and goings,
they fear nothing.

*Scare* is anxiety and worry,
*Fear* is dread.
Only those who uphold the scripture are called *Great Dao Body*,
moving forth with ease, returning without burden;
whether moving or resting,
pure and detached from worldly ties,
they are ever serene—
what anxiety, what dread?
Wherever they are,
they fear nothing.

**Explanation:**
The Confucian says:
*"Be cautious in what is unseen,
fearful of what is unheard."*
Is this not *fear*?
Yet joy, anger, sorrow, thought, grief, fear, and startle—
the Seven Emotions reside in all.
If one says, *"In all comings and goings, they fear nothing,"*
it seems contrary to caution and dread.
This is not so.
Caution and dread restrain desire,
preserving the true Dao.
The Seven Emotions reveal the fullness of human nature—
they urge one to subdue passions and return to essence.
If fear arises from inner instability,
stemming from external calamities,
and one is gripped by dread,
this is not the true path.
Thus the Master said:
*"Examine oneself and find no guilt—
what then to fear?"*
How can there be anxiety or dread?
In all their comings and goings, they fear nothing,
for body and Dao are one—
wherever they go, they are at ease.
The Confucian says:
*"Seeing the Great, the heart is tranquil."*
This aligns with their state.
Those who uphold the scripture move without fear—
this is natural, not forced.

Forced constraint, then the *Mòzǐ*’s "unmoved heart" is ultimately not the Dao’s realization.
Natural spontaneity, then the Master’s "no doubt from the heart" and Mencius’ "unmoved heart" all align with this scriptural truth.
Truly, the two teachings’ doctrine of the heart proclaims:
*"Suchness, natural and unshaken—
the Dao of divine transformation is here."*

If one forcibly grasps and does not self-transform,
holding fast yet failing to endure—
though no fear arises, it still does not accord with this scripture’s intent.

**Chapter Twenty-Seven of the *Yànyàn* Section (Continuation):**
Those who uphold this scripture are called *liángyī shēn*—
the "Body of the Skilled Physician," for they practice wondrous methods to bring ease to all.

Those who uphold this scripture are not merely called *Dàdào shēn*—
they are called *liángyī shēn*.
The physician is fitting—
medicine and illness must align to remove afflictions.

Worldly physicians examine forms and discern principles,
healing sickness, rescuing crises,
using drugs to dispel disease, benefiting life—
they earn renown for divine and skillful craft.
Yet true scripture-holders are not worldly physicians,
nor common healers, nor purveyors of coastal prescriptions.
Their golden needles move in silent measure—
they are the *Body of the Skilled Physician*.

They practice wondrous methods well:
human *qi* and temperament are mixed and varied—
some lose their balance at birth,
some bear visible ailments,
some bear invisible ailments,
some suffer bodily woes,
some suffer familial woes,
some suffer national woes,
some suffer age-long woes,
some suffer karmic woes across lifetimes.
Illness and suffering cling, endless in their cycle—
parents cannot instruct them,
sages cannot transform them,
laws cannot restrain them,
medicine cannot cure them,
salvation has no method.

Yet those who uphold this scripture act without deceit,
without forced intrusion—
their wondrous applications are fitting and true.
Their methods are sound, their teachings apt—
no bitter words, no harsh tones,
no defiance of the heart,
no burden to the body,
no forcing of the impossible,
no indulging in false compliance.
They practice wondrous methods to bring ease to all.

Thus, when the wondrous method is applied:
The deaf regain hearing;
Then the blind see clearly;
Then the mute speak;

「Then the lame rise and walk upright;
Then those long afflicted by chronic illness regain their vitality in an instant;
Then gray hair turns black, fallen teeth regrow;
Then the aged grow strong, the young grow mighty;
Then women conceive, and birds and beasts likewise bear offspring—whether born or unborn, all come to fruition;
Then the treasures of the earth are revealed, and gold and jade manifest in their forms;
Then withered bones revive, and all become living, complete persons.

It dispels all calamities, liberates all adversities.
Malevolent spirits and grudges of past lives never dare intrude or harm;
The nine ancestral ties and six kinsfolk—past, present, and future—
are untroubled, free from entanglement, their bonds dissolved in the void.

Abundance flourishes, the body grows light—
not merely lifting those burdened by grave illness,
but even preventing afflictions before they take form.
Truly, without medicine yet bringing joy,
it eternally preserves life to extend one’s years—
not a single remedy or technique,
but the Way’s own physician for all beings.

The Heavenly Physician is the best,
a compassionate father to all sentient beings;
wondrous methods in virtuous practice
bring ease to all who uphold them.

This scripture ascends to the **Great Dao of Reality** (*Zhēndào*), the **Marvelous Prescription for the Age** (*Shìshì qífāng*).
Every person inherently possesses it—
yet those who stray remain unaware.

Those who sincerely uphold this true scripture gain its rewards;
it is fitting to benefit the world.
Why, in this degenerate age, do selfish thoughts arise?
When one gains even a little,
yet does not extend compassion to all beings?
Like the fatness of Qin and the leanness of Yue,
they are unrelated—
at first, they do not teach the world,
but ultimately, they indulge their own desires.
Briefly enlightened, then obscured once more,
they cannot attain the Dao—
how lamentable!

Alas, to know the scripture yet not liberate the world—
that is wrong.
To falsely claim knowledge while arrogantly teaching others,
to recklessly transmit the Way—
that is an even greater sin.

If one can eliminate these two errors,
strive with earnest resolve to comprehend this scripture,
then universal liberation is possible.

**Continuation of the *Verified Signs* Section (28th Chapter):**
Those who uphold this scripture are called **Luminous Bodies** (*Guāngmíng shēn*), for they are constantly embraced and sustained by the **Heavenly Radiance** (*Dìguāng*).

Those who uphold this scripture
are not merely skilled physicians (*Liángyī shēn*), but **Luminous Bodies**.
Human nature is inherently pure and bright,
illuminating all without exception—
yet when the *qi* is constrained and obscured by worldly attachments,
its clarity grows dim, veiled by darkness.

For those who truly uphold this scripture,
their innate nature shines like the heavens,
their mind opens to boundless truth,
their light ever radiant,
their vital essence and essence refined—
as the **Great Void** (*Tàixū*) without clouds,
as the **radiance of sun and moon** in succession,
vast and overflowing,
profound and ever-flowing.
Truly, they are **Luminous Bodies** (*Guāngmíng shēn*), not stained by darkness.

They are constantly embraced and sustained by the **Heavenly Radiance** (*Dìguāng*).
The **Heavenly Sovereign** (*Dì*—the **Jade Emperor** *Yùdì*)’s radiance pervades all,
yet humans, being lowly and impure,
struggle to bear its weight.
Now, those who uphold this scripture
walk in the path of Heaven’s light,
illuminating the **Golden Court** (*Jīntíng*—the celestial realm),
and when the **Heavenly Radiance** (*Dìguāng*) is invoked,
the **Great Harmony** (*Tàihé*) reveals its brilliance.

The **Heavenly Radiance** (*Dìguāng*) enfolds them,
protecting those who uphold this scripture.
Those who uphold this scripture are transformed by its power,
eternally preserving their purity.
Their light intermingles with the **Heavenly Radiance**—
those who uphold this scripture,
in faith aligned with Heaven’s **virtue/power** (*Dé*),
share the **radiance of sun and moon**.

It has been said that the **Heavenly Dao** (*Tiāndào*) descends to benefit all,
its radiance without favor or partiality.
Humans receive Heaven’s bright decree,
inherently possessing **Great Radiance** (*Dà guāngmíng*).
Yet their nature is untainted by default,
their mind noble in its purity.
When humans indulge in avarice and pleasure,
they cannot keep the **Soul’s Platform** (*Língtái*—the mind’s pure essence) free of defilements—
like the sun and moon being eclipsed,
or clouds and mists obscuring the sky.

If one does not **refine their faults** (*Wén qíguò*—cultivate moral rectitude)
and **sever desire to return to principle** (*Jué yù huán lǐ*),
their momentary darkness swiftly clears,
opening to the **Four Directions and Eight Reaches** (*Sìtōng bādá*—all directions),
their brightness ever increasing.
There is no **Heavenly Radiance** that does not shine,
no **Heavenly Sovereign’s Light** that does not descend—
this is not so.

Humans, however, abandon themselves,
their thoughts restless and unceasing,
active by day, weary by night,
their minds never still.
Their deeds are false,
their thoughts impure,
contradicting Heaven’s will,
thus obscuring the **true scripture** (*Zhēnjīng*).

Even a slight awakening,
their faults become **karmic seeds** (*Yèshēng*—future consequences).
Guilt and retribution loom heavy,
their suffering never lightened.
If they do not swiftly amend,
using **eloquent refinement** (*Cí wén*—moral cultivation)
as their excuse,
Heaven cannot be deceived,
the gods cannot be fooled.
Humans’ self-perception
is like gazing upon their own lungs and liver—
this nature, where is it?
How can they bear to deceive their own hearts thus?

Therefore, the **Heavenly Decree** (*Tiānmìng*)’s blessings,
the **Heavenly Sovereign’s Light** (*Dìguāng xiánghù*—the Jade Emperor’s protection),
must belong to those who truly uphold this scripture
and cultivate the Dao to attain Reality (*Chéngzhēn*).

Those who truly uphold this scripture are **Luminous Bodies** (*Guāngmíng shēn*),
embracing the **Heavenly Radiance** (*Dìguāng*).
Alas, humans are all the same,
their **illuminated virtue** (*Míngdé*) equal—
yet why do they not all uphold this scripture,
fulfilling the Dao,
and aligning with the **Heavenly Sovereign’s intent** (*Dìxīn*)?

**Continuation of the *Verified Signs* Section (29th Chapter):**
Those who uphold this scripture are called **Bodies of Freedom** (*Zìzài shēn*), for they can freely traverse the **Heavenly Palaces and Marvelous Realms** (*Tiāngōng miàojìng*).

The virtues and merits of upholding this scripture
are beyond measure—
those who uphold it
are not merely **Luminous Bodies** (*Guāngmíng shēn*), but **Bodies of Freedom** (*Zìzài shēn*).
The **Three Calamities** (*Sānzāi*—fire, water, wind),
the **Four Slayings** (*Sìshā*—thieves, robbers, etc.),
the **Five Agents** (*Wǔxíng*—wood, fire, earth, metal, water),
the **Six Harms** (*Liùhài*—poison, weapons, etc.),
the **Seven Injuries** (*Qīshāng*—physical afflictions),
the **Eight Difficulties** (*Bānàn*—karmic hardships),
the **Nine Star Disasters** (*Jiǔxīng è*—celestial misfortunes),
and the **Ten Evil Karmas** (*Shì’ě yè*—ten transgressions)
all fail to entangle them—
their **karmic roots** (*Yègēn*) are forever severed.

They attain the **Three Elements** (*Sānyuán*—heaven, earth, human),
transcend the **Five Aggregates** (*Wǔyùn*—form, sensation, perception, etc.),
free from the **Four Marks** (*Sìxiàng*—impermanence, suffering, etc.),
severed from the **Hundred Non-Dharmas** (*Bǎi fēi*—unskillful deeds),
removed from the **Ten Thousand Phenomena** (*Wàn yǒu*—all worldly attachments),
surpassing the **loads of kalpas** (*Zàijié*—aeons of suffering),
truly attaining the **Great Freedom** (*Dà zìzài*—absolute liberation).

They traverse the **Heavenly Palaces and Marvelous Realms** (*Tiāngōng miàojìng*) by divine power.
These upholders of the scripture
possess **profound, effortless skill** (*Xuán gōng rúyì*—mystical, intuitive mastery),
their bodies attaining **Freedom** (*Zìzài*).

All the **Heavenly Palaces** (*Fánzhū tiāngōng*—various celestial realms),
all the **Marvelous Realms** (*Yīqiè miàojìng*—divine landscapes),
with **jade paths and gemstone steps** (*Bìlù yáo jiē*),
**twisted walls and painted barriers** (*Qiú qiáng cǎi bì*),
**the Jade Capital and Golden Gates** (*Yùjīng jīn què*—celestial city),
**the Purple Palace and Yellow Rooms** (*Zǐfǔ huáng fáng*—imperial abodes),
**palaces of jade and halls of pearl** (*Qióng lóu yùyǔ*),
**the Enchanted Gardens and Gemstone Pools** (*Wèn yuàn yáo chí*),
**the Mystic Heights and Secluded Platforms** (*Xuán dōu shàng jìng*—upper celestial realms),
**the Secret Halls and Red Pillars** (*Mì yuàn dān tái*—hidden sanctums),
**the Fragrant Forest and Sacred Paths** (*Bǎolín xiāng jìng*),
**the Divine Chambers and Vermilion Offices** (*Shénshì jiàng guān*),
**the Law-Bridge with Brocade Railings** (*Fǎ qiáo jǐn kǎn*),
**the White Hall and Rust-Colored Courtyard** (*Hàodiàn zhě tíng*),
as well as **jade grasses and rare flowers** (*Yáo cǎo qí huā*),
**ice peaches and snow plums** (*Bīng táo xuě lǐ*),
**fiery dates and flame-red jujubes** (*Huǒ zǎo huǒ zǎo*),
**nectar and ambrosia** (*Dān zhuàn qióng jiāng*),
**the Dao’s radiance and divine blessings** (*Dàoguāng xuán ruì*),
**rainbow clouds and celestial omens** (*Cǎi xiá yún xiāng*),
**divine carriages and lawful conveyances** (*Shén yú fǎ jià*),
**lawful treasures and heavenly beings** (*Fǎbǎo tiān rén*),
**all manner of wondrous essences** (*Zhū pǐn qí yīng*—rare, extraordinary substances),
**divine traversal and meditative observation** (*Shén yóu dìng guān*—spiritual wandering and insight),
all are explored in their triumphant journeys—
unattainable by ordinary mortals.

The virtues and merits of upholding this scripture
are beyond measure—
how much more so when its benefits
extend to all beings, both subtle and manifest,
alive and departed,
past and present?
Evil spirits are subdued,
the **Heavenly Radiance** descends,
divine wanderings through the heavens
are still but a fraction of its wonders—
then how boundless are its virtues and merits!」

「Speaking of the **Sage of Utmost Perfection** (*Shuō jīng zhì shèng yòu hé rú zāi*),
Ah! The **scripture’s virtues** are indeed the greatest.
It must be upheld with **unshaken sincerity** (*dāng zhì chéng yǒng chí*).

The **Application and Verification Chapter** continues with thirty-one sections.
If **Daoists or those of noble resolve** (*dào shì zhì rén*)—
those who can **establish an altar** (*néng jié tán*) and **recite the scripture** (*sòng jīng*),
wearing **new and pure garments** (*zhuó xīn jìng yī*),
at the **midnight hour** (*yè bàn*), when the **dark and silent** (*fěi yě jì*) **true form** (*zì zhēn xíng*) of the **sacred syllables** (*yún xiāng*) is invoked,
sitting alone in a **chamber of purity** (*qīng jìng shì*),
**rinsing the mouth and brushing the teeth nine times** (*kòu chǐ jiǔ tōng*),
facing east in **proper posture** (*duān zuò*),
reciting and chanting this scripture—
then, at that very moment,
**Heavenly Purity** (*tiān zhēn*) **descends upon the desk** (*yù jī*),
**Jade Consorts** (*yù fēi*) **sweep the ceremonial mat** (*fú yán*),
**ten thousand spirits** (*wàn shén*) **assemble in ranks** (*bān liè*),
**all the celestial realms** (*zhū tiān*) **come to the hall** (*lín xuān*),
**the Three Realms** (*sān jiè*) **stand in attendance** (*shì wèi*),
and the **Five Emperors** (*wǔ dì*) **oversee the reception** (*sī yíng*).
Those who uphold this scripture are called the **Twelve-Merit Body** (*shí'èr gōng dé shēn*),
and their **compassionate salvation** (*cí jì*) is boundless.

Again, of **Daoists or those of noble resolve** (*dào shì zhì rén*):
**Daoists** (*dào shì*), a common term for those who **pursue the Way** (*xiū dào rù xuán zhī tōng míng*).
**Noble resolve** (*zhì rén*), those with **determination** (*yǒu zhì zhī rén*).
Some mistakenly render it as **Sages of Perfection** (*zhì rén*—*fēi yě*), for only those who **attain the Dao and become True** (*dé dào chéng zhēn*) may be called such.
Those who study the scripture merely see the **Heavenly Purity** (*tiān zhēn*), **Jade Consorts**, **ten thousand spirits**, and **celestial realms**,
along with the **Three Realms** and **Five Emperors** descending and attending,
and thus assume it pertains to **Sages of Perfection** (*zhì rén*).
But they do not know that this scripture is the **Imperial Edict** (*dì chì*—*mì shì*),
and wherever it is, all spirits **offer reverence and guard** (*gòng fèng*).
When it encounters those who **recite and uphold** (*chí sòng*) it—
whether they be **foolish husbands or common wives** (*yú fū fán fù*), **infirm elders or ignorant children** (*shuāi sǒu méng tóng*)—
the spirits **respect such persons** (*shén jìng shì rén*) as if they were **receiving this Edict** (*rú fèng shì dì*).
If one **upholds the scripture with sincerity and reverence** (*chí jīng chéng jìng*), their **blessings and virtues** (*fú dé*) are boundless.
But **neglect or disrespect** (*dài màn zé jiù yāng lì zhì*) will bring **immediate retribution** (*jiù yāng*).
The spirits attend and guard because they **revere those who uphold the true scripture** (*jìng qí chí zhēn jīng*), not necessarily **Sages of Perfection** (*zhì rén*).
How much more so when they **establish the Dao-altar** (*jié dào fǎ*), **recite in the hall** (*chǎng fǔn sòng jīng*),
and wear **new and pure robes** (*zhuó xīn zuò jié qìng yī fú*)?
At the **midnight hour** (*yè bàn*), in the **silent and pure chamber** (*jìng shì zhī zhōng*),
when the **sacred syllables** (*yún xiāng*—*gǔ qú*) are **uttered in profound obscurity** (*dà mèi shí yě jì*),
sitting alone, **rinsing the mouth and brushing the teeth nine times** (*kòu chǐ jiǔ tōng*),
facing east, **upright in body and mind** (*duān shēn dìng zuò*),
