reciting and chanting this scripture—
then, at that very moment,
when these **noble resolvers** (*zhì rén*) **follow the method in purity** (*rú fǎ qīng jìng sòng jīng*),
**Heavenly Purity** (*tiān zhēn*) **descends upon the desk** (*yù jī*), and **Celestial Truths** (*zhū tiān zhī zhēn*) **come to the hall** (*lín xuān*),
**Jade Consorts and Spirit Maidens** (*líng fēi yù nǚ*) **sweep the ceremonial mat of the Dao** (*fú qīng fǎ yán*).
*Sweep* (*fú*) here means to **purify with solemn reverence** (*dǎng yě*), not to **contradict or oppose** (*fú nì*).
*The ceremonial mat* (*yán*) is the **mat of the Dao** (*fǎ shì*).
**Ten thousand spirits** (*wàn shén*) **assemble in ranks** (*bān liè*), as **imperial officials** (*qún chén*) do under the **edicts of mortal emperors** (*shì jiān dì wáng chì lìng*).
The **Primordial Scriptures** (*huáng jīng*) are the **secrets of the Jade Emperor** (*yù dì mì yán*), the **original intent of the First Beginning** (*yuán shǐ fǎ zhǐ*).
When the **noble resolvers** (*zhì rén*) **recite and uphold** (*chí sòng*), they **proclaim the Imperial Edict** (*dú xuān dì chì*) as it were,
and **all spirits** (*wàn shén*) **assemble in ranks and bow in reverence** (*suí biàn gǒng fèng*).
**All the celestial realms** (*zhū tiān*) **come to the hall** (*lín xuān*), with their **imperial truths and sacred conveyances** (*dì zhēn fǎ jià*).
*The hall* (*xuān*) is the **mat of the Dao** (*xuán àn*).
**The Three Realms** (*sān jiè*)—**the Heavenly Realm, Earthly Realm, and Watery Abode** (*tiān jiè, dì jiè, shuǐ fǔ jiè*)—
**deploy their divine attendants and historians** (*shén jiāng shì liè hù wèi*).
Or it may be said that **the Three Realms** (*sān jiè*)—**desire, form, and formlessness** (*yù, sè, wú sè*)—
are not the case here.
**The Five Emperors** (*wǔ dì*)—**the Five Directions, Five Spirits, and Five Elders of the Celestial Court** (*wǔ fāng wǔ líng wǔ lǎo dì*)—
**oversee the reception** (*sī yíng*).
Or it may be said that **the Five Emperors** (*wǔ dì*) are the **Five Sacred Mountains** (*wǔ yuè zūn dì*).
Since earlier there is mention of **ten thousand spirits** (*wàn shén*) and **Three Realms** (*sān jiè*), and within the Three Realms are the **Five Elders** (*wǔ lǎo*),
this must refer to the **Five Sacred Mountains and ten thousand spirits** (*wǔ yuè wàn shén*).
The Three Realms include the **Five Sacred Mountains** (*sān jiè zhōng yǒu wǔ yuè*), hence the **Five Elders** (*wǔ lǎo*).
In the scripture, the **Five Elders** (*wǔ lǎo*) **begin the questioning** (*qǐ wèn*), so when the scripture is opened,
the **Five Elders** (*wǔ lǎo*) **oversee the reception** (*sī yíng*) of the **Dao Ancestor** (*dào zǔ*).
*Oversee* (*sī*) means **to take charge** (*zhǔ yě*), **to accept** (*chéng yě*).
*Reception* (*yíng*) means **to meet and escort** (*qì yě*).
It signifies **the ritual homage to the Mysterious Sovereign** (*guì lǐ xū huáng zhī yì*).
Or it may also be said that *oversee the reception* (*sī yíng*) refers to **the spirits of the scripture ascending to the Dao’s obscurity** (*chí jīng zhī shén shēng xuán*).
But if one does not **recite the scripture with utmost devotion** (*qián*), the spirits will not **fully manifest their protection** (*bèi hù*).
The spirits **discern and respond** (*jiàn bào*), and this is inevitable.
Those who **see or hear** (*jiàn wén*) the scripture must **solemnly uphold it with reverence** (*lǐn rán gōng chí*).
Those who do not must **urgently seek to encounter it** (*dàn wéi wén qí yíng*).
To be **strict as if the spirits themselves are present** (*yán rú zhū shén zhī lín*), yet **not to seek their visible effects** (*bù qiú yìng jiàn zhī xiào*).
To **hold fast to the true scripture without thought or action** (*wú sī wú wéi, mì mì chí zhēn*),
so that the **spirit of one’s own body** (*yī shēn zhī shén*) **stands vigilant and eternally safeguards the Dao’s true scripture** (*sēn rán yǒng bǎo xuán zhēn jīng*).
Exhort them not to be negligent.

The **Application and Verification Chapter** continues with thirty-one sections.
Again, those who can **close their eyes and sit in still meditation** (*bì mù jìng sī*),
**retain and visualize this scripture** (*cún xiǎng shì jīng*),
unaware that their **body is enveloped in the Three Colors of Cloud-Qi** (*sān sè yún qì zhī zhōng*),
suddenly see their **form radiant and resplendent** (*shēn guāng míng hè yì*), ascending to the **Celestial Palaces** (*shàng shēng tiān gōng*).
**Multitudes of True Ones** (*zhōng zhēn*) **descend to greet them** (*xiāng xià yíng*).
Whatever they **request in their hearts** (*xīn yǒu suǒ qǐng*), all is **answered and granted** (*yīng fèng*).
**Immortal elixirs and wondrous treasures** (*xiān dān miào bǎo*) are **obtained at will** (*suí yì zì dé*).
It is fitting to **follow the prescribed methods** (*yīng dāng yī kē*) and **devoutly practice in silent mindfulness** (*míng xīn fèng xíng*).
Not only must one **devoutly recite** (*qián sòng*) this scripture and **gain the spirits’ protection** (*dé zhū shén hù*),
but also, when **closing their eyes in still meditation** (*bì mù jìng zuò*),
they may **subdue the Five Aggregates’ harm** (*sǐng xiǎng wǔ yùn zhī hài*), with **form** (*sè*) being the foremost.
The **disorder of form** (*sè zhī luàn xīn*) is **realized through the eyes** (*mù shí zhī*).
To **uphold the true scripture** (*fèng chí zhēn jīng*), one’s **body and mind must be harmonious** (*shēn xīn yí*).
To **close the eyes and attain stillness** (*bì mù yǐ jìng*), the **heart naturally enters Great Tranquility** (*xīn zì dà dìng*).
Yet the **Dao’s profound subtlety** (*dào zhī xuán wēi*) cannot be **grasped without contemplation** (*fēi sī bù rù*).
**Random thoughts** (*wàng sī*) only **disturb the True** (*yòu suǒ luàn zhēn*).
To **close the eyes and sit in still meditation** (*bì mù jìng zuò*), not **seeing what is desirable** (*bù jiàn kě yú*),
so that the **heart does not stray** (*xīn bù luàn*), to **remain silent and ponder** (*mò hē sī suǒ*),
**delving into the profound mysteries** (*mì rù shēn jī*—*dào zhī dà yào yě*).
Now, for those who **sit in still meditation with closed eyes** (*jìng zuò zhě*), it is said that **the eyelids should be half-lowered** (*liǎng mù bàn chuí lián*), not fully closed,
lest they engage in **ghostly schemes and occult practices** (*wèi zuò guǐ kuàng huó jì*—*bù zhī yīn qù zá niàn, shì yuē guǐ kuàng*).
If the **heart is pure** (*xīn qīng jìng*), what harm is there in **closing the eyes** (*bì mù*)?
The **common folk’s hearts are not resolute** (*shí rén xīn bù jué liè*), so they **hesitate when closing their eyes** (*bì mù yí shēng*).
Thus, they **half-open their eyes** (*bàn kāi yǎn*), lest they **fall into slumber or doubt** (*bù zhuó shuì mó yí shēng*).
If one **forgets both good and evil** (*shàn è liǎng wàng*), **holds neither being nor non-being** (*wú wú yě wú*), the **True Dao enters naturally** (*zhēn dào zì rù*).
What hindrance is there in **closing the eyes** (*bì mù*)?
The **half-lowered eyelids** (*chuí lián zhī lùn*) are merely a **precaution of the Mysterious Masters** (*xuán shī fáng wú zhì rén mó huò*).
Moreover, the **meaning of half-lowered eyelids** (*chuí lián zhī yì*) is to **not observe outwardly** (*bì mù bù guān*),
while **innerly possessing true illumination** (*nèi yǒu zhēn zhào*).
The **heart’s law is ever-awake** (*xīn fǎ xīng xīng*), **radiant and unobscured** (*guāng míng bù mèi*).
Like **lowering the curtain to attend to governance** (*rú chuí lián tīng zhèng*), though one does not **look upon the matters** (*bù guān guān kàn*),
those who **should respond** (*dāng yìng zhě*) are **without fail known** (*wú bù zhī qí*).
This is the **mechanism of Dao cultivation** (*gū jiā*), hence its inclusion in the discussion of the scripture.

The **cultivation of visualization** (*cún xiǎng*) is the scripture itself. Yet this visualization is not the summoning of visions or effects as in the *Zhāoshè Jīng* (Scripture of Summoning and Gathering). When practicing this method, one should revere the Jade Emperor as if seeing him in person, pondering the Dao and seeking the True—never lightly or carelessly.

Mere recitation of the scripture with a distracted mind is insufficient. One must **quietly preserve this heart**, delving deeply into its profound truths. When embodied in body and mind, the saying *"visualization is the scripture"* holds true—unaware, one finds oneself immersed in the **three-colored qi-clouds** (*sān sè yún qì*). These clouds arise from the **steaming of Heaven and Earth**.

When the mind is deeply settled in the scripture, it merges with the **Heavenly Heart** (*tiān xīn*), and with each sincere thought, the **auspicious clouds** (*qìng yún*) emerge—unaware, one is enveloped in the **three-colored qi-clouds of green, yellow, and white**. When the mind and body are still and upright, the **Dragon and Tiger coil and spiral** (*lóng hǔ pán xuán*), giving rise to these three-colored clouds.

If one attains True Perfection, then **five-colored clouds** (*wǔ sè yún*) gather, and the **nine radiant glories** (*jiǔ xiá guāng*) spread forth—this is yet another state.

Suddenly (*rú*), in the blink of an eye (*shǎo qīng shí*), one’s body shines **radiantly resplendent** (*guāng míng hè yì*), ascending to the **Celestial Palace** (*tiān gōng*), where the **multitudes of True Ones** descend to welcome.

**Suddenly**, in a short while, one’s body **glows brilliantly** (*shēn guāng huàn fā*), **magnificent and luminous** (*shèng yào bǐng yì*). As previously explained.

When the heart has a request, when the mind seeks entry into the **Celestial Palace**, all **supreme elixirs and wondrous treasures** (*yuánshǐ yùdì xiāndān miàobǎo*) are **offered in response**—whatever is desired is naturally obtained.

One must not merely **seek treasures**; the treasures are **offered to oneself**. One should **follow the prescribed methods** (*yī kē*), as previously explained.

The scripture is the **true nature of human essence** (*rén xìng zhēn*). Silent enlightenment and steadfast practice suffice.

Speaking of visualization, it seems to fall under the **second meaning** (*dì èr yì*). The Confucian classics say:
*"Faintly perceived, yet unseen—like a form without substance, yet clearly visible. It is as if one stands upon it."*

Is this not also the **second meaning**?

Alas, **enlightened sages are few**, while **mediocre minds prevail**. If one does not **grasp visualization**, how can one seek the **unheard teachings** (*bù wén zhī shì*) and thus **harmonize with Heaven and humanity**, transcend the mundane, and enter the sacred?

Let scholars ponder this.

---
**Continuation of the *Yìngyàn Pǐn* (Verification Chapter), Thirty-Second Section**

This scripture is the path by which **three-world Golden Immortals** (*sān shì jīn xiān*) and **ten-direction Great Saints** (*shí fāng dà shèng*) attain the **supreme wondrous Dao**. The **Jade Emperor** of this scripture is the **teacher of all heavens** and the **king of all saints**.

This scripture is not merely for those who recite it with devotion—even **three-world Golden Immortals**, whether of the past, present, or future worlds, must follow its methods to attain the **supreme wondrous Dao**.

**Golden Immortals** (*jīn xiān*) are those whose **Golden Elixirs do not decay** (*jīn dān bù huǐ*), the **true Daoists of the Great Mysterious** (*tài xuán zhēn xiān*). The **ten-direction Great Saints**—those of the **four cardinal, four diagonal, and upper-lower directions** (*sì zhèng fāng, sì yú fāng, shàng xià fāng*)—the **ten-direction numinous treasures and divine spirits** (*shí fāng língbǎo zūnshén*), the **Great Saints of Ultimate Truth and Boundless Extremes** (*zhì zhēn wújí dà shèng*)—all attain the **supreme wondrous Dao** by following its methods, as previously explained.

Progress in cultivation varies, and attainments differ. Those whose **Dao-verification stages** (*zhèngdào jiē pǐn*) have not yet been reached do not yet possess the **supreme**.

Whether **gods, humans, earthly, or ghostly immortals**; whether **desire-realm, form-realm, or formless heavenly deities**; whether **Bodhisattvas, Śrāvakas, Arhats, or Buddhist vehicles**; whether **transformed, great, beautiful, faithful, virtuous persons, or Confucian sages**—none of these are the **ultimate**.

Only **Celestial Immortals** (*tiān xiān*), **Wen Buddhas** (*wén fó*), and **unknowable Saints** (*bù zhī shèng*)—where **gods and Confucians** are named the **highest**—do the Golden Immortals and Great Saints, by **faithfully following this scripture**, merge with the **Imperial True Ones** (*dì zhēn*), thus attaining the **highest Immortal**, transcending and verifying the **supreme, ultimate, and wondrous Dao**, beyond the fruits of **heavenly blessings and virtues**.

This is the **Jade Emperor**. *Zhī* means *"this."* He is the **teacher of all heavens**—the **thirty-three heavens**, the **thirty-six heavens**, the **twelve thousand heavens**, the **three thousand great worlds**, and **all heavens**—who **transform and give rise to the multitudes of True Ones** through the *Huáng Jīng* (Imperial Scripture).

He is the **king of all saints**—whether **immortals, Confucian sages, Buddhas, heavenly beings, or gods**—all **yield their virtues**, **surrender their merits**, and **acknowledge their supremacy**, revering him through the ages.

Alas, if a person’s **Heavenly Sovereign** (*tiān jūn*) remains **serene and composed**, then the Dao may be attained. If one does not **cultivate the mind to enlightenment**, merging with Heaven in virtue, and **venerating the Supreme in emptiness**, one has **fallen short**. Be warned and reflect.

---
**Continuation of the *Yìngyàn Pǐn*, Thirty-Third Section**

Thus, when an **ordinary person** (*fán fú*) encounters this scripture and **devotes themselves with single-minded devotion**, even the **Five Emperors** (*wǔ dì*) will **assist and shelter**, summoning **multitudes of immortals**, commanding **divine officials**, directing **yin-yang forces**, earning the **respect of ten thousand spirits**, subduing **myriad gods**, keeping **a hundred evils at bay**, and binding **all demons** in form.

After death, one will **enter the Southern Palace for refinement**, ascending the **Upper Clarity** (*shàng qīng*) with **free and easy steps**, dwelling in **adaptability and eternal Dao**.

It is not only **Golden Immortals and Great Sages** who verify the Dao through this scripture.

Thus, when an **ordinary person** (*shìjiān fán fú*) encounters this scripture through **karmic opportunity**, and **devotes themselves with precision and sincerity**, even the **Five Elder Emperors** (*wǔ lǎo dìshì*—not the Five Peaks) will **aid their cultivation** and **supplement their deficiencies**. They will **summon immortals** and **command divine officials**—**issuing orders to make them act**, as immortals respond to command, and **controlling them to serve**, as divine officials obey.

The scripture states:
*"Those who cultivate the Dao with devotion can even command ghosts and subdue gods."*

Even an ordinary person, through **single-minded devotion to the scripture**, wielding the **power of Dao-law**, can **summon immortals and command gods**, directing **yin-yang forces**. Only through **precision and unity** can one **govern transformation** and **guide yin-yang**.

The **ten thousand spirits** will **reverently bow in awe**, and the **myriad gods** will **submit in fear and servitude**—without need for ritual. The **a hundred evils** will **avoid the path**, and the **multitudes of demons** will **restrain their forms**, daring not to reveal themselves.

After death, one’s spirit perceives what was unseen before.

One is then admitted to the **Southern Palace** for **refinement**—the **Southern Palace**, the Vermilion Refinement Bureau, where souls are measured and spirits are tempered. Having undergone **refinement**, one ascends to the **Upper Purity** realm, taking **divine strides** to reach the **Upper Purity** heavens—this is not the true Upper Purity domain, but merely the expression of ascending to heaven.

Freed to wander at will, one avoids the **Six Realms of Torment**, escapes the consequences of **karma**, and is bound by no constraints—moving effortlessly and at ease.

With the Dao, one endures eternally. Though initially not yet perfect, if one devotes oneself **single-mindedly** to the scripture, aligning one’s heart with the Dao, free from obstruction and entanglement, the spirit and soul become pure and undefiled, never again to perish or fall—thus enduring with the Dao.

This is what the **Daoist classics** mean by *"dying yet not perishing"* and what the **Buddhist scriptures** mean by *"enlightenment brings instant release."*

Even the most humble practitioner, through **single-minded devotion** to the scripture, achieves such results—then it is known how profound the **power of utmost sincerity** is.

Though of low understanding, one can still fully attain the Dao. Let the reader strive accordingly.

**Chapter 34: Manifestations of Response**
Moreover, when common folk in the world hear this scripture and their hearts yearn in reverence, they can, within their households, choose a pure and serene place, draw an image of the **Imperial Sage**, and with **earnest devotion**, offer incense morning and night—abundant **sacred flowers, lamps, and fruits**, honoring and nourishing the sacred form, chanting the **holy name**, and bowing in worship while reciting the scripture. Such a person shall attain **thirty kinds of supreme, wondrous virtues**:

1. The **ten thousand immortals** shall hold them in high esteem,
2. The **departed ancestors** shall be reborn in heaven,
3. Past **sufferings and calamities** shall be resolved and released,
4. All paths they tread shall be **smooth and open**.

「The remaining twenty kinds of supreme, wondrous virtues**:

5. They shall be free from theft and banditry,
6. All their desires shall be fulfilled,
7. They shall be delivered from water and fire calamities,
8. All misfortunes and adversities shall be subtly dispelled,
9. Their nightly dreams shall be auspicious and fortunate,
10. Illnesses and diseases shall not afflict them,
11. Their wisdom and intelligence shall be acute and clear,
12. All who see them shall rejoice,
13. Their clothing and food shall be abundant and flourishing,
14. Their descendants shall be honored and noble—*not merely wealthy and opulent, but virtuous and refined, free from ignoble or untimely misfortune*,
15. Their six kinsfolk shall take joy in them,
16. Their household and lineage shall dwell in harmony,
17. They shall be freed from the three kinds of evil retribution,
18. They shall be transformed from female to male,
19. Their appearance and bearing shall be dignified and awe-inspiring,
20. They shall become great ministers of the realm,
21. They shall be born as the sons of emperors,
22. Ghosts and spirits shall hold them in reverence and awe,
23. They shall attain the **Dharma of Retention**—*all past karma shall be exhausted, and their life-force shall flow unimpeded*,
24. All gods shall protect and honor those who uphold this scripture and revere the **Imperial Sage**,
25. Their nine lineages shall be sheltered—*the nine lineages being: the paternal great-grandfather, paternal grandfather, paternal ancestor, father, oneself, son, grandson, great-grandson, and remote descendant; or alternatively, the three generations of the father, the three generations of the mother, and the three generations of the wife*,
26. They shall live long in this world,
27. All sentient beings in the world shall rely upon their virtuous deeds,
28. The **Mara-kings** shall commend and welcome them,
29. They shall ascend beyond the realms of desire, form, and formlessness,
30. They shall ascend in broad daylight—*though the transformations of the immortals vary, this does not necessarily mean ascending in the flesh during daylight; rather, their essence harmonizes with the **Great Void** and their spirit roams the **Celestial Capital** of the Imperial Sage*.

To uphold this scripture with reverence and honor the **Imperial Sage**, though these virtues may be attained, one must first utterly abandon all secret lusts, seek no verification of their efficacy, nor cease their practice. With their heart aligned with the **Heavenly Dao**, only then shall they bear fruit—even if no fruit is borne, it shall not diminish their merit in doing good.

If one seeks only these effects, they are not truly transmitting the **Imperial Sage’s scripture**. May the observant heed this warning.

**Continuation of Chapter 35: Manifestations of Response**
At that time, the **Celestial Sage** further instructed the **Four Assemblies**, saying:

“The virtues of this scripture are such that it can shatter the **Yin Mountains** and the **Iron Encircled Mountains**, drain the waters of the **Sea of Suffering**, dispel the **Great Underworld Prison**, extract all beings from sin and torment, subdue violent and malevolent **Mara-demons**, and safeguard all lands.

It can extinguish all malevolent ghosts, banish all evil spirits and dark realms, and eliminate all grave illnesses. It can dissolve all malevolent poisons, sever ties with all wicked people—*either by preventing encounter or causing such persons to flee upon seeing them*—and tame all venomous beasts. Moreover, those who practice **Daoist refinement** shall transmute their **Yin-qi** into poisonous dragons, fierce beasts, and great serpents, each numbering in the hundreds of billions, all protecting this **true scripture** and ensuring their own subjugation, forever shielding it.

The remaining virtues are too numerous to recount exhaustively.

To uphold this scripture and honor the **Imperial Sage** yields thirty kinds of virtue.

At that time, the **Celestial Sage** further instructed the **Four Assemblies**, saying:

“The virtues of this scripture are such that it can shatter the **Yin Mountains** and the **Iron Encircled Mountains**, purifying all lingering dust.

It can drain the **Sea of Suffering**, turning heads toward the shore and leaving its waves dry. It can dispel the **Great Underworld Prison**, silencing all false attachments. It can extract beings from all sin and torment, severing the roots of karma and preventing any future retribution. It can subdue violent and malevolent **Mara-demons**, restraining their arrogance and perverse delusions. It can safeguard all lands, ensuring prosperity and peace, wealth for the realm, and security for its people.

It can extinguish all malevolent ghosts, banishing all malevolent and dark spirits, and severing ties with dark, evil destinies. It can eliminate all grave illnesses, cleansing all afflictions. It can dissolve all malevolent poisons, removing all worldly malevolence and the **great true poison** of the body. It can sever ties with all wicked people—*either by preventing encounter or causing such persons to flee upon seeing them*—and tame all venomous beasts.

Moreover, those who practice **Daoist refinement** shall transmute their **Yin-qi** into poisonous dragons, fierce beasts, and great serpents, numbering in the hundreds of billions, all protecting this **true scripture** and ensuring their own subjugation, forever shielding it.»

It can crush all heretical Dao/Way, shatter all worldly heresies, and destroy one’s own deluded, false attachments.

All the celestial beings—all the heavens and their realms—
shall naturally hold this scripture in reverence, spontaneously honoring it.

As for its remaining virtues, they are beyond exhaustive description—refer to what has been said before.

This scripture’s virtues dissolve what is difficult to dispel and remove what is difficult to eradicate. It transforms all things without exception, benefiting all without fail. It is the **great expedient means**, the **supreme Dharma category**.

Though it is the subtle speech of the most exalted sages, it is the very essence of what can be accomplished.

Strive earnestly, and the merit shall naturally manifest.

**Chapter Thirty-Six: The Manifestation of Verification (Continuation)**

At that time, the gathered Daoist assembly, the Golden Immortal Bodhisattvas, and the retinues of the True Saints, upon hearing this, rejoiced and leapt in exultation. They bowed in reverence and composed a hymn:

*"Great is the Ultimate Dao/Way,
Without origin, the Most High True One.
It ascends to elevate all heavens,
Descends to rescue the lost souls.
It has no teacher or ancestor—
The Dao/Way itself is the body.
In the Dan Platform and Purple Mansion,
At the Golden Gate and Jade Capital,
This wondrous law is hidden,
Bestowing universal blessings upon all living beings.
It eradicates my ten thousand sins,
And extends my boundless years.
Ten thousand spirits pay homage,
While the demon kings guard and welcome.
Its virtues flourish boundlessly,
Recorded in the Yellow Register of names,
Vast across countless eons,
Ensuring my eternal existence."*

Then the assembled Daoist congregation, having finished their hymn, bowed and took refuge. They paid respects and withdrew.

At that time, the Daoist assembly—
*The Daoist assembly, where the Dao/Way is expounded*—
the Golden Immortal Bodhisattvas and the retinues of the True Saints, upon hearing this, having finished the scripture, rejoiced and leapt in exultation, their joy overflowing like drums and dances. They bowed in reverence and composed a hymn:

*"Great is the Ultimate Dao/Way,
Immeasurable, unattainable.
Without origin, without beginning,
The Most High True One.
It ascends to elevate all heavens,
Transforming all above.
It descends to rescue the lost souls,
Penetrating the depths of the underworld,
Freeing all stagnant spirits to ascend.
It has no teacher, no ancestor.
The Dao/Way itself is the body—
Praising this scripture, the Dao/Way is the essence.
In the Dan Platform and Purple Mansion,
The supreme mysterious realm.
At the Golden Gate and Jade Capital—
As previously explained—
This wondrous law is hidden—
Hidden, as in treasured away—
Bestowing universal blessings upon all living beings,
Or with blessings as universal as the *Pu* degree.
It eradicates my ten thousand sins,
The scripture can annihilate all offenses.
It extends my boundless years,
The scripture can prolong life.
Ten thousand spirits pay homage,
Revering this scripture.
The demon kings guard and welcome those who hold the scripture.
Its virtues flourish boundlessly,
Its virtues are vast and everlasting.
Recorded in the Yellow Register—
The *Xuandu* Immortal Ledger, inscribed on golden tablets and yellow talismans—
Vast across countless eons,
Boundless and remote, spanning countless eons.
Ensuring my eternal existence,
Ensuring those who hold the Dao/Way and this scripture shall endure forever."*

Then the gathered True Saints of the Daoist assembly, having finished their hymn, bowed and took refuge in the *Supreme Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct and Assembly Scripture*. They paid respects to the Most High Sage and withdrew.

**The Conclusion of the Lower Scroll of the Supreme Jade Emperor’s Original Conduct and Assembly Scripture.**
